The Two Pillars of Tayammum
Stating the two pillars of tayammum

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two pillars of tayammum and derive their Qur'anic proof from Surah al-Ma'idah 5:6.

Core Idea
Tayammum has only two pillars: wiping the face and hands, as commanded in Quran 5:6.

This lesson focuses on the two essential acts (rukn) that constitute a valid tayammum. Unlike wudu which has four pillars, tayammum is simpler. You will learn exactly what must be wiped and why these two are the only compulsory elements, supported by direct Qur'anic evidence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Tayammum is a purification method using earth when water is unavailable. Its pillars are fard (obligatory). Determine what constitutes the act and its legal classification.
2
State the two pillars
From the text, state the two obligatory acts: wiping the entire face and wiping both hands including the elbows.
The hands include the elbows, as per Hanafi interpretation.
3
Locate the Qur'anic proof
Find the verse (Surah al-Ma'idah 5:6) and quote the relevant part: 'famsahu bi wujuhikum wa aydikum minhu'.
4
Explain the wajh al-dalalah
The imperative 'famsahu' (so wipe) indicates obligation (wujub) in Hanafi usul. The verse specifically addresses tayammum, establishing these two actions as compulsory.
5
Contrast with wudu
Note that tayammum has only two pillars, whereas wudu has four. This highlights the concession (rukhsah) of tayammum.

Source Text

ورکناه مسح اليدين والوجه . ترجمه : (۲۰۵) اور تیم کارکن دونوں ہاتھوں کا پونچھنا ہے، اور چہرے کا پونچھنا ہے۔ تشريح : : تیم کے دوفرائض ہیں [1] ایک فرض ہے تیم کی نیت سے پورے چہرے کو پونچھے، [۲] اور دوسرا فرض ہے دونوں ہاتھوں کو کہنیوں سمیت پونچھے۔ اس میں وضو کی طرح چار فرض نہیں ہیں۔ وجه : فامسحوا بوجوهكم وايديكم منه ما يريد الله ليجعل عليكم من حرج و لكن يريد ليطهر كم و ليتم نـعـمـتـه عليـكم لعلكم تشكرون ۔ ( آیت ۶ سورۃ المائدة (۵) اس آیت میں ہے کہ تیم کے لئے چہرے کو پونچھو اور ہاتھ کو پوچھو۔
And its two pillars: wiping the hands and the face. Translation of (205): The two obligatory acts of tayammum are wiping both hands and wiping the face. Explanation: Tayammum has two obligations: [1] The first obligation is to wipe the entire face with the intention of tayammum, [2] and the second obligation is to wipe both hands including the elbows. In this, there are not four obligations like in wudu. Proof: 'So wipe your faces and your hands with it. Allah does not wish to place any hardship upon you, but He wishes to purify you and complete His favor upon you that you may be grateful.' (Qur'an 5:6). In this verse, it is stated that for tayammum, wipe the face and wipe the hands.
Source pages p. 158

Commentary
This passage presents the two pillars (rukn) of tayammum. Unlike wudu which has four pillars (washing face, hands, wiping head, washing feet), tayammum has only two: wiping the entire face and wiping both hands including the elbows. The author emphasizes that there are no other pillars. The proof is from the Qur'anic verse (5:6) where Allah commands to wipe faces and hands. The Hanafi understanding is that the verse refers to tayammum specifically (as the context of the verse includes the mention of using earth due to illness or lack of water). The commentary adds that the intention (niyyah) is necessary for the act to be valid, as mentioned in the explanation.

Key Terms
ركن (rukn): Pillar or integral part of tayammum; its omission invalidates the act.
وجه (wajh): Face, which must be wiped entirely in tayammum.
يدان (yadan): Both hands including the elbows, which must be wiped in tayammum.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
How many pillars (rukn) does tayammum have?
A) Two
B) Three
C) Four
D) One

Key Takeaway
Tayammum has only two pillars: wiping the entire face and wiping both hands including the elbows, as proven by the Qur'anic command in Surah al-Ma'idah 5:6.

The Seven Sunan of Tayammum and Their Proofs
Listing sunan and providing proofs from Quran and Hadith

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the seven sunan of tayammum and explain the proofs from Quran and Sunnah that establish the sunnah of order (tartib) and continuity (muwalat).

Core Idea
Tayammum's sunan mirror wudu's sunan; the Quranic 'fa' proves order and immediacy.

This passage enumerates the seven recommended acts (sunan) of tayammum. While tayammum is a substitute for wudu, its sunan are derived from both the Quranic verse and the Prophet's practice. Understanding these sunan helps you perform tayammum with completeness while recognizing they are not obligatory.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its category
Recognize that tayammum is the subject and that these acts are sunan (recommended), not obligatory.
2
List the seven sunan from the text
Extract the seven sunan: basmalah, tartib, muwalat, starting with fingertips, bringing back from elbows, shaking hands, spreading fingers.
The text provides full list; confirm each from the Arabic.
3
Trace the analogy to wudu
Note the author's reasoning: tayammum is a deputy of wudu, so sunan of wudu become sunan here.
Basmalah, tartib, and muwalat are sunan in wudu; thus they are sunan in tayammum.
4
Examine the Quranic proof
Analyze the verse 'famsahu bi wujuhikum wa aydikum' – the letter 'fa' indicates order (tartib) and immediacy (muwalat).
This is the primary textual proof for these two sunan.
5
Examine the hadith proof
Review the hadith of 'Ammar ibn Yasir, which shows the Prophet and Companions performing two strikes: first face, then hands, with immediacy.
The hadith reinforces the order and continuity established by the verse.

Source Text

Chapter on the sunan of tayammum. The sunan of tayammum are seven: (206) saying the basmalah at the beginning, tartib (order), muwalat (continuity), (20?) and starting with the fingertips after placing the hands on the earth. In tayammum, there are seven sunan: At a glance: 1. Saying Bismillah at the beginning. 2. Tartib. 3. Muwalat. 4. Starting from the fingertips after placing the hands on the earth. ... and bringing back from the elbows. 5. Shaking the hands (dusting off). 6. Keeping the fingers spread. ☆☆☆ Translation of (206): The sunan of tayammum are seven: (1) Saying Bismillah at the beginning. (2) Performing tayammum in order. (3) Performing it consecutively. Explanation: Tayammum is a deputy of wudu, and in wudu, saying Bismillah at the beginning, performing the actions in the order they appear in the verse, and performing them consecutively are sunan. Therefore, these will also be sunan in tayammum. Proof: (1) In the verse, it is stated to first wipe the face and then wipe the hands; thus the order is sunnah. The verse is: 'So wipe your faces and your hands with it' (Qur'an 5:6). (2) In the hadith, this same order is reported: From 'Ammar ibn Yasir, he narrated that they wiped (tamassahu) while with the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) with earth (sa'eed) for the Fajr prayer, so they struck their palms on the earth, then wiped their faces with one wipe, then returned and struck their palms on the earth another time, and wiped their hands all the way to the shoulders and armpits from the inner sides of their hands. (Sunan Abi Dawud, Chapter on tayammum, p. 57, no. 318). In this hadith, with the first strike they wiped the face, and then with the second strike they wiped the hands. And through the letter 'fa', it also indicates immediacy, thus muwalat is also established. Translation of (207): [4] Starting with the fingertips after placing the hands on the earth. [5] And bringing back from the elbows.
Source pages p. 159

Commentary
This passage enumerates the seven sunan (recommended acts) of tayammum. The author first lists them in Arabic: saying Bismillah, observing order (tartib), continuity (muwalat), and the position of the hands (starting from fingertips, bringing back from elbows, shaking the hands, spreading fingers). The Urdu commentary adds that tayammum is the deputy of wudu, so its sunan follow wudu. The proof for order and continuity is from the Qur'anic verse (5:6) where the word 'fa' (then) implies order and immediacy. Additionally, the hadith of 'Ammar ibn Yasir shows that the Prophet (peace be upon him) and his companions performed tayammum in two strikes: first face, then hands. The second part (207) details the third and fourth sunan regarding the manner of wiping. Note that these sunan are recommended, not obligatory; omission does not invalidate tayammum but reduces its perfection.

Key Terms
سنة (sunnah): Recommended act in tayammum; omission does not invalidate but loses reward.
ترتيب (tartib): Performing tayammum in the order of face then hands.
موالاة (muwalat): Performing the actions consecutively without delay.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the primary proof for the sunnah of order (tartib) in tayammum according to this passage?
A) The Quranic verse using 'fa' indicating sequence.
B) A hadith from 'Aishah about wiping the head.
C) Consensus of all madhahib.
D) Analogical reasoning from eating.

Key Takeaway
The sunan of tayammum are recommended acts; omitting them does not invalidate tayammum but reduces its perfection.

Sunnahs of Tayammum and Ruling on Delaying It
Explains seven sunnahs of tayammum and delay rulings

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the seven sunnahs of tayammum, explain their proofs, and apply the ruling on when it is mustahab or wajib to delay tayammum.

Core Idea
Tayammum has seven sunnahs; delay is mustahab when hopeful but wajib when water is certain.

In this passage, we learn about the recommended acts (sunnahs) that perfect tayammum, and the important distinction between delaying it due to hope or certainty of finding water. Understanding these sunnahs helps one perform a complete substitute purification, and knowing the delay ruling prevents invalid prayer.

Guided Path
1
Enumerate the seven sunnahs
Read the passage and list the seven sunnahs of tayammum: saying Bismillah, order (tartib), continuity (muwalat), starting from the fingers, bringing back from the elbows, shaking the hands, and spreading the fingers.
These are found in paragraphs (206)-(208) of the Arabic.
2
Examine the proofs for each sunnah
For each sunnah, identify the evidence (dalil) from Quran or hadith as cited in the commentary. For example, tartib and muwalat are derived from the verse 'famsahu biwujuhikum waaydikum' and the hadith of Ammar ibn Yasir.
The hadith of Ammar shows the order and continuity via the letter 'fa'.
3
Distinguish the delay rulings
Note the two scenarios for delaying tayammum: (1) hope of finding water → mustahab to delay until near end of time; (2) certainty of water (by promise or proximity) → wajib to delay and wait for water, even if prayer becomes qada.
The proof for the second scenario includes the saying of Ali.
4
Apply to a practical scenario
Given a traveler hoping to find water soon, decide whether to delay tayammum or perform it immediately. Use the passage's criteria: if only hope, delay is mustahab; if certainty, delay becomes wajib.
The key distinction is certainty vs. mere hope.

لغت : نفض : جھاڑا۔ تفریح الاصابع : انگلیوں کو کشادہ رکھنا۔
ترجمه : (۲۰۹) اور جو پانی ملنے کی امید رکھتا ہو اس کے لئے وقت نکلنے سے پہلے تک تیم کی تاخیر مستحب ہے۔ اور جس کو پانی دینے کا وعدہ کیا گیا ہو اس کو تیم میں تاخیر کرنا واجب ہے، اگر چہ نماز قضا ہو جانے کا اندیشہ ہو۔
تشریح : کسی کو پانی ملنے کی امید ہو تو اس کے لئے تیم کر کے نماز پڑھنے کی تاخیر کرنا مستحب ہے، اور جب وقت نکلنے لگے تو تیم کر کے نماز پڑھ لے، اور نماز قضاء نہ کرے۔ لیکن اگر پانی دینے کا وعدہ کیا ہے، اور اس کے پاس پانی بھی موجود ہے، یا ایک میل کے اندر پانی ملنا یقینی ہے تو چاہے نماز قضا ہو جائے پانی حاصل کر کے وضو کرے۔ وجه : (۱) دونوں مسئلوں میں فرق یہ ہے کہ پہلے میں صرف امید ہے، ہو سکتا ہے کہ پانی نہ ملے، اس لئے صرف و ہم پر نماز قضا نہ کرے، اور دوسرے میں پانی ملنا یقینی ہے اس لئے آیت کے اعتبار سے وہ یقینی طور پر پانی پانے والا ہے اس لئے اس کے لئے تیم کی گنجائش نہیں ہوگی ، وہ نماز کی قضا کرے اور اصل طہارت پر عمل کرے۔ (۲) حضرت علی کا قول ہے۔ عــن عـلـى قـال : اذا
الرجل في السفر تلوم ما بينه و بين آخر الوقت فان لم يجد الماء تيمم و صلی. (دار قطنی ، باب فی بیان
Section on the Sunnahs of Tayammum. The sunnahs of tayammum are seven: (206) Saying Bismillah at the beginning, order, and continuity; (20) and bringing the hands forward after placing them in the dust. In tayammum there are seven sunnahs: The sunnahs of tayammum at a glance: 1. Saying Bismillah at the beginning. 2. Order. 3. Continuity. 4. Starting from the fingers after placing both hands on the ground. 5. ... and bringing back from the elbows. 6. Shaking both hands (dusting). 7. Keeping the fingers spread. ☆☆☆ Translation: (206) The sunnahs of tayammum are seven: (1) Saying Bismillah at the beginning. (2) Performing tayammum in order. (3) Performing it continuously. Explanation: Tayammum is the deputy of wudu, and in wudu saying Bismillah at the beginning, and performing actions in the order they appear in the verse, and performing them continuously are sunnah; therefore these are also sunnah in tayammum. Proof: (1) The verse says: 'So wipe your faces and your hands with it' (Surah al-Ma'idah, 5:6) - the order is sunnah. (2) The same order appears in hadith: From Ammar ibn Yasir... (Abu Dawud, Bab al-Sayyim, p.57 no.318). This hadith shows that the first strike was for the face and the second for the hands, and the letter 'fa' indicates immediacy, thus continuity is proven. Translation: (207) [4] Starting with the fingers after placing both hands on the ground. [5] And bringing back from the elbows. Section on the Sunnahs of Tayammum ... and bringing them back (208), and shaking them and spreading the fingers (209). And it is recommended to delay tayammum for one who hopes for water before. Explanation: After striking the hands on the ground a second time, one should start wiping from the fingers and draw up to above the elbows, then bring the palm back to the fingertips, so that the entire hand is wiped. This is sunnah. The phrase 'bringing the hands forward after placing them in the dust and bringing them back' has another meaning: at the time of the strike, move the hand slightly forward and slightly back so that the dust fully adheres to the hand. Proof: From Ammar ibn Yasir... (Abu Dawud, Bab al-Sayyim, p.57 no.318). This hadith shows that they started from the fingertips and drew the palm to the shoulders. Translation: (208) [6] Shaking both hands (dusting). [7] Keeping the fingers spread. Explanation: If too much dust sticks to the palm, it is sunnah to shake it off so that the face and hands do not become overly dusty and the body does not get dirty. While wiping, keep the fingers spread so that every part is reached. This is also sunnah. Proof: From Shaqiq... he said: 'It would have sufficed you to do this' and he struck his hand on the ground and shook it... (Abu Dawud, Bab al-Sayyim, p.58 no.321). This hadith mentions shaking the hand. Vocabulary: Nafd: shake. Tafrij al-asabi': spreading the fingers. Translation: (209) For one who hopes to find water, it is recommended to delay tayammum until just before the time expires. And for one who has been promised water, it is obligatory to delay tayammum even if there is fear of missing the prayer. Explanation: If someone hopes to find water, it is recommended to delay performing tayammum and praying. When the time is about to expire, he should perform tayammum and pray, and not make up the prayer later. But if he has been promised water, and he has water available, or water is certain within one mile, then even if the prayer becomes qada, he should obtain water and perform wudu. Proof: (1) The difference between the two cases is that in the first there is only hope; water may not be found, so he should not let the prayer become qada based on mere doubt. In the second, finding water is certain, so according to the verse he is definitely one who finds water; therefore tayammum is not permissible for him. He should make up the prayer and act with original purification. (2) The saying of Ali: from Ali, he said: 'When a man is on a journey, he should wait until near the end of the time; if he does not find water, he performs tayammum and prays.' (Dar Qutni, Bab fi Bayan...)
Source pages p. 159

Commentary
This passage is an expansion on the sunnahs of tayammum and the ruling on when to delay it. The author lists seven sunnahs: (1) saying Bismillah, (2) performing in a specific order, (3) performing continuously without delay, (4) starting the wipe from the fingertips after placing hands on the dust, (5) bringing the hands back from the elbows, (6) shaking off excess dust from the hands, and (7) spreading the fingers apart during the wipe. Each sunnah is supported by evidence from the Quran or hadith. For example, the order and continuity are derived from the verse 'Famshu biwujuhikum waaydikum minhu' and the practice of Ammar ibn Yasir. The wiping from fingertips to elbows is based on another narration of Ammar. Shaking the dust is proven from the hadith of Shaqiq. The passage then discusses the ruling on delaying tayammum: if one hopes to find water, it is recommended (mustahab) to delay until near the end of the prayer time, but if one is certain to find water (e.g., by promise or proximity), it becomes obligatory (wajib) to wait and perform wudu, even if it means missing the prayer time. The distinction is based on certainty versus mere hope, and the authority of Ali ibn Abi Talib is cited. The passage focuses on sunnah-level actions (not wajib) for tayammum, except in the case of certainty of water where delay becomes wajib.

Key Terms
تیمم (tayammum): Dry ablution using clean earth as a substitute for wudu or ghusl when water is unavailable or harmful.
سنت (sunnah): Recommended actions that the Prophet regularly performed but did not obligate; omission is not sinful but deprives one of reward.
ترتیب (tartib): Performing the actions of tayammum in a specific order: first the face, then the hands.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling on delaying tayammum for one who has been promised water?
A) Mustahab (recommended)
B) Wajib (obligatory)
C) Haram (forbidden)
D) Makruh (disliked)

Key Takeaway
The seven sunnahs perfect tayammum; delay is mustahab when hopeful for water but becomes wajib when water is certain.

Sunnah Actions of Tayammum: Forward/Backward Movement, Shaking, and Spreading Fingers
Explains sunnah actions with hadith evidence

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three sunnah actions of tayammum (iqbal wa idbar, nafd, tafrij al-asabi') and identify their proofs from the Sunnah.

Core Idea
The sunnah actions of tayammum perfect the purification; omitting them does not invalidate it.

In this passage, the author details the recommended (sunnah) actions of tayammum: moving the hands forward and backward, shaking off excess dust, and spreading the fingers. These actions are derived from the practice of the Prophet (peace be upon him) as recorded in authentic hadith. Understanding these sunan helps you perform tayammum in the most complete manner.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three sunnah actions
From the Arabic text, extract the three sunnah actions: iqbal al-yadayn wa idbarihima (forward and backward movement), nafd (shaking), and tafrij al-asabi' (spreading fingers). Note their descriptions in the commentary.
2
Examine the hadith proofs
Two hadith are cited: one from Ammar ibn Yasir showing wiping up to the shoulders (evidence for hand movement), and one from Shaqiq showing shaking the hand (evidence for nafd). Understand how each supports the sunnah ruling.
Dalil block in the toolbox provides details.
3
Distinguish sunnah from fard/wajib
The text explicitly states these are sunnah, not fard or wajib. Omitting them does not invalidate tayammum, but leaving them reduces perfection. This distinction is critical in Hanafi fiqh.
Hanafi position box confirms sunnah_muakkadah.

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement with proof (sunna with hadith evidence). It explains the sunnah actions of tayammum, specifically the iqbal wa idbar (forward and backward movement) and nafd (shaking) and tafrij al-asabi' (spreading fingers). The commentary clarifies that after striking the ground a second time, one should wipe from the fingertips up to the elbows and back, and that moving the hands forward and backward on the ground ensures thorough dust coverage. Shaking off excess dust and spreading fingers are also sunnah to ensure even wiping and cleanliness. The hadith from Ammar ibn Yasir shows wiping up to the shoulders, and from Shaqiq shows shaking the hand. These are all recommended actions (sunnah); omitting them does not invalidate tayammum but leaves perfection.

Key Terms
اقبال اليدين (iqbal al-yadayn): Moving the hands forward after placing them in dust
ادبارهما (idbarihima): Moving the hands backward (after forward movement)
نفض (nafd): Shaking the hands to remove excess dust
تفريج الاصابع (tafrij al-asabi'): Spreading the fingers apart during wiping

Delaying Tayammum: Hope vs Promise of Water
Ruling on delaying tayammum with proof from hadith

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on delaying tayammum for a traveler who hopes for water versus one who is promised water, and apply the correct ruling to given scenarios.

Core Idea
Hope makes delay mustahabb; promise/certainty makes delay wajib, even if prayer becomes qada.

This lesson tackles a common question: When may a traveler delay tayammum while waiting for water? The answer depends on the degree of certainty. A mere hope allows delay as a recommended act, but a promise or certainty of obtaining water makes it obligatory to wait, even at the risk of missing the prayer time. The passage provides proofs from the sunnah and the saying of Ali (ra).

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios
Read the passage and identify the two distinct cases: (1) one who merely hopes to find water, and (2) one who has been promised water or is certain of it within a mile, or promised clothing/water vessels.
The ruling for promise of clothing/means differs slightly: delay is wajib only until fear of qada.
2
Ruling for hope
For the hope scenario, the text states that delaying tayammum is mustahabb (recommended) until near the end of the prayer time. If water is found afterward, the prayer is valid and need not be repeated.
The hadith of Abu Sa'id al-Khudri supports this: the Prophet praised the one who did not repeat.
3
Ruling for promise/certainty
For the promise/certainty scenario, delaying tayammum becomes wajib (obligatory), even if the prayer becomes qada. The person is legally considered able to use water, so tayammum is not allowed.
The difference is based on the Quranic condition 'not finding water' (verses 4:43, 5:6).
4
Understand the evidence
The author cites the saying of Ali (talawwum) and the hadith of Abu Sa'id al-Khudri as proofs. Analyze the hadith: the Prophet's response indicates the sunnah is to not repeat, which implies delay is commendable.
For promise, the evidence is analogical: since water is certain, tayammum is invalid.
5
Distinguish the boundary
Note that for promise of clothing or water vessel (bucket/rope), the obligation to delay is only until fear of qada, unlike water promise which is even after qada. This is because these are means, not the water itself.
This nuance prevents automatic generalization.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ترجمه : (۲۰۹) اور جو پانی ملنے کی امید رکھتا ہو اس کے لئے وقت نکلنے سے پہلے تک تیم کی تاخیر مستحب ہے۔ اور جس کو پانی دینے کا وعدہ کیا گیا ہو اس کو تیم میں تاخیر کرنا واجب ہے، اگر چہ نماز قضا ہو جانے کا اندیشہ ہو۔
تشریح : کسی کو پانی ملنے کی امید ہو تو اس کے لئے تیم کر کے نماز پڑھنے کی تاخیر کرنا مستحب ہے، اور جب وقت نکلنے لگے تو تیم کر کے نماز پڑھ لے، اور نماز قضاء نہ کرے۔ لیکن اگر پانی دینے کا وعدہ کیا ہے، اور اس کے پاس پانی بھی موجود ہے، یا ایک میل کے اندر پانی ملنا یقینی ہے تو چاہے نماز قضا ہو جائے پانی حاصل کر کے وضو کرے۔ وجه : (۱) دونوں مسئلوں میں فرق یہ ہے کہ پہلے میں صرف امید ہے، ہو سکتا ہے کہ پانی نہ ملے، اس لئے صرف و ہم پر نماز قضا نہ کرے، اور دوسرے میں پانی ملنا یقینی ہے اس لئے آیت کے اعتبار سے وہ یقینی طور پر پانی پانے والا ہے اس لئے اس کے لئے تیم کی گنجائش نہیں ہوگی ، وہ نماز کی قضا کرے اور اصل طہارت پر عمل کرے۔ (۲) حضرت علی کا قول ہے۔ عـن عـلـى قـال : اذا الرجل في السفر تلوم ما بينه و بين آخر الوقت فان لم يجد الماء تيمم و صلی. (دار قطنی ، باب فی بیان خروج الوقت ويجب التاخير بالوعد بالماء ولو خاف القضاء (۲۱۰) ويجب التاخير بالوعد بالثوب او السقاء ما لم يخف القضاء . ٢١١ الف ويجب طلب الماء الى مقدار اربع مائة خطوة ان ظنّ الموضع الذي يجوز التيم فيه، ج اول ص ۱۹۵ نمبر ۰ اسے سن لیتی ، باب من تلوم ما بینه و بین آخر الوقت رجاء وجود الماء ، ج اول ص ۱۳۳۵ نمبر (۱۱۰) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ پانی کی امید کرنے والوں کے لئے مؤخر کرنا مستحب ہے۔ (۳) لیکن اگر اول وقت میں نماز پڑھ لی پھر پانی پایا تو نماز نہیں لوٹائے گا۔ ابوداود کی لمبی حدیث کا ٹکڑا یہ ہے۔ عن ابــى سـعـيـد الـخـدرى قـال خـرج رجلان في سفر فحضرت الصلاة وليس معهما ماء فتيمما صعيدا طيبا فصليا ثم وجدا الماء في الوقت فأعاد أحدهما الصلاة و الوضوء و لم يعد الآخر ، ثم أتيا رسول الله الله فذكر اذالك له فقال للذي لم يعد ((أصبت السنة و أجزأتك صلاتك ، )) وقال للذى توضأ و أعاد لك الاجر مرتين )) (ابوداودشریف ، باب استیم یسجد الماء بعد ما یصلی فی الوقت ،ص ۵۵ نمبر ۳۳۸) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ تیم کر کے نماز پڑھی اور وقت کے اندرہی پانی پالیا تو دوبارہ نماز لوٹانے کی ضرورت نہیں ہے۔ ترجمه : (۲۱۰) اور جس کو کپڑے یا پانی کے اسباب ( مثل ڈول رسی کے ) دینے کا وعدہ کیا گیا ہو اس کو قضا نہ ہونے تک تاخیر کرنا واجب ہے۔ تشریح ننگے کے پاس کپڑا نہیں ہے کسی نے کپڑا دینے کا وعدہ کیا یا پانی لانے کے اسباب مثلا ڈول رہی دینے کا وعدہ کیا تو نماز قضا نہ ہونے تک تاخیر کرنا واجب ہے، پس جب آخیر وقت آجائے تو تیم کر کے نماز پڑھے، اور نگا آدمی اشارے سے نماز پڑھ لے۔ وجه : پانی دینے کے وعدے اور کپڑا دینے کے وعدے، یا ڈول رہی دینے کے وعدے میں فرق یہ ہے کہ پانی اصل ہے، اور ڈول رسی پانی کے حاصل کرنے کے اسباب ہیں اس لئے اسباب کے وعدے میں نماز قضا ہونے سے پہلے پہلے تک تاخیر کرنا واجب ہے، اور اصل پانی کے وعدے میں نماز قضا ہو جائے تب بھی اصل پر عمل کرنا ضروری ہے۔ کیونکہ وہ پانی پانے والا ہے۔
لغت : بالثوب: ننگے کے لئے کپڑے کا وعدہ مراد ہے۔ السقاء : سیراب کرنے کا آلہ مراد ہے ڈول رسی۔
Translation: (209) And for one who hopes to find water, it is mustahabb to delay tayammum until the time expires. And for one who has been promised water, it is wajib to delay tayammum, even if there is fear that the prayer will become qada. Explanation: For one who hopes for water, it is mustahabb to delay performing tayammum and prayer, and when the time is about to expire, he should perform tayammum and pray, and the prayer will not be qada. But if he has been promised water and water is present with him, or water is certain within a mile, then even if the prayer becomes qada, he should obtain water and perform wudu. Evidence: (1) The difference between the two issues is that in the first there is only hope; it is possible water will not be found, so he should not make his prayer qada based on mere hope. In the second, water is certain, so according to the verse, he is definitely one who finds water; therefore, tayammum is not permissible for him; he should make his prayer qada and act on original purity. (2) The saying of Ali: 'When a man is on a journey, he should wait between himself and the end of the time; if he does not find water, he performs tayammum and prays.' (Daraqutni, chapter on the exit of time, and it is obligatory to delay if promised water even if fear of qada (210) and it is obligatory to delay if promised clothing or a water vessel as long as there is no fear of qada. (211) It is obligatory to seek water up to four hundred steps if he thinks the place where tayammum is permissible is nearby... This hadith indicates that it is mustahabb for those hoping for water to delay. (3) But if he prayed at the beginning of the time and then found water, he does not repeat the prayer. A portion of the long hadith of Abu Dawud: From Abu Sa'id al-Khudri: Two men went on a journey, prayer time came, they had no water, so they performed tayammum and prayed. Then they found water within the time. One repeated his prayer and wudu, the other did not. They came to the Prophet and mentioned this. He said to the one who did not repeat: 'You followed the Sunnah and your prayer suffices.' And to the one who performed wudu and repeated: 'For you is double reward.' (Abu Dawud, Bab al-Istimta' bi al-Ma', p. 55, no. 338). This hadith indicates that if tayammum was performed and then water was found within the time, there is no need to repeat. Translation: (210) And for one who has been promised clothing or means of water (like a bucket and rope), it is obligatory to delay until qada does not occur. Explanation: If a naked person has no clothing and someone promises clothing, or promises means of bringing water like a bucket and rope, then delaying is wajib until the prayer is not missed. So when the end of time comes, he performs tayammum and prays, and the naked person prays with gestures. Evidence: The difference between the promise of water and the promise of clothing or means is that water is the original, and bucket and rope are means to obtain water. Therefore, in the promise of means, delaying is obligatory only until fear of qada, while in the promise of water, it is obligatory to act on the original even if the prayer becomes qada, because he is one who will definitely get water. Vocabulary: 'al-thawb': promise of clothing for a naked person. 'al-saqa': means of watering, bucket and rope.
Source pages p. 160

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof, covering the recommendation and obligation of delaying tayammum based on hope or promise of water or clothing. It clarifies two scenarios: (1) If one hopes to find water (not certain), it is mustahabb to delay tayammum until near the end of the time; if water is found, the prayer is valid and need not be repeated. (2) If water is promised or certain (e.g., within a mile), then delaying tayammum is wajib (obligatory) even if prayer becomes qada, because the person is considered able to use water. The hadith of Ali and the hadith of Abu Sa'id al-Khudri support the recommendation of delay for hope and that prayer is not repeated. The obligation for promise of clothing or water vessel (like bucket and rope) is also wajib, but only until fear of qada, because these are means, not the water itself. The key distinction is certainty versus hope: hope allows tayammum; certainty requires pursuit of water.

Key Terms
تلوم (talawwum): To wait and delay until near the end of the prayer time
وعد (wa'd): A promise or commitment to provide water or clothing
قضاء (qada): Making up a missed prayer after its time

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling for a traveler who has been promised water and is certain it will arrive, even if it means missing the prayer time?
A) Mustahabb to delay tayammum
B) Wajib to delay tayammum even if prayer becomes qada
C) Permissible to choose between tayammum and waiting
D) Recommended to delay only until the end of the time

Key Takeaway
The ruling on delaying tayammum depends on the degree of certainty: hope makes it mustahabb, promise/certainty makes it wajib.

Taharah — Purification
intermediate
12 min
Sunnahs of Tayammum: Delaying Prayer, Seeking Water, and Its Limits
Section on sunnahs of tayammum with rulings and proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rulings on delaying prayer due to promise of water or covering, the obligation to seek water up to 400 steps or from companions, the requirement to buy water at fair price, and the permissibility of multiple prayers with one tayammum.

Core Idea
Delaying prayer for promised water is wajib even at risk of missing qada; seeking water up to 400 steps is also wajib; one tayammum suffices for all prayers.

This lesson gathers several rulings from the Hanafi school on the sunnahs of tayammum. It covers when one must delay prayer due to a promise of water or covering, the obligation to actively seek water up to a defined distance, and the flexibility of using one tayammum for multiple prayers. Each ruling is supported by hadith proof.

Guided Path
1
Identify the six rulings
The passage presents six distinct rulings: (210) delay for promise of water, (211a) delay for promise of garment/water-skin, (211) seek water up to 400 steps, (211b) request water from companion, (212) buy water at fair price, (213) one tayammum for multiple prayers.
2
Note conditions for each ruling
For delaying, the condition differs: for water, delay even if qada is missed; for garment, delay only if qada not missed. Seeking water requires safety and expectation of water nearby. Requesting from companion is wajib only if water is not withheld. Buying is wajib only at fair price and if extra funds available.
3
Define key terms
'Ghalwah' is defined as 400 steps or about 200 yards. 'Thaman mithl' means fair market price. 'Qada' is the make-up prayer.
4
Examine the hadith proofs
The Abu Dawood hadith of two travelers shows that finding water within prayer time after tayammum does not require repetition. The Bukhari hadith of Aisha's necklace shows the Prophet seeking water nearby, indicating the obligation to seek.
5
Apply to practical scenarios
For example, a traveller promised water by a fellow villager must delay his prayer even if it means he will have to make it up later. If water is found but not given except at an inflated price, he is not obliged to buy.

فصل في سنن التيمم
قربه مع الامن والا فلا . (۲۱۱ [ب]) ويـجـب طلبه ممن هو معه ان كان في محل لا تشح بـه النفوس (۲۱۲) وان لم يعطه الا بثمن مثله لزمه شراءه به ان كان معه فاضلا عن نفقته ۱۱۰۴) اس عمل صحابی میں ہے کہ ایک غلوۃ سے آگے پانی تلاش نہیں کرتے ۔ (۲) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ قرب و جوار میں پانی تلاش کیا۔ عن عائشة سقطت قلادة لى بالبيداء ..... ثم ان النبى الله الله استيقظ و حضرت الصبح فالتمس الماء فـلـم يـوجـد ۔ ( بخاری شریف، باب قولہ تعالی فل تجد واما قیمو اصعید اطیب ( آیت ۶ سورۃ المائدۃ ۵) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ پانی کی امید پر تھوڑی دور تک پانی تلاش کیا۔ لغت غلوة: آدمی جہاں کھڑا ہے وہاں سے جہاں تک تیر جا سکے اس مسافت کو بغلوۃ ، کہتے ہیں۔ درمختار میں غلوۃ کا دو ترجمہ کیا ہے [1] تین سو سے چار سو ہاتھ ، [۲] اور دوسرا ترجمہ کیا ہے تین سو سے چار سو قدم ۔ عبارت یہ ہے۔ ( قدر غلوۃ) ثلاث مأة ذراع من كل جانب .. اى الى اربع مأة ... قدر غلوة من كل جانب ، و هى ثلاث مأة خطوة الى اربع مأة ، وقيل قدر رمية سهم - (درمختار، باب مطلب فى تقدیر الغلوۃ ، ج اول ص ۴۶۳/۴۶۲) ۔ ایک ذراع آدھے گز کا ہوتا ہے اس اعتبار سے ایک غلوۃ ۲۰۰ گز ہوا ترجمه : (۲۱۱ (ب) اور اگر اپنے رفیق کے ساتھ ایسی جگہ پر پانی ہو جہاں انسان پانی کا بخل نہ کرتا ہو تو اس سے طلب کرنا واجب ہے تشریح : پانی ایسی چیز ہے جو مفت ملتی ہے اس لئے اگر ساتھی کے پاس موجود ہو تو گویا کہ وہ پانی پانے والا ہے اس لئے اس سے مانگنا واجب ہے ۔ ہاں اگر ایسی جگہ ہو کہ مانگنا مشکل ہو اور لوگ دینے میں بخل کرتے ہوں تو مانگنا واجب نہیں ہے۔ تیخ بخالت کرنا وجه : اس حدیث میں دوسروں سے حضور نے پانی مانگا ہے۔ قال دخلت على عائشة فقلت : الا تحدثيني عن مرض رسول الله علم ..... قال ضعو الى ماءً في المخضب قالت فقعد فاغتسل ثم ذهب لينوء فأغمى عليه ثم افاق . فقال الله الله : أصلى الناس ؟ قلنا : لا هم ينتظرونک یا رسول الله قال ضعو الى ماءً في المخضب فقعد فاغتسل. (بخاری شریف، باب انما جعل الامام لیونتم به ص۱۱۲، نمبر ۷ ۶۸ ر مسلم شریف، باب استخلاف الامام اذا عرض له عذر ص ۱۷۶ نمبر ۹۳۶/۴۱۸) اس حدیث میں آپ نے دوسرے سے پانی مانگا ہے۔ ترجمه (۲۱۲) اور اگر نہیں دیتا ہو مگر مناسب قیمت میں پس اگر اس کے پاس اپنے خرچ سے زیادہ ہو تو اس کو خرید نالازم ہے۔ تشریح : دو باتیں ہوں تو پانی خریدے ورنہ تیم کر کے نماز پڑھے [1] پانی مناسب قیمت میں دیتا ہو، اگر زیادہ قیمت مانگ رہا ہو تو خرید نا واجب نہیں [۲] اپنے ضروری خرچ سے زیادہ ہوتب خریدے اگر ضروری خرچ سے زیادہ نہ ہوتو نہ خریدے۔ ترجمه : (۲۱۳) اور ایک تیم سے جتنی فرض و نوافل نماز چاہے پڑھ سکتا ہے۔ اور وقت سے پہلے تیم کرنا بھی درست ہے۔
Chapter on the Sunnahs of Tayammum. The time exits and it is obligatory to delay [prayer] due to a promise of water even if he fears missing the [time of] qada (210). And it is obligatory to delay due to a promise of a garment or a water-skin as long as he does not fear missing the qada (211a). And it is obligatory to seek water up to the measure of four hundred steps if he thinks the place where tayammum is permissible [exists]... [Then Urdu commentary]
Source pages p. 161

Commentary
This passage is from the section on the sunnahs of tayammum. It presents several rulings: (210) It is obligatory to delay prayer if one has been promised water, even if that means missing the time for making up the prayer later. (211a) Similarly, it is obligatory to delay if promised a garment to cover oneself or a water-skin, as long as one does not fear missing the make-up prayer entirely. The Urdu commentary elaborates: the difference between a promise of water itself and a promise of means to obtain water (like a bucket) is that with water itself, one should delay even if it means missing the prayer time, whereas with means, one delays only until just before the time ends. (211) It is obligatory to seek water up to 400 steps if one is safe and thinks water is near. The commentary defines 'ghalwah' as about 200 yards based on a report from Ibn Umar and from Aisha (hadith of the necklace). (211b) It is obligatory to request water from a companion if they are in a place where people are not stingy with water. If the place is such that people are stingy, it is not obligatory. (212) If a person does not give water except at a fair price, then it is obligatory to buy it if one has extra money beyond his necessary expenses. (213) One can pray as many obligatory and supererogatory prayers as he wishes with a single tayammum, and it is permissible to perform tayammum before the time of prayer. The rulings are based on clear hadith proofs, such as the hadith of the two travelers narrated by Abu Dawood.

Key Terms
غلوة (ghalwah): The distance from which an arrow can be shot; approximately 300-400 cubits or 200 yards.
ثمن مثل (thaman mithl): Fair price or market value of the water.
قضاء (qada): The make-up prayer performed after its prescribed time due to a valid excuse.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if someone promises you water but you fear that if you delay prayer you will miss the make-up time, what is the ruling?
A) You must not delay and should perform tayammum immediately.
B) You must delay prayer even if it means missing the make-up time.
C) You may choose either option.
D) You must delay prayer only until the end of the current prayer time, then perform tayammum if water does not arrive.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school obligates delaying prayer for a promise of water even at risk of missing qada, and obligates seeking water up to 400 steps, while allowing one tayammum for multiple prayers.

Seeking Water from a Companion for Tayammum
Explains the obligation of requesting water from a companion for tayammum.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on seeking water from a companion for tayammum and apply its conditions.

Core Idea
Seeking water from a companion is wajib when available and not withheld by stinginess.

Tayammum is a concession for when water is unavailable. But what if a companion has water nearby? The Hanafi school clarifies that one must first seek water from the companion before resorting to dry ablution. This lesson unpacks the ruling, its conditions, and the evidence from the Prophet's practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is the specific act being ruled upon? It is seeking water from a companion. What is the hukm? Wajib (obligatory) under certain conditions.
The ruling is not unconditional; it depends on the companion's location and disposition.
2
Locate the dalil
Two proofs are cited: the practice of the Companions searching for water within a ghulwah, and the hadith where the Prophet (PBUH) asked others for water during his illness.
The hadith is from Bukhari and Muslim, showing the Prophet's action.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The Prophet's asking for water indicates that seeking from others is a recommended or required step before tayammum. In the context of a traveler with a companion, it becomes wajib because water is available through the companion.
The Hanafi usul principle: al-amr yufidu al-wujub (command indicates obligation) applies here via the Prophet's action.
4
Note the condition
The obligation is conditioned on the companion being in a place where people are not stingy with water (la tashah bihi al-nufus). If asking is difficult or the companion is stingy, the obligation drops.
This is a practical consideration for the traveler's circumstances.
5
Evaluate the exception
The text also mentions that if the companion is in a place where asking is difficult (manqah mushkil) and people are stingy, then seeking is not wajib. This shows the ruling is flexible.
The exception preserves ease in the religion.

Source Text

فصل في سنن التيمم
قربه مع الامن والا فلا . (۲۱۱ [ب]) ويـجـب طلبه ممن هو معه ان كان في محل لا تشح بـه النفوس
اس عمل صحابی میں ہے کہ ایک غلوۃ سے آگے پانی تلاش نہیں کرتے ۔ (۲) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ قرب و جوار میں پانی تلاش کیا۔ عن عائشة سقطت قلادة لى بالبيداء ..... ثم ان النبى الله الله استيقظ و حضرت الصبح فالتمس الماء فـلـم يـوجـد ۔ ( بخاری شریف، باب قولہ تعالی فل تجد واما قیمو اصعید اطیب ( آیت ۶ سورۃ المائدۃ ۵) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ پانی کی امید پر تھوڑی دور تک پانی تلاش کیا۔ لغت غلوة: آدمی جہاں کھڑا ہے وہاں سے جہاں تک تیر جا سکے اس مسافت کو بغلوۃ ، کہتے ہیں۔ درمختار میں غلوۃ کا دو ترجمہ کیا ہے [1] تین سو سے چار سو ہاتھ ، [۲] اور دوسرا ترجمہ کیا ہے تین سو سے چار سو قدم ۔ عبارت یہ ہے۔ ( قدر غلوۃ) ثلاث مأة ذراع من كل جانب .. اى الى اربع مأة ... قدر غلوة من كل جانب ، و هى ثلاث مأة خطوة الى اربع مأة ، وقيل قدر رمية سهم - (درمختار، باب مطلب فى تقدیر الغلوۃ ، ج اول ص ۴۶۳/۴۶۲) ۔ ایک ذراع آدھے گز کا ہوتا ہے اس اعتبار سے ایک غلوۃ ۲۰۰ گز ہوا
ترجمه : (۲۱۱ (ب) اور اگر اپنے رفیق کے ساتھ ایسی جگہ پر پانی ہو جہاں انسان پانی کا بخل نہ کرتا ہو تو اس سے طلب کرنا واجب ہے
تشریح : پانی ایسی چیز ہے جو مفت ملتی ہے اس لئے اگر ساتھی کے پاس موجود ہو تو گویا کہ وہ پانی پانے والا ہے اس لئے اس سے مانگنا واجب ہے ۔ ہاں اگر ایسی جگہ ہو کہ مانگنا مشکل ہو اور لوگ دینے میں بخل کرتے ہوں تو مانگنا واجب نہیں ہے۔ وجه : اس حدیث میں دوسروں سے حضور نے پانی مانگا ہے۔ قال دخلت على عائشة فقلت : الا تحدثيني عن مرض رسول الله صلى الله عليه ..... قال ضعو الى ماءً في المخضب قالت فقعد فاغتسل ثم ذهب لينوء فأغمى عليه ثم افاق . فقال : اصلى الناس ؟ قلنا : لا هم ينتظرونك يا رسول الله قال ضعو الى ماءً في المخضب فقعد فاغتسل. (بخاری شریف، باب انما جعل الامام لیونتم به ص۱۱۲، نمبر ۷ ۶۸ ر مسلم شریف، باب استخلاف الامام اذا عرض له عذر ص ۱۷۶ نمبر ۹۳۶/۴۱۸) اس حدیث میں آپ نے دوسرے سے پانی مانگا ہے۔
Chapter on the Sunnahs of Tayammum.
Seeking water when there is safety and otherwise... (211[b]) It is obligatory to seek it from the one who is with him if he is in a place where people are not stingy with it.
This is the action of a Companion: that they do not seek water beyond one ghulwah. (2) In this hadith, water was sought in the vicinity. From Aisha: 'My necklace fell at al-Bayda'... then the Prophet (peace be upon him) woke up and the time for Fajr came, so he sought water but did not find it.' (Bukhari, chapter on the verse 'then you do not find water'...). In this hadith, water was sought a short distance away in hope of finding it.
Linguistics of ghulwah: The distance from where a person stands to where an arrow can be thrown is called a ghulwah. In Durr al-Mukhtar, two translations are given: [1] three hundred to four hundred cubits, [2] three hundred to four hundred steps. The text: 'The measure of a ghulwah is three hundred cubits from each side... up to four hundred... the measure of a ghulwah from each side is three hundred steps to four hundred, and it is said the distance of an arrow shot.' (Durr al-Mukhtar, chapter on the estimation of ghulwah, vol.1 pp.463/462). One cubit is half a yard, so one ghulwah is 200 yards.
Translation: (211(b)) And if water is with his companion in a place where people are not stingy with water, then requesting it from him is obligatory.
Explanation: Water is something that is obtained for free, so if the companion has it, it is as if he is one who can obtain water, so asking him is obligatory. However, if it is a place where asking is difficult and people are stingy in giving, then asking is not obligatory. Proof: In this hadith, the Prophet asked others for water. He said: 'I entered upon Aisha and said: Will you not tell me about the illness of the Messenger of Allah... he said: Put water for me in the basin...' [hadith continues]. (Bukhari, chapter on the imam is only appointed to be followed, p.112, no. 768; Muslim, chapter on the appointment of a successor when an excuse arises, p.176, no. 936/418). In this hadith, he asked others for water.
Source pages p. 162

Commentary
This passage from Thamaratun Najah explains the ruling on seeking water from a companion when performing tayammum. The author states that it is obligatory (wajib) to ask one's companion for water if the companion is in a place where water is not withheld due to stinginess. The commentary provides two proofs: the practice of the Companions, who only searched for water within one ghulwah (about 200 yards), and the hadith of Aisha where the Prophet himself asked others for water during his illness. The key condition is that the request should not be difficult; if the people are stingy or the situation makes asking problematic, the obligation drops. This ruling is based on the principle that water is usually freely available, so a traveler should not resort to tayammum without first seeking water from his companions.

Key Terms
غلوة (ghulwah): A distance measure: approximately 200 yards (300-400 cubits).
تيمم (tayammum): Dry ablution with earth as a substitute for wudu or ghusl when water is unavailable.
واجب (wajib): Obligatory - a duty whose omission is sinful without excuse.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, in which situation is it obligatory to seek water from a companion for tayammum?
A) Always, regardless of circumstances
B) Only if the companion is a stranger
C) When the companion is in a place where water is not withheld due to stinginess
D) Only if the companion offers water first

Key Takeaway
Before tayammum, it is wajib to ask a companion for water if the companion is in a setting where water is freely given, but the obligation drops if asking is difficult.

Ruling on Buying Water for Tayammum
States the obligation to purchase water from a companion at a fair price if one has surplus funds.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions under which it is wajib to buy water for tayammum and identify when the obligation does not apply.

Core Idea
Water for purification must be purchased at a fair price if you have surplus funds; otherwise, tayammum suffices.

This lesson examines the Hanafi ruling on purchasing water for tayammum when a companion refuses to give it for free. The passage sets clear conditions for the obligation to buy, balancing the necessity of purification with financial hardship. You will learn the two key conditions that must be met for the purchase to be wajib, and when tayammum remains a valid alternative.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and Its Ruling
The act is purchasing water from a companion who demands payment. The ruling under certain conditions is wajib (obligatory).
If conditions are not met, the ruling is not wajib; tayammum is permissible.
2
Examine Condition 1: Fair Price
The seller must demand a fair market price (thaman mithl), not an excessive amount. If the price is exorbitant, there is no obligation to buy.
Fair price is determined by local market value.
3
Examine Condition 2: Surplus Funds
The buyer must have funds beyond essential living expenses (fadlan 'an al-nafaqah). If he has only enough for his necessities, he is not required to purchase.
Essential expenses include food, shelter, and basic needs.
4
Determine the Consequence When Conditions Are Met
If both conditions are satisfied, buying the water is wajib. He must perform wudu with that water.
Failing to buy when obliged invalidates the prayer if tayammum is used.
5
Note the Hanafi Emphasis
The ruling is wajib, not fard, because the obligation is conditional. Some other schools may not require purchase at all, considering tayammum sufficient even when water is available.
This highlights a practical difference (thamarah al-khilaf) between schools.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۲۱۲) وان لم يعطه الا بثمن مثله لزمه شراءه به ان كان معه فاضلا عن نفقته
ترجمه : (۲۱۲) اور اگر نہیں دیتا ہو مگر مناسب قیمت میں پس اگر اس کے پاس اپنے خرچ سے زیادہ ہو تو اس کو خرید نالازم ہے۔ تشریح : دو باتیں ہوں تو پانی خریدے ورنہ تیم کر کے نماز پڑھے [1] پانی مناسب قیمت میں دیتا ہو، اگر زیادہ قیمت مانگ رہا ہو تو خرید نا واجب نہیں [۲] اپنے ضروری خرچ سے زیادہ ہوتب خریدے اگر ضروری خرچ سے زیادہ نہ ہوتو نہ خریدے۔
(212) And if he does not give it except for a price equivalent to its value, he is obligated to buy it if he has with him surplus beyond his expenses. Translation: (212) And if he does not give it except at a reasonable price, then if he has surplus beyond his expenses, he is obligated to buy it. Explanation: There are two conditions: [1] The water is given at a fair price; if he demands an excessive price, it is not obligatory to buy. [2] He has surplus beyond his essential expenses; if he does not, he does not buy.
Source pages p. 162

Commentary
This passage provides the ruling when a companion refuses to give water for free but offers to sell it at a fair market price. In such a case, if the person in need of water has sufficient funds beyond his essential needs, it becomes obligatory (wajib) to purchase the water. The commentary clarifies two conditions: the price must be fair (thaman mithl), and the buyer must have surplus money after covering his own necessary expenses. If either condition is not met, tayammum is permissible without purchase. This ruling is based on the principle that water is essential for purification and should be acquired if reasonably possible.

Key Terms
ثمن مثل (thaman mithl): Fair market price for the water.
فضل عن النفقة (fadlan 'an al-nafaqah): Surplus beyond essential living expenses.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When is it obligatory to buy water for tayammum according to this passage?
A) Whenever the companion asks for payment
B) Only if the water is very cheap
C) If the companion sells at a fair price and the buyer has surplus beyond expenses
D) It is never obligatory to buy water

Key Takeaway
Buying water for tayammum is wajib only when the seller offers a fair price and the buyer has surplus funds beyond essential expenses; otherwise, tayammum is sufficient.

Ruling on Performing Multiple Prayers with One Tayammum
Declares the permissibility of multiple prayers with one tayammum and cites a proof from the tabi'in.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that a single tayammum is valid for multiple prayers and identify the proof from the tabi'in (al-Hasan and Ibn al-Musayyab).

Core Idea
One tayammum suffices for multiple prayers until hadath – it is the substitute for water.

This passage addresses a practical concern: can a person who has performed tayammum pray more than one obligatory or supererogatory prayer without renewing it? Building on the principle that tayammum is a substitute for wudu, the Hanafi school extends the same effect. We will examine the ruling and its proof from a saying of the tabi'in.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
The act is performing multiple prayers (both obligatory and voluntary) with a single tayammum. The ruling is that this is permissible (ja'iz) and that tayammum may even be performed before the prayer time enters.
The ruling is stated in the first line of the passage.
2
Locate the proof
The proof cited is a saying (qawl) of two tabi'in: al-Hasan al-Basri and Sa'id ibn al-Musayyab. They said: 'He performs tayammum and it suffices for all prayers as long as he does not have hadath; it is like water.'
This is a qawl sahabi (actually qawl tabi'i) from Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq and Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The key phrase in the proof is 'it is like water' (huwa bi-manzilat al-ma'). This indicates that tayammum has the same legal effect as water regarding validity for multiple prayers, provided no hadath occurs.
This analogy is the basis for the Hanafi position.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Other madhahib (e.g., Shafi'i) hold that a new tayammum is required for each obligatory prayer, viewing tayammum as a limited concession rather than a full substitute.
The Hanafi view is stronger in this proof due to the explicit statement of the tabi'in.
5
Evaluate the mufta bihi
The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) in the Hanafi school is that one tayammum suffices for all prayers until hadath. This is based on zahir al-riwayah and the cited athar.
This ruling is practical for travelers and those in need of tayammum.

Source Text

ترجمه : (۲۱۳) ویصلى بـالتـيـمـم الـواحـد مـا شـاء من الفرائض والنوافل ،وصح تقديمه على الوقت . تشریح : حنفیہ کے نزدیک تیم پانی کا خلیفہ ہے اس لئے جس طرح ایک وضو سے کئی وقتوں کی نماز پڑھ سکتا ہے، اسی طرح ایک تیم سے کئی وقتوں کی نماز پڑھ سکتا ہے۔ اور اس سے یہ بھی ثابت ہوا کہ وقت سے پہلے بھی تیم کر سکتا ہے۔ وجه : (ا) عن الحسن و ابن المسيب قالا يتيمم و تجزيه الصلوات كلها ما لم يحدث ، هو بمنزل لة الماء - (مصنف عبدالرزاق ، باب کم یصلی تیم واحد، ج اول ص ۱۶۹ نمبر ۸۳۵ مصنف ابن ابی شبیه ، باب فی التیم کم یصلی به من صلاة ، ج اول ،ص ۱۴۷ نمبر ۱۹۹۴) اس قول تابعی میں ہے کہ ایک تیم سے کئی نمازیں پڑھ سکتا ہے ۔ اور اس سے یہ بھی معلوم ہوا کہ وقت سے پہلے بھی تیم کر سکتا ہے۔
Translation: (213) And he may pray with one tayammum as many obligatory and voluntary prayers as he wishes, and it is valid to perform it before the time [of prayer]. Explanation: According to the Hanafis, tayammum is a substitute for water, so just as one can pray several prayers in different times with one wudu, similarly he can pray several prayers with one tayammum. And this also proves that tayammum can be performed before the time. Proof: (1) From al-Hasan and Ibn al-Musayyab: they said, 'He performs tayammum and it suffices for all prayers as long as he does not have hadath; it is like water.' (Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq, Bab Kam Yussalli bi Tayammum Wahid, vol.1 p.169 no.835; Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah, Bab fi al-Tayammum Kam Yussalli bihi min Salat, vol.1 p.147 no.1994). In this saying of a tabi'i, it is mentioned that one can pray many prayers with one tayammum. And from this it is also learned that tayammum can be performed before the time.
Source pages p. 162

Commentary
This passage establishes that a single tayammum is sufficient for multiple prayers, both obligatory and voluntary, and that it can be performed before the prayer time enters. The Hanafi reasoning is analogical: just as wudu remains valid for multiple prayers until it breaks, tayammum as its substitute carries the same effect. The proof is cited from the tabi'in, al-Hasan al-Basri and Sa'id ibn al-Musayyab, who explicitly stated that tayammum suffices for all prayers as long as no hadath occurs. This ruling also allows performing tayammum in advance of the prayer time, similar to wudu.

Key Terms
تيمم واحد (tayammum wahid): A single dry ablution performed once that suffices for multiple prayers until hadath occurs.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Only one obligatory prayer
B) As many prayers as one wishes until hadath occurs
C) Only voluntary prayers
D) Only one prayer per time

Key Takeaway
One tayammum suffices for multiple prayers until hadath occurs, just as wudu does.

Ruling on Tayammum for a Person with Wounds
Determines the ruling for tayammum vs washing based on majority of body wounded.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for a wounded person based on the majority of the body being wounded or healthy, and apply the rule without combining tayammum and washing.

Core Idea
If most of the body is wounded, tayammum is wajib; if most is healthy, wash and wipe the wound — do not combine both.

Performing purification with wounds requires careful application of the majority rule. This lesson clarifies when a wounded person must perform tayammum and when washing with wiping over the wound suffices, based on the Hanafi school's evidence from hadith.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
Determine if most of the body (or most of the limbs of wudu) is wounded or healthy. The ruling depends on the majority condition.
If half the body is wounded, treat as majority wounded according to the text.
2
Apply the ruling based on majority
If majority is wounded → perform tayammum (either for wudu or ghusl). If majority is healthy → wash the healthy parts and wipe over the wound (if bandaged).
Wiping over the wound is done by wiping over the bandage with wet hands.
3
Understand the principle of substitution
Tayammum is a substitute (nā'ib) for washing. When the original (washing) is possible, the substitute cannot be combined with it. Therefore, do not perform both tayammum and washing; one suffices.
The hadith mentions combining tayammum and washing, but it is interpreted for extensive wounds.
4
Examine the proof from hadith
The Prophet (peace be upon him) said that a wounded man who was told to wash and died should have performed tayammum and wiped over the wound. This proves that tayammum is sufficient when washing is harmful.
The Hanafis limit this to cases where the majority is wounded.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ترجمه : (۲۱۴) ولو كان اكثر البدن او نصفه جريحا تيمم . وان كان اكثره صحيحا غسله ومسح الجريح تشریح : یہاں یہ قاعدہ ہے کہ اکثر بدن زخمی ہو تو پورے بدن کو زخمی مان کر غسل کے لئے تیم کر لے، یا وضو میں جن اعضاء کو دھویا جاتا ہے اس کے اکثر زخمی ہے تو کل کو زخمی مان کر تیم کر لے ، اور اگر اکثر جگہ ٹھیک ہے تو کل کو ٹھیک مان کر فسل میں پورے بدن کو دھوئے اور وضو میں اعضاء وضو کو دھوئے ، اور جہاں زخم ہے وہاں پٹی باندھ کر اس پر مسح کر لے ۔ تا ہم تمیم بھی کرے، اور وضو بھی کرے، یا غسل کا تیم کرے، اور غسل جنابت بھی کرے یہ دونوں کو جمع کرنا ٹھیک نہیں ہے، کیونکہ تیتم نائب ہے اس لئے جب اصل آ گیا تو اس کے ساتھ نائب کو جمع کرنا جائز نہیں ہے۔ دونوں میں سے ایک کو کرنا کافی ہے۔ وجه : (۱) عن جابر قال خرجنا في سفر فاصاب رجلا منا حجرا فشجه فى رأسه ثم احتلم فسأل اصحابه فـقـال هـل تجدون لي رخصة في التيمم ؟ قالوا ما نجد لك رخصة و انت تقدر على الماء فاغتسل فمات فلما قدمنا على النبي علم اخبر بذالک فقال قتلوه قتلهم الله الا سألوا اذا لم يعلموا فانما شفاء العى السوال ، انما كان يكفيه ان يتيمم و يعصر او يعصب ـ شک موسی ـ علی جرحه خرقة ثم يمسح عليها و يغسل سائر جسده - ابوداود شریف باب المجد ودر تیم ص ۶۱ نمبر ۳۳۶) اس حدیث میں تیتیم اور غسل دونوں کو جمع کرنے کا اشارہ ملتا ہے لیکن تیم کی شکل میں زیادہ زخم پرمحمول کی جائے گی ، اور فسل ، اور وضو کی شکل میں کم زخم پر حمل کی جائے گی ۔(۲) عن ابن عباس يخبر ان رجلا اصابه جرح في رأسه على عهد رسول الله الله ثم اصابه احتلام فامر بالاغتسال فاغتسل فكز فمات فبلغ ذالك النبی الله الله فقال قتلوه قتلهم الله ، اولم يكن شفاء العى السوال ؟ قال
Translation: (214) And if most of the body or half of it is wounded, he performs tayammum. And if most of it is healthy, he washes it and wipes over the wound. Explanation: Here is the rule: if most of the body is wounded, consider the entire body as wounded and perform tayammum for ghusl; or if most of the limbs washed in wudu are wounded, consider all as wounded and perform tayammum. And if most parts are healthy, consider all as healthy and wash the entire body for ghusl and wash the limbs for wudu, and where there is a wound, bandage it and wipe over it. However, performing tayammum and also performing wudu, or performing tayammum for ghusl and also ghusl janabah, it is not correct to combine both, because tayammum is a substitute, so when the original is available, combining it with the substitute is not permissible. One of them is sufficient. Proof: (1) From Jabir: he said, 'We went out on a journey and a man was hit by a stone and wounded in his head, then he had a wet dream. He asked his companions: "Do you find any concession for me to perform tayammum?" They said: "We see no concession for you while you have water." So he took a bath and died. When we came to the Prophet (peace be upon him), he was told of that, and he said: "They killed him, may Allah kill them! Why did they not ask when they did not know? Indeed, the cure for ignorance is to ask. It would have been sufficient for him to perform tayammum and to wrap or bandage—Musa doubted—a cloth over his wound, then wipe over it and wash the rest of his body." (Abu Dawud, Bab al-Majd wa al-Tayammum, p.61 no.336). In this hadith, there is an indication of combining tayammum and washing, but it is interpreted for the case of extensive wounds; for the case of few wounds, it is interpreted for washing and wiping. (2) From Ibn Abbas: he reports that a man had a wound on his head at the time of the Messenger of Allah, then he had a wet dream, and he was ordered to take a bath, so he took a bath and died. The Prophet was told and said: "They killed him, may Allah kill them! Is not the cure for ignorance to ask?" He said...
Source pages p. 163

Commentary
This passage addresses the case of a person who has wounds on his body and needs purification. The Hanafi rule is based on the majority: if most of the body (or most of the limbs of wudu) are wounded, then tayammum is performed instead of washing. If most are healthy, then the healthy parts are washed, and the wound is wiped over the bandage. Importantly, one should not combine tayammum and washing; either one suffices because tayammum is a substitute. The proof is the hadith of Jabir and Ibn Abbas, where a wounded man was told to wash and died, and the Prophet condemned that, indicating that tayammum with wiping over the wound would have been sufficient. The commentary explains that the hadith is understood according to the extent of wounds.

Key Terms
جريح (jarih): A person with a wound on his body.
مسح على الجرح (mash 'ala al-jarh): Wiping over the wound with wet hands.
تيمم (tayammum): Dry purification using earth or dust as a substitute for wudu or ghusl.
نائب (nā'ib): Substitute; here referring to tayammum as a substitute for washing with water.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) Wash the healthy parts and wipe over the wound
C) Only wipe over the wound and not wash anything
D) Combine tayammum and washing

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi rule for a wounded person depends on the majority of the body: if most is wounded, tayammum suffices; if most is healthy, wash and wipe over the wound, but never combine both.

Nullifiers of Tayammum
Ruling on nullifiers of tayammum

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the nullifiers of tayammum, identify the unique nullifier (ability to use water), and explain the Quranic proof.

Core Idea
Tayammum is nullified by whatever nullifies wudu, plus the ability to use sufficient water.

Tayammum is a substitute purification, but it has its own rules. In this lesson, we examine what breaks tayammum. You will see that in addition to the usual nullifiers of wudu, the very ability to use water for wudu also invalidates tayammum. This is derived from the Quranic verse that conditions tayammum upon the absence of water.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Tayammum is a valid purification method when water is unavailable. Its nullifiers are listed in the matn.
2
List the common nullifiers
Anything that nullifies wudu (e.g., passing urine, stool, wind, madhi, wadi) also nullifies tayammum.
This is because tayammum is a substitute (badal) for wudu.
3
Spot the additional nullifier
The ability to use sufficient water for wudu also nullifies tayammum. This is unique to tayammum.
The Quranic condition 'if you find no water' implies that finding water lifts the permission.
4
Examine the proofs
The Quran (4:43) and the statement of al-Thawri in Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq support this ruling.
The verse: '...and you find no water, then perform tayammum...'
5
Apply the ruling
If a person performs tayammum and later becomes able to use water, the tayammum is broken and he must perform wudu for subsequent prayers.
His previous prayer performed with tayammum remains valid.

Source Text

فصل في سنن التيمم
ولا يجمع بين الغسل والتيمم . (۲۱۵) وينقضه ناقض الوضوء والقدرة على استعمال الماء
الکافی(۲۱۶) و مقطوع اليدين والرجلين اذا كان بوجهه جراحة يصلى بغير طهارة ولا يعيد. عطاء: فبلغنا ان رسول الله الله الله قال : لو غسل جسده و ترک رأسه حيث اصابه الجراح ۔ (ابن ماجہ شریف ، باب في الحجر وح تصيبه الجنابة فيخاف على نفسه ان انفسل ص ۸۱ نمبر۵۷۲ر دار قطنی، باب جواز التیم لصاحب الجراح، الخ ، ج اول ص ۱۹۸، نمبر (۷۲) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ جسم کے کم جگہ پر زخم ہو تو غسل جنابتہ میں باقی جگہ کو دھولے اور زخم کی جگہ پر پٹی باندھ کر مسح کرلے۔ جریج : زخمی۔
ترجمه : (۲۱۵) اور جو وضو کے ناقض ہیں وہی ناقض تیم ہیں۔ اور کافی پانی پراستعمال کی قدرت بھی ناقض تیم ہیں۔ تشریح : تیم وضو کا نائب ہے اس لئے وضو کوتوڑنے والی جتنی چیزیں ہیں وہ سب تیم کو توڑنے والی ہیں، مثلا حدث ، ندی، ودی، سے وضو ٹوٹتا ہے تو ان سے تھیم بھی ٹوٹ جائے گا، اور مزید ایک چیز سے تیم ٹوٹے گا، اتنے پانی کے استعمال پر قدرت ہو جائے جو وضو کے لئے کافی ہو تو اس سے تیم ٹوٹ جائے گا۔
وجه : (۱) فلم تجدوا ماء فتيمموا صعيدا طيبا . آيت ۴۳ ، سورة النساء (۴ ) . کہ پانی نہ ہو تو تیم کرو ۔ اور اس نے پانی پالیا اسلئے تیم ٹوٹ جائیگا ۔ (۲) عن الثورى قال اذا تيمم الرجل ثم مر بماء ، فقال حتى آتى ماء آخر فقد نقض تيممه ـ ويتوضأ لتلك الصلاة. (مصنف عبدالرزاق، باب تیم ثم يمر بالماء هل يتوضاً ؟ ، ج اول ،ص۱۸۰، نمبر۸۹۲) اس قول تابعی میں ہے کہ پانی پر گزرنے سے تیم ٹوٹ جائے گا۔ ترجمه : (۲۱۶) اور دونوں ہاتھ پاؤں کٹے ہوئے شخص کے منہ پر زخم ہو تو وہ بغیر طہارت کے نماز پڑھ لیوے اور پھر نہ دہرائے ۔

Chapter on the Sunnahs of Tayammum. And do not combine between ghusl and tayammum. (215) It is nullified by the nullifiers of wudu and the ability to use sufficient water. (216) And the one whose hands and feet are cut off, if his face has a wound, prays without purification and does not repeat. (This hadith indicates that if the wound is on a part of the body, in ghusl janabah he washes the rest and wipes over the bandage.) Translation: (215) The same things that nullify wudu nullify tayammum. And the ability to use sufficient water also nullifies tayammum. Explanation: Tayammum is the deputy of wudu, so everything that breaks wudu breaks tayammum, e.g., hadath, madhi, wadi. And one additional thing breaks tayammum: when one becomes able to use water sufficient for wudu. Proof: (1) '...and you find no water, then perform tayammum with clean earth' (Surah al-Nisa 4:43). Since he found water, tayammum is broken. (2) From al-Thawri: If a man performs tayammum then passes by water, he said: 'Until I reach other water' - he has nullified his tayammum and must perform wudu for that prayer. (Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq) This statement of a Tabi'i indicates that passing by water breaks tayammum. Translation (216): And a person whose both hands and feet are cut off, if he has a wound on his face, he should pray without purification and not repeat. Explanation: In tayammum, both hands are wiped, and he has no hands, so wiping the hands is dropped. The face is wiped, and his face has a wound, so wiping is also dropped. Therefore, he makes the intention of tayammum and prays without wiping anything, and there is no need to repeat the prayer later. Proof: From Aisha that she borrowed a necklace from Asma and it was lost, so the Messenger sent some of his Companions to search for it. The prayer time overtook them, and they prayed without wudu. When they came to the Prophet, they complained to him, and the verse of tayammum was revealed. (Bukhari, Muslim) In this hadith, the Companions did not find water and were not yet aware of tayammum, so they prayed without wudu, and the Prophet did not rebuke them. Similarly, this...
Source pages p. 164

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from the text. It covers three matters: (1) The prohibition of combining ghusl and tayammum simultaneously. (2) The nullifiers of tayammum. (3) A special case of a person with amputated limbs and a facial wound. The passage follows the order of the main text, then provides Urdu translation and commentary with Arabic proofs. The first ruling is straightforward: one cannot perform both ghusl and tayammum together; they are alternatives. The second ruling lists nullifiers: anything that nullifies wudu (like passing urine, stool, wind, or madhi) also nullifies tayammum. Additionally, the ability to use sufficient water nullifies tayammum, because tayammum is only permitted when water is unavailable. The proof for this is the verse of tayammum, which conditions the absence of water, and the statement of al-Thawri. The third ruling addresses a rare case: a person whose hands and feet are cut off and whose face has a wound. Since tayammum requires wiping the face and hands, but both are impossible (no hands to wipe and facial wound prevents wiping), the person is excused from tayammum entirely. He prays with the intention of tayammum but without actual wiping, and his prayer is valid without repetition. This is based on the incident of the Companions who prayed without wudu when they had no water and no knowledge of tayammum, and the Prophet did not require them to repeat. All rulings here are from the Hanafi school.

Key Terms
تيمم (tayammum): Dry ablution with clean earth as a substitute for wudu or ghusl when water is unavailable or harmful.
ناقض (naqid): That which nullifies or breaks the state of purity (taharah).

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Passing wind
B) The ability to use sufficient water
C) Madhi
D) Sleeping

Key Takeaway
Tayammum is nullified by the same things as wudu plus the ability to use sufficient water, so always check for water availability.

The Case of the Amputated Person
Special case ruling for amputated limbs and facial wound

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the ruling for a person with amputated limbs and a facial wound regarding tayammum, and state why prayer is valid without repetition.

Core Idea
When tayammum is impossible due to missing limbs and wounds, the obligation drops and prayer is valid without purification.

The text presents a special case: a person whose hands and feet are amputated and whose face has a wound. Tayammum normally requires wiping the face and hands, but here both are impossible. The Hanafi ruling is that such a person prays with only the intention of tayammum, without actual wiping, and the prayer is valid without repetition. This is based on the principle of necessity and the precedent of the Companions who prayed without wudu before the revelation of tayammum.

Guided Path
1
Identify the person and the situation
The person has both hands and feet amputated, and his face has a wound. This makes normal tayammum impossible.
2
Determine the requirement of tayammum
Tayammum requires wiping the face and hands. The hands are missing, and the face cannot be wiped due to wound.
3
Apply the ruling of dropping obligations
Since both wiping actions are impossible, they are dropped. The person makes intention (niyyah) for tayammum and prays without any wiping.
This is based on the principle that obligations are dropped when impossible (al-mashaqqah tajlib al-taysir).
4
Examine the proof
The proof is the incident of the Companions when they lost a necklace. They prayed without wudu because they had no water and no knowledge of tayammum, and the Prophet did not order them to repeat.
This shows that when purification is impossible, prayer without purification is valid.
5
Conclude the ruling
The prayer is valid (sahih) and does not need to be repeated (la yu'id).

الکافی(۲۱۶) و مقطوع اليدين والرجلين اذا كان بوجهه جراحة يصلى بغير طهارة ولا يعيد. عطاء: فبلغنا ان رسول الله الله الله قال : لو غسل جسده و ترک رأسه حيث اصابه الجراح ۔ (ابن ماجہ شریف ، باب في الحجر وح تصيبه الجنابة فيخاف على نفسه ان انفسل ص ۸۱ نمبر۵۷۲ر دار قطنی، باب جواز التیم لصاحب الجراح، الخ ، ج اول ص ۱۹۸، نمبر (۷۲) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ جسم کے کم جگہ پر زخم ہو تو غسل جنابتہ میں باقی جگہ کو دھولے اور زخم کی جگہ پر پٹی باندھ کر مسح کرلے۔ جریج : زخمی۔

(مصنف عبدالرزاق، باب تیم ثم يمر بالماء هل يتوضاً ؟ ، ج اول ،ص۱۸۰، نمبر۸۹۲) اس قول تابعی میں ہے کہ پانی پر گزرنے سے تیم ٹوٹ جائے گا۔ ترجمه : (۲۱۶) اور دونوں ہاتھ پاؤں کٹے ہوئے شخص کے منہ پر زخم ہو تو وہ بغیر طہارت کے نماز پڑھ لیوے اور پھر نہ دہرائے ۔

بخاری شریف ، باب استعارة الثياب للعروس و غيرها ،ص ۹۲۳ نمبر ۵۱۶۴ر مسلم شریف ، باب التیم ، ص ۱۵۸ نمبر ۸۱۷/۳۶۷) اس حدیث میں صحابی نے پانی نہیں پایا، اور ابھی تک تخم کا علم نہیں تھا تو بغیر وضو کے نماز پڑھی اور حضور نے کچھ نہیں فرمایا، اسی طرح یہ
Chapter on the Sunnahs of Tayammum. And do not combine between ghusl and tayammum. (215) It is nullified by the nullifiers of wudu and the ability to use sufficient water. (216) And the one whose hands and feet are cut off, if his face has a wound, prays without purification and does not repeat. Ata: It reached us that the Messenger of Allah said: If he washes his body and leaves his head where the wound is... (This hadith indicates that if the wound is on a part of the body, in ghusl janabah he washes the rest and wipes over the bandage.) Translation: (215) The same things that nullify wudu nullify tayammum. And the ability to use sufficient water also nullifies tayammum. Explanation: Tayammum is the deputy of wudu, so everything that breaks wudu breaks tayammum, e.g., hadath, madhi, wadi. And one additional thing breaks tayammum: when one becomes able to use water sufficient for wudu. Proof: (1) '...and you find no water, then perform tayammum with clean earth' (Surah al-Nisa 4:43). Since he found water, tayammum is broken. (2) From al-Thawri: If a man performs tayammum then passes by water, he said: 'Until I reach other water' - he has nullified his tayammum and must perform wudu for that prayer. (Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq) This statement of a Tabi'i indicates that passing by water breaks tayammum. Translation (216): And a person whose both hands and feet are cut off, if he has a wound on his face, he should pray without purification and not repeat. Explanation: In tayammum, both hands are wiped, and he has no hands, so wiping the hands is dropped. The face is wiped, and his face has a wound, so wiping is also dropped. Therefore, he makes the intention of tayammum and prays without wiping anything, and there is no need to repeat the prayer later. Proof: From Aisha that she borrowed a necklace from Asma and it was lost, so the Messenger sent some of his Companions to search for it. The prayer time overtook them, and they prayed without wudu. When they came to the Prophet, they complained to him, and the verse of tayammum was revealed. (Bukhari, Muslim) In this hadith, the Companions did not find water and were not yet aware of tayammum, so they prayed without wudu, and the Prophet did not rebuke them. Similarly, this...
Source pages p. 164

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from the text. It covers three matters: (1) The prohibition of combining ghusl and tayammum simultaneously. (2) The nullifiers of tayammum. (3) A special case of a person with amputated limbs and a facial wound. The passage follows the order of the main text, then provides Urdu translation and commentary with Arabic proofs. The first ruling is straightforward: one cannot perform both ghusl and tayammum together; they are alternatives. The second ruling lists nullifiers: anything that nullifies wudu (like passing urine, stool, wind, or madhi) also nullifies tayammum. Additionally, the ability to use sufficient water nullifies tayammum, because tayammum is only permitted when water is unavailable. The proof for this is the verse of tayammum, which conditions the absence of water, and the statement of al-Thawri. The third ruling addresses a rare case: a person whose hands and feet are cut off and whose face has a wound. Since tayammum requires wiping the face and hands, but both are impossible (no hands to wipe and facial wound prevents wiping), the person is excused from tayammum entirely. He prays with the intention of tayammum but without actual wiping, and his prayer is valid without repetition. This is based on the incident of the Companions who prayed without wudu when they had no water and no knowledge of tayammum, and the Prophet did not require them to repeat. All rulings here are from the Hanafi school.

Key Terms
مقطوع اليدين (maqtu' al-yadayn): A person whose hands are cut off (amputated).
جراحة (jarahah): Wound; a physical injury.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) He must perform tayammum by striking his stumps on earth.
B) He prays without purification and his prayer is valid.
C) He must have someone help him perform tayammum.
D) He is excused from prayer.

Key Takeaway
When tayammum is impossible due to physical incapacity, the obligation drops and prayer is valid without purification.

The Ruling and Conditions of Wiping over Khuffs (Mas'h 'ala al-Khuffain)
Ruling and conditions of mas'h 'ala al-khuffain

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on wiping over khuffs, identify the conditions for its validity, and distinguish the eight types of khuffs mentioned in the text.

Core Idea
Wiping over khuffs is valid for minor hadath even if made of thick cloth; the proof is mutawatir hadith.

This passage introduces the chapter on wiping over khuffs, a key concession in taharah. The Hanafi school affirms its validity based on mass-transmitted hadith, and expands the definition of khuff to include any thick covering that prevents water seepage. We will examine the ruling, the proof, and the various types of khuffs recognized in the tradition.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The passage states that wiping over khuffs is valid (sahih) for minor hadath (al-hadath al-asghar) for both men and women. This is the core ruling.
2
Locate the proof (dalil)
The proof is cited from the mutawatir hadith of Sa'd ibn Abi Waqqas that the Prophet (ﷺ) wiped over his khuffs. The Hanafi school relies on this sunnah as the primary evidence.
The passage also mentions Imam al-Shafi'i's argument from a qira'ah, but the Hanafi response is that the hadith is mutawatir.
3
Apply the condition of material
The khuff may be made of any thick material, not necessarily leather, as long as it prevents water from reaching the skin. This is a key Hanafi position.
The presence or absence of a leather sole is irrelevant.
4
Distinguish minor vs. major hadath
Wiping is only valid for states requiring wudu (minor hadath). It is not valid for janabah or other states requiring ghusl (major hadath).
This limitation is clearly stated in the commentary.
5
Classify the eight types of khuffs
The passage enumerates eight types, from thick leather to thin cloth. Only those that are thick and non-porous are valid for mas'h. Identify each category.
Refer to the list: mujallad, mun'al, takhthin, jūrab, jūrbān yashafān, jarmūqayn, mūqayn.
