Chapter on wiping over the khuffs. (217) Wiping over the khuffs is valid for minor hadath for men and women, even if they are made of thick material other than leather, whether they have a leather sole or not. [A man who does not have the ability to purify would pray without purification.] Chapter: The explanation of wiping over socks. Necessary note: Mas'h means to pass a wet hand over a limb or something. Proof: (1) From Abu Waqqas that the Prophet wiped over the khuffs. (Bukhari, Muslim) This hadith indicates that he wiped over the khuffs. The proof for wiping over khuffs is from mutawatir hadith. However, if one recites 'wa arjulakum' with a kasrah in the verse (Surah al-Ma'idah 5:6), Imam al-Shafi'i says that this implies the permissibility of wiping over khuffs. [1] Khuff: leather sock. There are 8 types of khuffs: [2] Mujallad: thick cloth sock with leather on the sole and edges. (1) Mun'al: thick cloth sock with leather only on the sole. [3] [4] Takhthīn: thick cloth sock with no leather anywhere. [5] Jūrab: cloth sock with no leather. [1] Jūrbān yashafān: thin cloth sock through which water can seep to the skin. [7] Jarmūqayn: wearing a leather sock over another leather sock. [8] Mūqayn: wearing thick socks over the first pair; they are mu'qayn. Translation: (217) Wiping over socks is permissible for men and women in minor hadath, even if the sock is made of thick material other than leather, and whether or not it has a leather sole. Explanation: Wiping over socks is not permissible where ghusl is required, but only where wudu is required due to minor hadath. If a sock is made of thick cloth other than leather such that the water for wiping does not seep through to the skin, then it is permissible.
Source pages p. 165

Commentary
This passage begins a new chapter on the important topic of wiping over khuffs (mas'h 'ala al-khuffain). It begins by stating the ruling: wiping over khuffs is valid (sahih) for minor hadath (al-hadath al-asghar, i.e., states that require wudu) for both men and women. Importantly, the khuff does not have to be made of leather; it can be made of any thick material that prevents water from seeping through to the skin. The presence or absence of a leather sole is irrelevant. The author then provides a definition of mas'h, a proof from the hadith of Sa'd ibn Abi Waqqas (the Prophet wiped over his khuffs), and notes that the evidence for mas'h 'ala al-khuffain is mutawatir (mass-transmitted) in the Hanafi view. There is a brief mention of Imam al-Shafi'i's argument from the Quranic verse (Surah al-Ma'idah 5:6) with kasrah on arjulakum, implying wiping rather than washing. The passage then lists eight types of khuffs with technical terms. The commentary clarifies that wiping is not allowed for janabah or other states requiring ghusl; it is only for minor hadath. The key condition is that the khuff must be made of thick material such that water for mas'h does not reach the skin. This ruling is established by the Hanafi school based on the mutawatir hadith.

Key Terms
مسح على الخفين (mas'h 'ala al-khuffain): Passing a wet hand over the khuffs (socks or boots) as a substitute for washing the feet in wudu.
خف (khuff): A covering for the feet, traditionally made of leather, but in this context includes thick cloth socks that prevent water seepage.
تخینین (takhthīn): A thick cloth sock without any leather, one of the eight types of khuffs.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) A thick woollen sock that prevents water from reaching the skin
C) A leather boot worn over a thin sock
D) A cloth sock with a small hole

Key Takeaway
Wiping over khuffs is a valid substitute for washing feet in wudu, permitted for any thick covering that prevents water from reaching the skin, based on mutawatir hadith.

Taharah — Purification

First Condition for Wiping over Khuffs: Wearing After Washing Feet
States the first condition for wiping over khuffs and provides evidence

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the first condition for wiping over khuffs and identify the primary evidence from hadith.

Core Idea
Khuffs must be worn after feet are washed; wiping invalid if condition unmet.

Wiping over khuffs is a concession in wudu, but it has conditions. The first and most important condition is that the khuffs must be put on after the feet have been washed and are pure. This lesson explores the exact ruling, the two valid sequences, and the primary proof from the Sunnah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the condition
Read the first line of the Arabic text. It states that the first condition is wearing the khuffs after washing both feet. Note that this includes two permissible sequences.
The condition is a prerequisite for the validity of wiping.
2
Analyze the two scenarios
The text explains two ways: (1) complete wudu then wear khuffs; (2) wash feet, wear khuffs, then complete wudu. The key is that no invalidator occurs between washing feet and completing wudu.
If wudu breaks before completion, wiping is not valid.
3
Examine the primary evidence
The hadith of Mughirah ibn Shu'bah is cited. The Prophet said, 'Leave them, for I put them on while both [feet] were pure.' This proves that the feet must be pure at the time of wearing.
The imperative to leave the khuffs implies wiping is allowed under that condition.
4
Consider the supporting narration
The athar from Sa'd ibn Abi Waqqas reinforces the condition. He says wiping is valid if feet were pure when put into khuffs, and removal is only for janabah.
This shows the condition was understood and practiced by Companions.
5
Contrast with other schools
Some schools allow wiping if khuffs were worn in a state of purity, even if not immediately after washing. The Hanafi position requires washing immediately before wearing (or completing wudu without an invalidator).
The difference affects many practical scenarios.

الاول لبسهما بعد غسل الرجلين ولو قبل كمال الوضوء اذا اتمه قبل حصول ناقض للوضوء. وجه : (ا) عن مغيرة بن شعبة قال كنت مع النبي ﷺ في سفر فاهويت لا نزع خفيه فقال دعهما فاني ادخلتهما طاهرتين فمسح عليهما . (بخاری شریف، باب اذا ادخل رجلیه و هما طاهرتان ، ص ۴۰ نمبر ۲۰۶) (۲) عن سعد بن ابي وقاص خرج من الخلاء فتوضأ ومسح على خفيه فقيل له : أتمسح عليهما وقد خرجت من الخلاء قال: نعم اذا ادخلت القدمين الخفين و هما طاهرتان فامسح عليهما ولا تخلعهما الا لجنابة - (مصنف ابن ابی شیبۃ ، باب ۲۱۸ من کان لا يوقت في المسح شيئاً ، ج اول ص ۱۶۸ نمبر ۱۹۳۳ مصنف عبدالرزاق، باب المسح على الخفين ، ج اول ص ۱۵۴، نمبر ۷۶ ) تشریح : موزے پر مسح کرنے کی پہلی شرط یہ ہے کہ دونوں پاؤں کو دھو کر موزہ پہنا ہو۔ اس کی دوصورتیں ہیں [1] ایک یہ ہے کہ وضو مکمل کرنے کے بعد موزہ پہنے۔ [۲] دوسری صورت یہ ہے کہ پہلے پاؤں دھو کر موزہ پہن لے، اس کے بعد ہاتھ اور منہ دھوئے، لیکن شرط یہ ہے کہ وضوٹو ٹنے سے پہلے وضو مکمل کر ليا ہو، پس اگر وضو پورے ہونے سے پہلے وضوٹوٹ گیا تو مسح کرنا جائز نہیں ہے۔
First [condition]: wearing them after washing the two feet, even if before completing wudu, provided that he completes it before something that invalidates wudu occurs. Evidence: (1) From Mughirah ibn Shu'bah: I was with the Prophet (peace be upon him) on a journey, and I bent down to remove his khuffs, and he said: 'Leave them, for I put them on while both [feet] were pure.' So he wiped over them. (2) From Sa'd ibn Abi Waqqas: He came out of the lavatory, performed wudu, and wiped over his khuffs. Someone said to him: 'Do you wipe over them after coming out of the lavatory?' He said: 'Yes. When you put your feet into the khuffs while they are pure, then wipe over them and do not remove them except for janabah.' Explanation: The first condition for wiping over khuffs is that both feet are washed before putting on the khuff. There are two forms: (1) putting on the khuff after completing wudu, (2) first washing the feet and putting on the khuff, then washing the face and hands, provided that wudu is completed before an invalidator occurs. If wudu breaks before completion, then wiping is not permissible.
Source pages p. 166

Commentary
This passage presents the first of seven conditions for the validity of wiping over khuffs (leather socks). The condition is that the khuffs must be worn after the feet have been washed and are in a state of ritual purity (tahara). The author explains two scenarios: either the entire wudu is completed before putting on the khuffs, or the feet are washed first, the khuffs are put on, and then the rest of wudu is completed. The key point is that the feet must be pure at the time of wearing, and no invalidator of wudu (hadath) may occur between washing the feet and completing wudu. The evidence cited includes the well-known hadith of Mughirah ibn Shu'bah from Sahih al-Bukhari, where the Prophet (peace be upon him) explicitly states that he put his khuffs on while his feet were pure. This is the primary evidence. Additionally, an athar from Sa'd ibn Abi Waqqas shows that the Companion understood this condition and applied it, also noting that removal of khuffs is only required for major ritual impurity (janabah), not for minor hadath. Hanafi fiqh relies on these proofs to establish this condition. Note: In the Hanafi school, this condition is part of the seven known conditions for wiping over khuffs, and it is considered a ruling from the Zahir al-Riwayah.

Key Terms
الخف (al-khuff): Leather sock that covers the foot and ankle, worn for travel or cold, upon which wiping (mash) is permitted in wudu.
طاهرتان (tahiratani): Dual feminine of tahir, meaning both feet are in a state of ritual purity, specifically after being washed in wudu.

C) The khuffs must be pure and cover the ankles.

Key Takeaway
The first condition for wiping over khuffs is that they must be worn after the feet have been washed and remain pure until wudu is completed.

The Four Conditions for Wiping over Khuffs
Matn + commentary listing four conditions with proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the four conditions for valid wiping over khuffs and identify the proof for each condition from the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
Khuff wiping substitutes foot-washing only if the khuff fully covers, allows walking, has minimal tears, and stays on unaided.

In this lesson, we examine the second through fifth conditions that make wiping over khuffs a valid substitute for washing the feet in wudu. Each condition is grounded in the practice of the Prophet ﷺ and the Companions. Understanding these conditions ensures that the rukhsah (concession) is applied correctly without overstepping its limits.

Guided Path
1
Identify the second condition
The khuff must cover both ankle bones (ka'bain). If it is shorter, the foot is not fully covered and wiping is invalid. Proof: hadith of Jabir showing extent of wiping from toes to shin.
2
Identify the third condition
The khuff must permit customary walking. Materials like glass, wood, or iron do not allow normal walking, so wiping on them is invalid. Proof: the Prophet wiped on leather khuffs, which are worn for walking.
This condition is specific to Hanafi school; Shafi'i does not require it.
3
Identify the fourth condition
Each khuff must be free of a tear equivalent to three of the smallest toes. If the tear is that large, the foot is considered exposed, invalidating wiping. Smaller tears are overlooked. Proof: hadith that if the foot emerges, wiping is not allowed.
The measurement is by the smallest toes of the foot.
4
Identify the fifth condition
The khuff must stay on the foot without being tied. It must be thick or structured enough to remain in place naturally. Proof: implied from the definition of khuff as a covering that stays on without extra fastening.
If the khuff falls off when walking without tying, wiping is invalid even if tied afterwards.
5
Review the overall requirement
All conditions must be met at the time of wiping. If any condition is violated, wiping is invalid and the feet must be washed. The practical effect (thamarah al-khilaf) is that many modern shoes do not qualify as khuffs.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

ترجمه : (۲۲۰) (۳) تیسری شرط یہ ہے کہ ان موزوں سے معتاد چلنا ممکن ہو، تو اب کا نچ یا لکڑی یا لوہے کے موزے پر مسح جائز نہیں۔ تشریح : حضور نے اصل تو چمڑے کے موزے پر مسح فرمایا ہے، جس میں صحیح طور پر چلنا ممکن ہے ، اس لئے ایسے موزے پر مسح جائز ہے جس میں معتادطور پر چلنا ممکن ہو، چونکہ کانچ کے موزے لکڑی کے موزے، یا لوہے کے موزے میں معتادطور پر چلناممکن نہیں اس لئے ان پر مسح بھی جائز نہیں ہے۔ وجه : اس حدیث میں اس کا اشارہ موجود ہے۔ عن ابی وقاص عن النبي علم انه مسح على الخفين. (بخاری شریف، باب المسح على الخفين، ص ۳۹ نمبر ۲۰۲ مسلم شریف ، باب المحعلی الخفین، ص ۱۳۲ نمبر ۶۲۶/۲۷ ) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ آپ صلى الله عليه وسلم نے چمڑے کے موزے پر مسح فرمایا۔ جس سے استدلال کیا جا سکتا ہے کہ غیر معتاد موزے پر مسح جائز نہ ہو۔ معتاد: جس میں عادت کے طور پر چلنا آسان ہو۔ زجاج: کانچ ،شیشہ۔
ترجمه : (۲۲۱) چوتھی شرط یہ ہے کہ: دونوں میں سے ہر ایک پاؤں کی چھوٹی انگلیوں میں سے تین انگلیوں کی مقدار پھٹن سے خالی ہو۔ تشریح : ہر موزے میں الگ الگ طور پر پاؤں کی چھوٹی انگلیوں کی مقدار سے تین انگلیوں کی مقدار پھٹن نہ ہو تب اس موزے پر مسح جائز ہو گا۔ اگر دونوں موزوں کو ملا کر تین انگلیوں کی مقدار پھٹن ہو تو اس سے مسح جائز ہے۔ تین انگلیاں اس لئے ہے کہ یہ اکثر قدم ہے جو موزہ نکلنے کے درجے میں ہے۔ وجه : (۱) عن رجل من اصحاب النبي الله في الرجل يمسح على خفيه ثم يبدو له فينزعهما قال يغسل قدميه (السن للبیھقی ، باب من ضلع خفیه بعد مامسح علیهما ج اول ص ۴۳۲، نمبر۱۳۷۰) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ موزہ نکل جائے تو مسح جائز نہیں ہے، اور تین انگلیوں کی مقدار پھٹا ہوا ہو تو گویا کہ نکلنا ہے اس لئے مسح جائز نہیں ہوگا۔(۲) سألت معمرا عن الخرق يكون في الخف فقال اذا خرج من مواضع الوضوء شيء فلا تمسح عليه واخلع (اسن للبيهقي ، باب الخف الذى مسیح علیہ رسول الله ج اول ص ۴۲۵، نمبر ۱۳۴۷ مصنف ابن ابی شیبة ، ۲۲۱ فی الرجل میسج علی خفیہ ثم مخلعها ، ج اول ص ۱۷۰، نمبر ۱۹۵۸) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ موزے میں پھٹن ہو اور پاؤں نکل جاتا ہو تو اس پر مسح نہ کرے اور کھول کر پاؤں دھوئے ۔
ترجمه : (۲۲۲) [۵] پانچویں شرط یہ ہے کہ : پاؤں پر بغیر باندھے موزہ پھہر سکے۔ تشریح : موزہ اتنا موٹا ہو یا موزے کی ساخت ایسی ہو کہ وہ بغیر الگ سے باندھے ہوئے پاؤں پر ٹھہر جائے تب اس پر مسح جائز
(219) The second condition: both [khuffs] cover the ankles. (220) The third condition: possibility of walking customarily in them, so it is not allowed on a khuff of glass, wood, or iron. (221) The fourth condition: each of them is free from a tear of the size of three smallest toes. (222) The fifth condition: they stay on the feet without tying. Translation of Urdu commentary: For (219): The second condition: the khuffs must cover both ankles. Explanation: If the khuff covers the ankle, wiping is allowed; if smaller, not allowed. Evidence: (1) Hadith from a Companion: if the khuff is removed, one must wash the feet. (2) Hadith of Jabir: wiping extends from toes to shin. For (220): Third condition: customary walking possible; not allowed on glass, wood, or iron. Explanation: The Prophet wiped on leather khuffs which allow normal walking. Other materials do not allow normal walking, so wiping is not allowed. Evidence: Hadith of Abu Waqqas: the Prophet wiped on leather khuffs. For (221): Fourth condition: each khuff is free from a tear equal to three smallest toes. Explanation: If tear is less than that in each or combined, wiping is allowed; if three toes size, it is considered as if the foot is exposed. Evidence: (1) Hadith: if the foot emerges, wiping is invalid. (2) Hadith: if the foot comes out of the tear, do not wipe but remove and wash. For (222): Fifth condition: the khuffs stay on without tying. Explanation: The khuff must be thick or structured so it stays on without a separate tie; then wiping is allowed.
Source pages p. 167

Commentary
This passage from Thamaratun Najah presents the second to fifth conditions for the validity of wiping over khuffs (leather socks) during wudu. The author begins by stating the conditions in the matn (primary text) and then provides the Urdu commentary with evidence. The second condition requires that the khuffs cover the ankles. If they are shorter, wiping is not valid because the part that needs to be washed (the foot up to the ankles) is not covered. The proof is from the practice of the Companions and a hadith indicating the extent of wiping. The third condition requires that the khuffs permit customary walking. The Prophet wiped on leather khuffs, so only materials that allow normal walking are acceptable. Glass, wood, or iron khuffs do not allow this, so wiping on them is invalid. The proof is from the hadith of the Prophet wiping on leather khuffs. The fourth condition sets a maximum tear: if each khuff has a tear the size of three of the smallest toes, it is as if the foot is exposed, so wiping is invalid. Smaller tears are ignored. The proof is from hadith indicating that if the foot emerges, wiping is not allowed. The fifth condition requires that the khuffs stay on the feet without being tied. They must be thick or structured enough to remain in place on their own. If they fall off without tying, wiping is invalid. These conditions ensure that the khuffs serve their purpose as a covering for the feet.

Key Terms
خف (khuff): A leather sock or boot that covers the foot and ankle, worn over wudu.
مسح (mas-h): Wiping wet hands over the khuff instead of washing the feet in wudu.
خرق (kharq): A tear in the khuff exposing the foot.
كعب (ka'b): The ankle bone, protruding on each side of the foot.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
The four conditions ensure that the khuff is a true covering that substitutes foot washing, based on the practice of the Prophet and the Companions.

Condition of Khuff Material for Wiping Over
Ruling with proof on impermissibility of wiping over non-leather khuffs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the condition of the khuff material for wiping and apply it to determine the permissibility of wiping over a given material in wudu.

Core Idea
Wiping over khuffs is only valid on materials that allow customary walking.

The Hanafi school permits wiping over khuffs during wudu as a concession, but this concession is not unlimited. The key condition is that the khuff must be of a material that allows normal walking. This lesson examines the ruling on khuffs made of glass, wood, or iron, and the evidence from the Prophet's practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is wiping over khuffs. The text rules that wiping over khuffs made of glass, wood, or iron is not permissible.
The ruling applies specifically to these materials because they do not allow customary walking.
2
Understand the condition (mu'tad)
The text explains that the Prophet originally wiped over leather khuffs, which allow walking properly. The condition is that the khuff must be such that walking in it is possible in the customary manner (mu'tad).
Customary walking means it is easy and normal to walk in the khuff.
3
Examine the dalil
The proof is a hadith from Abu Waqqas that the Prophet wiped over leather khuffs (Bukhari and Muslim). The text uses this to infer that non-customary khuffs are excluded.
The hadith is ahad (non-mutawatir), but sufficient for this ruling.
4
Derive the wajh al-dalalah
The Prophet's specific practice on leather indicates that the permissibility is tied to the suitability for walking, since leather is a material that naturally allows customary walking. Materials like glass, wood, and iron do not.
The 'illa (effective cause) is the ability to walk customarily, not the material itself.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
على خف من زجاج او خشب او حديد. جائز نہیں۔ تشریح : حضور نے اصل تو چمڑے کے موزے پر مسح فرمایا ہے، جس میں صحیح طور پر چلنا ممکن ہے ، اس لئے ایسے موزے پر مسح جائز ہے جس میں معتادطور پر چلنا ممکن ہو، چونکہ کانچ کے موزے لکڑی کے موزے، یا لوہے کے موزے میں معتادطور پر چلناممکن نہیں اس لئے ان پر مسح بھی جائز نہیں ہے۔ وجه : اس حدیث میں اس کا اشارہ موجود ہے۔ عن ابی وقاص عن النبي علم انه مسح على الخفين. (بخاری شریف، باب المسح على الخفين، ص ۳۹ نمبر ۲۰۲ مسلم شریف ، باب المحعلی الخفین، ص ۱۳۲ نمبر ۶۲۶/۲۷ ) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ آپ صلى الله عليه وسلم نے چمڑے کے موزے پر مسح فرمایا۔ جس سے استدلال کیا جا سکتا ہے کہ غیر معتاد موزے پر مسح جائز نہ ہو۔ معتاد: جس میں عادت کے طور پر چلنا آسان ہو۔ زجاج: کانچ ،شیشہ۔
On a khuff of glass or wood or iron. Not permissible. Explanation: The Prophet originally wiped over leather khuffs, in which walking is possible properly. Therefore, wiping is permissible over a khuff in which walking is possible in the customary manner. Since walking is not possible in the customary manner on glass khuffs, wooden khuffs, or iron khuffs, therefore wiping over them is also not permissible. Evidence: There is an indication in this hadith. From Abu Waqqas from the Prophet that he wiped over the khuffs. (Bukhari, Bab al-Mash ala al-Khuffayn, p. 39 no. 202; Muslim, Bab al-Mash ala al-Khuffayn, p. 132 no. 626/27) This hadith states that the Prophet wiped over leather khuffs. From this it can be inferred that wiping over non-customary khuffs is not permissible. Mu'tad: that in which walking is easy customarily. Zujaj: glass.
Source pages p. 168

Commentary
This passage states the ruling regarding the material of the khuff. The Hanafi position is that wiping over khuffs is only permissible if the khuff is made of leather or similar material that allows normal walking. The text explicitly rules that khuffs made of glass, wood, or iron do not permit wiping. The evidence is taken from the practice of the Prophet (peace be upon him) who wiped over leather khuffs. Since glass, wood, and iron are not materials in which walking is customary, they are excluded. The commentary explains that the original permissibility is established for leather, and by analogy, any material that allows customary walking is permissible, while those that do not are impermissible.

Key Terms
خف (khuff): A leather sock or boot worn over the foot, usually made of thick leather, reaching above the ankle, over which wiping is permitted in wudu under certain conditions.
مسح (mash): Wiping; in this context, passing wet hands over the khuff instead of washing the feet during wudu.
زجاج (zujaj): Glass; a material from which khuffs are not customarily made for walking.
معتاد (mu'tad): Customary; that which is normally used and easy for walking.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Wiping over khuffs is only valid if the khuff is made of a material that allows customary walking, as evidenced by the Prophet's practice on leather.

Condition of No Hole of Three Fingers in Khuff
States a condition and supports with naqli evidence

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the condition regarding holes in khuffs for wiping and apply it to determine validity.

Core Idea
A khuff with a hole of three smallest toes is like being removed — wiping invalid.

Wiping over khuffs is a concession that replaces washing the feet. But this concession has conditions. One key condition is that the khuff must be intact enough to cover the foot. This lesson examines the Hanafi position on the size of a hole that breaks the coverage and makes wiping invalid.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is wiping over khuffs. The ruling being conditioned is its permissibility. The condition is that each khuff must be free from a hole of three small toes.
The ruling category here is shart (condition), not a hukm taklifi.
2
Understand the measurement
The hole is measured by the smallest toes of the foot. Three of those toes, if exposed, is the threshold. This is considered 'majority of the foot' and equivalent to removal.
The measurement is per individual khuff, not combined.
3
Examine the evidence
The passage cites two narrations: a Companion's statement about removing the khuff, and Ma'mar's instruction that if the foot emerges from wudu places, wiping is invalid.
The evidence is of zanni thubut and dalala, yet relied upon in practice.
4
Apply the condition
If each khuff has less than three fingers' hole, wiping is valid. If combined across both khuffs it totals three, still valid because condition applies individually.
This is a key practical distinction.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والرابع خلو كل منهما عن خرق قدر ثلاث اصابع من اصغر اصابع القدم . ترجمه : (۲۲۱) چوتھی شرط یہ ہے کہ: دونوں میں سے ہر ایک پاؤں کی چھوٹی انگلیوں میں سے تین انگلیوں کی مقدار پھٹن سے خالی ہو۔ تشریح : ہر موزے میں الگ الگ طور پر پاؤں کی چھوٹی انگلیوں کی مقدار سے تین انگلیوں کی مقدار پھٹن نہ ہو تب اس موزے پر مسح جائز ہو گا۔ اگر دونوں موزوں کو ملا کر تین انگلیوں کی مقدار پھٹن ہو تو اس سے مسح جائز ہے۔ تین انگلیاں اس لئے ہے کہ یہ اکثر قدم ہے جو موزہ نکلنے کے درجے میں ہے۔ وجه : (۱) عن رجل من اصحاب النبي الله في الرجل يمسح على خفيه ثم يبدو له فينزعهما قال يغسل قدميه (السن للبیھقی ، باب من ضلع خفیه بعد مامسح علیهما ج اول ص ۴۳۲، نمبر۱۳۷۰) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ موزہ نکل جائے تو مسح جائز نہیں ہے، اور تین انگلیوں کی مقدار پھٹا ہوا ہو تو گویا کہ نکلنا ہے اس لئے مسح جائز نہیں ہوگا۔(۲) سألت معمرا عن الخرق يكون في الخف فقال اذا خرج من مواضع الوضوء شيء فلا تمسح عليه واخلع (اسن للبيهقي ، باب الخف الذى مسیح علیہ رسول الله ج اول ص ۴۲۵، نمبر ۱۳۴۷ مصنف ابن ابی شیبة ، ۲۲۱ فی الرجل میسج علی خفیہ ثم مخلعها ، ج اول ص ۱۷۰، نمبر ۱۹۵۸) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ موزے میں پھٹن ہو اور پاؤں نکل جاتا ہو تو اس پر مسح نہ کرے اور کھول کر پاؤں دھوئے ۔
And the fourth: that each of them is free from a hole of the measure of three fingers from the smallest toes. Translation: (221) The fourth condition is that each of the two [khuffs] is free from a tear of the measure of three fingers from the small toes. Explanation: If each khuff individually does not have a tear of three fingers' measure from the small toes, then wiping is permissible on that khuff. If by combining both khuffs the tear equals three fingers, then wiping is permissible. Three fingers because it is the majority of the foot, which is at the level of the khuff coming off. Evidence: (1) From a man from the Companions of the Prophet regarding a man who wiped over his khuffs then decided to remove them. He said: He should wash his feet. (al-Bayhaqi, Bab man khala'a khuffayhi ba'd ma masaha 'alayhima, vol. 1, p. 432, no. 1370) This hadith states that if the khuff comes off, wiping is not permissible, and a tear of three fingers is like it coming off, so wiping is not permissible. (2) I asked Ma'mar about a tear in the khuff; he said: If something comes out from the places of wudu, then do not wipe over it and remove it. (al-Bayhaqi, Bab al-khuff alladhi masaha 'alayhi Rasulullah, vol. 1, p. 425, no. 1347; Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah, no. 1958) This hadith states that if there is a tear in the khuff and the foot comes out, do not wipe over it and wash the feet.
Source pages p. 168

Commentary
This passage details the fourth condition for the validity of wiping over khuffs: there must be no hole in the khuff equivalent to three of the smallest toes in size. This condition applies individually to each khuff; if the total hole across both khuffs equals three fingers but individually less, wiping is still valid. The threshold of three fingers is set because it is considered the point where the foot is effectively exposed, as if the khuff has come off. The evidence includes two narrations: one from a Companion indicating that if the khuff is removed, wiping is nullified; the other from Ma'mar, a Tabi'i, stating that if any part of the wudu area emerges, wiping is invalid. Thus, a tear allowing such exposure invalidates wiping.

Key Terms
خرق (kharq): A hole or tear in the khuff.
اصابع (asabi'): Fingers; here used for toes (اصابع القدم) as the measure.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If each khuff has a hole of two small toes, but combined they equal three toes, is wiping valid?
A) Yes, because each individual khuff has less than three fingers
B) No, because the total is three fingers
C) No, because the hole is in both
D) Yes, because three fingers is allowed

Key Takeaway
A hole of three smallest toes in a khuff invalidates wiping; this is measured per khuff individually.

The Fifth Condition for Wiping over Khuff: Self-Supporting Without Tying
Fifth condition: khuff must stay on foot without tying.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the fifth condition for the validity of wiping over khuff and apply it to determine whether a particular khuff qualifies.

Core Idea
Wiping over khuff is a dispensation; only a khuff that stays on without tying preserves the dispensation's basis.

This lesson unpacks the fifth condition from the classical Hanafi text: the khuff must remain on the foot without external tying. We'll explore why this matters, how it's derived from analogy to leather khuffs, and how to apply it today.

Guided Path
1
State the condition
The fifth condition is that the khuff stays on the foot without additional tying. Read the Arabic phrase and its translation carefully.
The Arabic uses 'استمساكهما على الرجلين من غير شد'.
2
Understand the rationale
The original permissibility of wiping is established for leather khuffs, which are thick and stay on without tying. The condition is derived from this attribute.
The author uses qiyas: the illa (effective cause) is firmness without external support.
3
Apply to modern khuffs
Today's khuffs often have elastic or rubber inside, making them self-supporting. Determine whether a given khuff meets the condition by testing if it stays on without tying.
If the khuff requires a lace or rubber band to stay on, it fails the condition.
4
Distinguish from other conditions
This is one of several conditions for wiping. Other conditions include that the khuff covers the feet to the ankles, is worn in a state of purity, etc. This condition is specific to the self-supporting nature.
Memorize the list of conditions from your fiqh text.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والخامس استمساكهما على الرجلين من غير شد. ترجمه : (۲۲۲) [۵] پانچویں شرط یہ ہے کہ : پاؤں پر بغیر باندھے موزہ پھہر سکے۔ تشریح : موزہ اتنا موٹا ہو یا موزے کی ساخت ایسی ہو کہ وہ بغیر الگ سے باندھے ہوئے پاؤں پر ٹھہر جائے تب اس پر مسح جائز ہوگا، اور اگر اتا پتلا ہے یا اتنا کھلا ہواہے کہ الگ سے ری سے باندھنے کی ضرورت ہے تو اس پر سح درست نہیں ہو گا۔ آج کل موزے کے اندر ہی ربر سیٹ کیا ہوتا ہے اس لئے الگ سے باندھنے کی ضرورت نہیں پڑتی۔ وجه : اصل تو پاؤں کو دھونا ہے، حدیث کی بنا پر چمڑے کے موزے پر مسح جائز قرار دیا گیا ہے اس لئے چمڑے کے موزے کی شرطیں ملحوظ رکھی گئیں ہیں ۔ لغت : استمساک: مسلک سے مشتق ہے بھہرا ر ہے۔ شد: باندھنا۔
And the fifth: their staying on the feet without tying. Translation: (222) [5] The fifth condition is that the khuff can stay on the foot without tying. Explanation: If the khuff is thick enough or its structure is such that it stays on the foot without separate tying, then wiping it is permissible. But if it is thin or so loose that it requires separate tying with a lace, then wiping it is not correct. Nowadays, khuffs have rubber inside them, so there is no need for separate tying. Evidence: The original ruling is to wash the feet; wiping over leather khuffs was made permissible based on hadith. Therefore, the conditions of leather khuffs are kept in mind. Vocabulary: 'Istimsak' is derived from 'masik' meaning holding; 'shadd' means tying.
Source pages p. 168

Commentary
This passage presents the fifth condition: the khuff must stay on the foot without needing to be tied. The key idea is that the khuff should be self-supporting; if it is so thin or loose that it requires a separate lace or fastener to remain on the foot, wiping is not valid. The commentary uses modern examples: today's khuffs often have elastic or rubber inside, making tying unnecessary. The evidence is rational: since the basic obligation is washing the feet, the dispensation of wiping is only for khuffs that are firmly attached like leather ones. Thus, a khuff that needs tying lacks this firmness.

Key Terms
استمساك (istimsak): Staying on; the property of a khuff that it remains on the foot without external support.
شد (shadd): Tying; additional fastening required for the khuff to stay.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is wiping not permissible on a thin khuff that requires a lace to stay on?
A) Because it does not cover the foot
B) Because it does not stay on without tying
C) Because it is not made of leather
D) Because it is too thin to prevent water

Key Takeaway
A khuff must stay on the foot without additional tying; otherwise, wiping over it is invalid.

The Impermeability Condition of Khuff
Sixth condition of khuff: must be impermeable.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the sixth condition of wiping over khuff and apply it to distinguish between thick and thin socks.

Core Idea
A khuff must be thick enough to block water from reaching the foot; otherwise, wiping is invalid.

This passage explains the sixth condition of wiping over the khuff: it must be impermeable. The author clarifies that a thin sock through which water seeps does not qualify. The evidence comes from the practice of early tabi'is who allowed wiping over thick socks. Understanding this condition helps you determine valid wiping scenarios in daily wudu.

Guided Path
1
Identify the condition
The passage states that the khuff must prevent water from reaching the foot. What specific quality does it require?
2
Understand the rationale
Why must the khuff be thick? Connect to the purpose of wiping.
3
Examine the evidence
The author cites two tabi'is. What is their statement? How does it support the condition?
4
Distinguish thickness
Apply the condition: cotton sock vs thin sock – which qualifies and why?
5
Note the cross-madhhab nuance
Some schools allow wiping on thin socks; the Hanafi school requires thickness.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والسادس منعهما وصول الماء الى الجسد . ترجمه : (۲۲۳) [۲] چھٹی شرط یہ ہے کہ: موزہ پاؤں تک پانی پہونچنے کو منع کرے۔ تشریح : اگر سوت کا موزہ ہے تو وہ اتنا موٹا ہو کہ جب اس پر مسح کرے تو اس کی تری پاؤں کی کھال تک نہ پہونچے ۔ اگر پتلا موزہ ہے جس میں مسح کا پانی چھن کر کھال تک پہنچ جاتا ہے تو اس پر مسح جائز نہیں ہوگا۔ وجه : عن سعيد بن المسيب و الحسن أنهما قالا : يمسح على الجوربين اذا كانا صفيقين . (مصنف ابن ابی شیبة ، ۲۲۳ فی المسیح علی الجوربین ، ج اول ص ۱۷۱ نمبر ۱۹۷۶) اس قول تابعی میں ہے کہ جورب موٹا ہو تو مسح کرے ورنہ نہیں۔
And the sixth: that they prevent water from reaching the body. Translation: (223) [2] The sixth condition is that the khuff prevents water from reaching the foot. Explanation: If it is a cotton khuff, it must be thick so that when one wipes it, the moisture does not reach the skin. If it is a thin khuff through which the water of wiping seeps to the skin, then wiping is not permissible. Evidence: From Sa'id ibn al-Musayyib and al-Hasan that they said: One may wipe over socks if they are thick. (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah, no. 1976) This statement of the Tabi'is indicates that if the sock is thick, wiping is allowed, otherwise not.
Source pages p. 169

Commentary
This passage explains the sixth condition: the khuff must be impermeable to water. The purpose of wiping is to simulate washing the feet; if the water from wiping passes through the khuff and reaches the foot, then the foot effectively gets wet, but the act of wiping over the khuff becomes meaningless. The condition is that the khuff must be thick enough that the moisture of the wiping hand does not penetrate to the skin. The evidence is the statement of two prominent Tabi'is, Sa'id ibn al-Musayyib and al-Hasan al-Basri, who allowed wiping over thick socks (jawrab). This analogy indicates that a khuff must similarly be thick.

Key Terms
جورب (jawrab): Sock; a foot covering made of cloth or similar material.
صفيق (safiq): Thick; referring to a sock that is dense enough to prevent water penetration.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Permissible if it covers the foot
B) Permissible if it is tied
C) Not permissible because water will seep through
D) Permissible only for travelers

Key Takeaway
The khuff must be thick enough to prevent water from reaching the foot; otherwise, wiping is invalid.

Condition for Wiping: The Front Part of the Foot
Seventh condition for wiping over khuffs: front foot length.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the seventh condition for wiping over khuffs and explain why the hadith of Jabir requires the front part to be at least three fingers long.

Core Idea
Wiping over khuffs requires the foot's front part to be three small fingers long; the act of wiping starts from the toes.

The seventh condition for wiping over khuffs is that the front part of the foot must be intact to the extent of three small fingers of the hand. This condition is derived from the very manner of wiping as demonstrated by the Prophet: starting from the tips of the toes and drawing the hand up to the shin. Without sufficient front part, the wiping cannot be performed according to the Sunnah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the condition
Read the passage and locate the exact wording of the seventh condition: that the front part of the foot (muqaddam al-qadam) must be at least three small fingers of the hand in length.
The text explicitly states 'قدر ثلاث اصابع من اصغر اصابع اليد' (measure of three fingers from the smallest fingers of the hand).
2
Understand the rationale
The condition is based on the act of wiping itself: the hand must draw from the toes upward. If the front part is missing, there is no place to start the wiping motion.
The commentary explains that the front part must be present for the fingers to be drawn over it.
3
Apply the condition to a scenario
Consider a person whose foot is amputated at the toes, leaving only the heel. Even if the heel is long, wiping is not valid because the front part is less than three fingers.
The text explicitly says: 'لو كان فاقدا مقدم قدمه لا يمسح على خفه ولو كان عقب القدم موجودا' (if one lacks the front part of his foot, he should not wipe over his khuff even if the heel is present).
4
Examine the proof
The hadith of Jabir describes the Prophet demonstrating wiping from the tips of the toes to the shin. This establishes the method and implies the necessity of the front part.
The hadith is cited: 'من اطراف الاصابع الى اصل الساق' (from the tips of the toes to the beginning of the shin).
5
Note the madhhab difference
This is a Hanafi condition; other schools may not specify a minimum length for the front part. Recognize that this is a point of ikhtilaf.
The analytical toolbox marks cross_madhhab_status as 'mukhtalaf_fih'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والسابع ان يبقى من مقدم القدم قدر ثلاث اصابع من اصغر اصابع اليد. فلو كان فاقدا مقدم قدمه لا يمسح على خفه ولو كان عقب القدم موجودا. ترجمه : (۲۲۴) [۷] ساتویں شرط یہ ہے کہ ہاتھ کی چھوٹی تین انگلیوں کے برابر پاؤں کا اگلا حصہ باقی ہو۔ اب اگر کسی کے پاؤں کا اگلا حصہ موجود نہ ہو چاہے پاؤں کی ایڑی ہوتب بھی وہ موزوں پر مسح نہیں کر سکتا۔ تشریح : حدیث میں ہے کہ پاؤں کی انگلیوں سے مسح شروع کرے اور کھینچتے ہوئے پنڈلی تک لے جائے ،اس لئے پاؤں کا اگلا حصہ کم از کم تین انگلیوں کی مقدار موجود ہو تب ہی تو اس پر انگلیاں کھینچ کر مسح کریں گے ، اس لئے اگر ایڑی کا حصہ موجود ہو اور اگلا حصہ تین انگلیوں کی مقدار بھی نہ ہو تو اس پر مسح جائز نہیں ہے۔ وجه : حدیث یہ ہے ۔ عن جابر قال مر رسول الله الا الله برجل يتوضأ ويغسل خفيه فقال بيده كانه دفعه انما امرت بالمسح قال رسول الله الله الله بيده هكذا من اطراف الاصابع الى اصل الساق و خطط بالاصابع. (ابن ماجہ شریف، باب فی مسح اعلی الخف واسفلہ، ص ۷۸ نمبر (۵۵) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ پاؤں کی انگلیوں کی جانب سے کھینچتے ہوئے پنڈلی تک لے گئے ۔
And the seventh: that there remains from the front part of the foot the measure of three fingers from the smallest fingers of the hand. So if one lacks the front part of his foot, he should not wipe over his khuff even if the heel is present. Translation: (224) [7] The seventh condition is that the front part of the foot should be at least three small fingers of the hand in length. Now if a person's front part of the foot is not present, even if the heel is there, he cannot wipe over the khuffs. Explanation: In the hadith, it states that one should start wiping from the toes and draw the hand up to the shin. Therefore, the front part of the foot must be at least three fingers in length so that the fingers can be drawn over it for wiping. Hence, if the heel part is present but the front part is less than three fingers, wiping is not permissible. Evidence: The hadith is from Jabir who said: The Messenger of Allah passed by a man performing wudu and washing his feet. He said with his hand as if pushing him: 'I have only been commanded to wipe.' Then the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) demonstrated with his hand like this, from the tips of the toes to the beginning of the shin, and he drew lines with his fingers. (Ibn Majah, Bab fi mash a'la al-khuff wa asfalah, p. 78, no. 55) This hadith shows that wiping is done from the toes upward.
Source pages p. 169

Commentary
This passage outlines the seventh condition for wiping: the foot must have a front portion of at least three fingers' length (measured by the small fingers of the hand). This is because the act of wiping involves starting from the toes and drawing the hand up the leg. If the toes or the front part of the foot are missing, the wiping cannot be performed correctly. The hadith from Jabir demonstrates the proper method: starting at the tips of the toes and going to the shin. Therefore, without sufficient front part, the wiping is not valid, even if the heel is intact.

Key Terms
مقدم القدم (muqaddam al-qadam): The front part of the foot, including the toes.
عقب القدم ('aqib al-qadam): The heel of the foot.

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) Three small fingers of the hand
D) The entire foot

Key Takeaway
The front part of the foot must be at least three small fingers long; otherwise, wiping over khuffs is invalid.

Duration of Wiping Over Khuffs: Resident vs. Traveler
Ruling on the duration of wiping for resident vs traveler.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the duration of wiping for a resident and a traveler, and determine the validity of wiping in given time scenarios.

Core Idea
Wiping over khuffs is valid only within a fixed period: 24 hours for residents, 72 hours for travelers.

This lesson presents a concise ruling on the time limits for wiping over khuffs. The Hanafi school distinguishes between a resident (muqim) and a traveler (musafir). Knowing these durations is essential for correctly performing wudu while wearing khuffs, especially when traveling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two categories
The ruling distinguishes between a resident (muqim) and a traveler (musafir). Understand who qualifies as each.
A traveler is someone undertaking a journey of approximately 120 km or three days' travel.
2
Memorize the durations
For a resident, the period is one day and night (24 hours). For a traveler, it is three days and nights (72 hours).
The count starts from the moment the khuffs are put on after complete wudu, not from the first wipe.
3
Apply the rule
Given a scenario with a start time and status, calculate the expiry time and determine if a later wipe is within the valid period.
If the period expires, the khuffs must be removed and feet washed for the next wudu.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويمسح المقيم يوما و ليلة والمسافر ثلاثة ايام بلياليها
And the resident wipes for one day and night, and the traveler for three days with their nights.
Source pages p. 169

Commentary
This is a concise statement of the duration for which wiping over khuffs is valid. For a resident (muqim), the period is 24 hours (one day and one night). For a traveler (musafir), it is 72 hours (three days and their nights). This ruling is based on the practice of the Prophet and is well-established in the Hanafi school. The count begins from the first time the khuffs are put on after complete wudu, and once the period expires, the khuffs must be removed and the feet washed for the next wudu. This lesson is a straightforward ruling without additional proof in this text, but it is supported by hadith elsewhere.

Key Terms
مقيم (muqim): Resident; a person who is not traveling, i.e., staying in one place.
مسافر (musafir): Traveler; one who undertakes a journey of at least three days' distance.
يوما و ليلة (yawman wa laylatan): One full day and night, i.e., 24 hours.
ثلاثة ايام بلياليها (thalathat ayyam bi layaliha): Three days and their nights, i.e., 72 hours.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A traveler puts on khuffs at 8 AM on Monday. Until what time is wiping valid?
A) 8 AM on Tuesday
B) 8 AM on Thursday
C) 8 AM on Wednesday
D) 8 AM on Friday

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi ruling: a resident wipes for 24 hours, a traveler for 72 hours, counting from when the khuffs are donned after complete wudu.

Sixth Condition for Wiping over Khuffs: Impermeability
States the sixth condition: khuff must prevent water reaching foot

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the sixth condition for valid wiping over khuffs, identify the proof from the tabi'in, and apply the rule to determine whether wiping is valid on different types of footwear.

Core Idea
Wiping on khuffs requires impermeability: water must not reach the foot.

In this lesson, we examine the sixth condition for the validity of wiping over khuffs: the covering must be thick enough to prevent water from penetrating to the foot. This condition is derived from the practice of the tabi'in and is a key distinction of the Hanafi school. Understanding this rule will help you evaluate the validity of masah on various socks and boots in daily wudu.

Guided Path
1
Identify the condition
State the sixth condition: the khuff must block water from reaching the body.
This is a shart (condition) for validity, not a rukn.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is a statement from Sa'id ibn al-Musayyib and al-Hasan al-Basri: wiping is allowed on thick socks.
This is a qawl of a tabi'i, not a marfu' hadith.
3
Analyze the wajh al-dalalah
The phrase 'idha kana safiqayn' makes thickness a condition; thickness ensures impermeability.
The conditional 'idha' indicates that thickness is a prerequisite.
4
Distinguish from leather
Leather khuffs are naturally impermeable; for socks, thickness must be verified.
Thick socks may substitute if they meet the condition.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(٢٢٣) والسادس منعهما وصول الماء إلى الجسد. عن سعيد بن المسيب والحسن أنهما قالا: يمسح على الجوربين إذا كانا صفيقين. (مصنف ابن أبي شيبة، ٢٢٣ في المسيح على الجوربين، ج أول ص ١٧١ نمبر ١٩٧٦)
(223) And the sixth is that they prevent water from reaching the body. From Sa'id ibn al-Musayyib and al-Hasan: 'Wiping is allowed over socks if they are thick.' (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah, 223, chapter on wiping over socks, vol. 1, p. 171, no. 1976)
Source pages p. 169

Commentary
This is a ruling with proof from a tabi'i. The sixth condition for valid wiping over khuffs (or thick socks) is that they must be impermeable: water from the wiping hand should not seep through to the foot. The proof comes from the statement of Sa'id ibn al-Musayyib and al-Hasan al-Basri, who explicitly permitted wiping over socks only if they are thick (safiqayn). The principle is that since wiping replaces washing the feet, the barrier must be effective. If socks are thin and water passes through, the wiping is ineffective and invalid. The condition applies equally to leather khuffs.

Key Terms
الخف (al-khuff): A leather sock or boot worn over the foot, used as a substitute for washing during wudu.
صفيق (safiq): Thick and dense, such that water cannot pass through easily.

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) The khuff must be worn for at least one day.

Key Takeaway
Wiping over khuffs is only valid if the covering is impermeable; thin socks do not suffice.

Seventh Condition: The Forefoot Must Remain
Ruling with proof from hadith

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi condition regarding the forefoot for masah over khuffs and apply it to scenarios of partial foot amputation.

Core Idea
Masah over khuffs requires the forefoot to exist—without it, wiping cannot conform to the sunnah.

In this lesson, we examine the seventh condition for valid masah over khuffs: the presence of the front part of the foot. The Hanafi school stipulates at least three fingers' width from the toes. If the forefoot is missing, wiping is invalid even if the heel remains. This condition is derived from the Prophet's action and instruction as recorded in the hadith of Jabir.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is wiping over khuffs during wudu. The ruling here is a condition (shart) for its validity. State the condition: the front part of the foot must be present to the extent of three of the smallest fingers of the hand.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is the hadith of Jabir (Ibn Majah no. 55) where the Prophet gestured from the tips of the toes to the shin, indicating the starting point for wiping.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The gesture from 'the tips of the toes' shows that the wiping action begins at the toes. If the toes and the forefoot are absent, the prescribed motion cannot be performed as demonstrated, rendering masah invalid.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
This condition is specific to the Hanafi school. Other schools may allow masah even if the forefoot is missing, as long as the heel covers the foot. However, Hanafis consider the hadith's explicit starting point as decisive.
5
Apply the ruling
Consider a person whose foot is amputated just behind the toes, leaving the ball of the foot and the heel. Measure the remaining forefoot: if it is less than three small-finger widths, masah is invalid and the foot must be washed.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(٢٢٤) والسابع أن يبقى من مقدم القدم قدر ثلاث أصابع من أصغر أصابع اليد. فلو كان فاقدا مقدم قدمه لا يمسح على خفه ولو كان عقب القدم موجودا. عن جابر قال: مر رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم برجل يتوضأ ويغسل خفيه فقال بيده كأنه دفعه: إنما أمرت بالمسح. قال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم بيده هكذا من أطراف الأصابع إلى أصل الساق وخط بالأصابع. (ابن ماجة، باب في مسح أعلى الخف وأسفله، ص 78 نمبر 55)
(224) And the seventh is that there remains from the front of the foot the size of three fingers of the smallest fingers of the hand. If he is lacking the front of his foot, he does not wipe over his khuff even if the heel of the foot is present. From Jabir: The Messenger of Allah صلى الله عليه وسلم passed by a man performing wudu and washing his khuffs, and he gestured with his hand as if pushing him: 'I have only been commanded to wipe.' The Messenger of Allah صلى الله عليه وسلم gestured with his hand like this from the tips of the toes to the shin, and drew lines with his fingers. (Ibn Majah, chapter on wiping the top and bottom of the khuff, p. 78 no. 55)
Source pages p. 169

Commentary
This is a ruling with proof from hadith. The seventh condition is that the front part of the foot (the toes and the area near them) must be present to the extent of three small fingers' width. This is because the prescribed method of wiping starts from the toes and goes up to the shin, as demonstrated by the Prophet's gesture in the hadith of Jabir. If the forefoot is amputated or missing, the wiping motion cannot be performed correctly, so masah is invalid even if the heel remains. This condition ensures the act matches the sunnah. The hadith explicitly instructs wiping from the 'tips of the toes to the shin', emphasizing the starting point.

Key Terms
مقدم القدم (muqaddam al-qadam): The front part of the foot, including the toes and the area up to the metatarsals.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the minimum required length of the forefoot for valid masah over khuffs according to the Hanafi school?
A) The entire foot must be intact.
B) The heel must be present.
C) Three fingers of the smallest hand fingers from the toes.
D) At least one toe.

Key Takeaway
For masah over khuffs, the forefoot must remain at least three small-fingers' length; otherwise, washing the foot is required.

Duration of Wiping for Resident and Traveler
States the time limit for wiping: one day/night for resident, three for traveler

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the time limits for wiping over khuffs for a resident and a traveler, and identify when the duration begins.

Core Idea
The duration of wiping is fixed: 1 day/night for a resident, 3 for a traveler.

Wiping over khuffs is a concession granted to ease purification. But this concession is not unlimited – the Lawgiver has fixed specific time limits based on travel status. In this lesson, we examine the ruling from Hanafi fiqh and the hadith proof that determines these durations.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is being ruled upon? Wiping over khuffs. What is the hukm? A permissible act with a fixed maximum duration. The duration depends on whether one is a muqim (resident) or musafir (traveler).
The act itself is a rukhsah (concession) that replaces washing the feet.
2
Locate the dalil
The author cites the hadith of Aisha (ra) stating that the Prophet (saw) fixed the durations. This hadith is reported in multiple authoritative collections, and its transmission is qati (certain).
The hadith is the primary textual source (dalil naqli) for this ruling.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
How does the hadith prove the ruling? The explicit mention of 'three days with their nights' and 'a day and a night' directly establishes the numerical limits. In Hanafi usul, this explicit statement (nass) is decisive in meaning (dalala zanni, but strong).
The clarity of the numbers leaves no room for interpretation of the maximum.
4
Note the thamarah al-khilaf
Is there any disagreement? The ruling is nearly unanimous (muttafaq alayh) across schools. Some minor ikhtilaf exists on whether the traveler's period includes the night of the third day, but the Hanafi position is clear that the entire 72 hours is counted.
The practical effect (thamarah) is that both resident and traveler know exactly when wiping must stop.
5
Confirm the mufta bihi
The operative ruling for fatwa today: Resident wipes for 24 hours, traveler for 72 hours. The duration begins from the first hadath (breaking of wudu) after wearing the khuffs, not from the time of wearing.
This detail is critical for correct practice.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(٢٢٥) ويمسح المقيم يوما وليلة والمسافر ثلاثة أيام بلياليها. عن عائشة رضي الله عنها قالت: جعل رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم ثلاثة أيام ولياليهن للمسافر ويوما وليلة للمقيم. (مسلم، باب التوقيت في المسح على الخفين، ص 130 نمبر 139/276؛ وأبو داود، باب التوقيت في المسح، ص 23 نمبر 57؛ والنسائي، باب التوقيت في المسح على الخفين للمقيم، ص 18 نمبر 129)
(225) And the resident wipes for a day and a night, and the traveler for three days with their nights. From Aisha (may Allah be pleased with her), she said: 'The Messenger of Allah made it three days with their nights for the traveler, and a day and a night for the resident.' (Muslim, chapter on determining the time for wiping over khuffs, p. 130 no. 139/276; Abu Dawud, chapter on determining the time for wiping, p. 23 no. 57; al-Nasa'i, chapter on determining the time for wiping over khuffs for the resident, p. 18 no. 129)
Source pages p. 169

Commentary
This is a ruling with proof from hadith. The duration for wiping over khuffs differs based on travel status: a resident (muqim) may wipe for one full day and night (24 hours), while a traveler (musafir) may wipe for three days and nights (72 hours). The proof is the well-known hadith from Aisha, which is agreed upon by multiple hadith collections. These time limits begin from the first hadath after wearing the khuffs, not from the time of wearing. The ruling shows that wiping is a concession to ease purification, but it is not unlimited; after the period ends, the khuffs must be removed for the next wudu.

Key Terms
مقيم (muqim): A person who is not traveling (staying in a place with intention to remain).
مسافر (musafir): A person who is traveling a distance that permits qasr (approx. 88 km).

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) One day and one night
C) Until he removes them
D) Only once

Key Takeaway
The duration for wiping over khuffs is fixed by hadith: one day/night for resident, three for a traveler, beginning from the first hadath after wearing.

Start of Wiping Duration from Hadath
Determines that the wiping period begins at the first hadath after wearing

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on when the wiping period begins and explain the hadith proof.

Core Idea
The wiping period starts at the first hadath after wearing khuffs, not at the time of wearing.

Many assume the 24-hour or 72-hour concession for wiping over khuffs starts as soon as you put them on. But the hadith teaches otherwise: the count begins only after you first break your wudu. This lesson clarifies the correct starting point and the evidence behind it.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is the act being ruled upon? It is the duration for wiping over khuffs. The ruling is that the period begins at the time of hadath after wearing, not at the time of wearing.
2
Locate the dalil
The primary proof is the hadith of Abd al-Rahman ibn Abi Bakrah (Ibn Majah no. 556). The key phrase is 'thumma ahdatha wudua'an' (then he commits a hadath of wudu).
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
How does the hadith prove the point? The phrase 'then he commits a hadath' shows that the hadath triggers the concession; the count begins from that event. If it began at wearing, the hadith would not mention the hadath as a condition.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Some early scholars held different views, but the Hanafi position is consistent with the hadith and is relied upon for fatwa.
The athar from al-Shawri also supports counting from hadath.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(٢٢٦) وابتداء المدة من وقت الحدث بعد لبس الخفين. عن عبد الرحمن بن أبي بكرة عن أبيه عن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم أنه رخص للمسافر إذا توضأ ولبس خفيه ثم أحدث وضوءً أن يمسح ثلاثة أيام ولياليهن وللمقيم يوما وليلة. (ابن ماجة، باب ما جاء في التوقيت في المسح للمقيم والمسافر، ج 78 نمبر 556) وعن الشورى في المسح على الخفين قال: فإنك تمسح من الحدث حتى كان العصر، فإنك تمسح عليهما حتى العصر من الغد. (مصنف عبد الرزاق، باب المسح عليهما من الحدث، ج أول ص 164 نمبر 807)
(226) And the beginning of the period is from the time of hadath after wearing the two khuffs. From Abd al-Rahman ibn Abi Bakrah from his father from the Prophet صلى الله عليه وسلم that he granted concession for the traveler that if he performs wudu and wears his two khuffs, then he commits a hadath of wudu, he may wipe for three days with their nights, and for the resident one day and night. (Ibn Majah, chapter on what has come about the timing for wiping for resident and traveler, vol. 78 no. 556) And from al-Shawri regarding wiping over khuffs, he said: 'You may wipe from hadath until before Asr; you may wipe over them until Asr the next day.' (Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq, chapter on wiping over them from hadath, vol. 1 p. 164 no. 807)
Source pages p. 170

Commentary
This is a ruling with proof. The duration for masah does not begin from the moment the khuffs are put on, but from the first time the person becomes in a state of hadath (i.e., breaks wudu) after wearing them. For example, if one puts on khuffs at Fajr but remains in wudu until Zuhr and then breaks wudu, the 24-hour (or 72-hour) period starts at Zuhr, not at Fajr. This is proven by the hadith of Ibn Abi Bakrah which specifies 'thumma ahdatha wudua'an' (then he committed a hadath of wudu), indicating that the hadath triggers the count. The athar from al-Shawri also confirms that the period is counted from the time of hadath. If the period expires, the khuffs must be removed; wiping is no longer valid.

Key Terms
الحدث (al-hadath): The state of ritual impurity that invalidates wudu (e.g., passing wind, urine, etc.)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When does the duration for wiping over khuffs begin?
A) At the moment the khuffs are put on
B) At the first hadath after wearing the khuffs
C) At the first wudu after wearing
D) At the completion of the first full day

Key Takeaway
The wiping period begins at the first hadath after wearing the khuffs, as proven by the hadith and Hanafi ruling.

Effect of Changing Travel Status on Wiping Duration
Ruling on duration change due to travel status shift

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for two scenarios: a resident who travels during the wiping period, and a traveler who becomes a resident after one day of wiping.

Core Idea
Your travel status determines your max wiping period; changing status resets it.

The duration for which you can wipe over your khuffs depends on whether you are a resident (muqim) or a traveler (musafir). But what happens if your status changes mid‑period? This passage from the matn gives the Hanafi rule for two common cases: a resident who travels before finishing his 24‑hour period, and a traveler who becomes a resident after having wiped for a day and a night. Understanding this ruling helps you apply the concession correctly when your situation changes.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios
The passage presents two cases: (1) a resident wipes, then travels before completing his resident period; (2) a traveler wipes, then becomes a resident after having wiped for a day and a night.
These are the only two changes of status addressed; the ruling is specific to each.
2
Apply the rule to each scenario
For the first case: the resident who travels 'completes the traveler's period' – meaning he now has the full 3‑day traveler period from the moment of travel (not restarting). For the second case: if the traveler has already wiped one full day and night when he becomes a resident, he must remove the khuffs immediately; if he has wiped less than that, he completes one full day and night (the resident's maximum).
The key is that the new status defines the total allowable duration, but any time already wiped counts toward that new maximum.
3
Note the consequence
If a traveler becomes a resident after exactly one day of wiping, he cannot extend because the resident period is only 24 hours – which he has already used. If he becomes a resident after, say, 12 hours, he may continue wiping for another 12 hours (to complete 24).
This ruling prevents exceeding the resident's limit while honoring the traveler's concession when applicable.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(٢٢٧) وإن مسح مقيم ثم سافر قبل تمام مدته أتم مدة المسافر. وإن أقام المسافر بعد ما يمسح يوما وليلة نزع وإلا يتم يوما وليلة.
(227) If a resident wipes then travels before completing his period, he completes the traveler's period. And if a traveler settles after he has wiped for a day and a night, he removes [the khuffs]; otherwise he completes a day and a night.
Source pages p. 170

Commentary
This is a ruling statement on the interaction of travel status with wiping duration. Two scenarios are addressed. First: If a resident (muqim) begins wiping and then travels (before his 24-hour period expires), his period is automatically extended to the traveler's 72-hour period. This is because the ruling follows actual status; once he becomes a traveler, he is entitled to the longer concession. The clock resets? No, he continues from where he left off? Actually, the text says 'he completes the traveler's period', meaning he now has 3 days from the start? The commentary explains: he finishes the traveler's period, implying he gets the full traveler's duration from the point of travel? The Urdu tashreeh says: when he starts traveling, he is no longer a resident, so he will complete the traveler's period. The second scenario: If a traveler wipes (e.g., on a long journey) and then becomes a resident (muqim) after having wiped for one day and one night, he must immediately remove his khuffs because his remaining time as a traveler is less than what he would have as a resident? Actually, the ruling: he removes if he has already wiped one day and night; if less than that, he completes one day and night. This is because as a resident, his maximum period is 24 hours. If he already used 24 hours as a traveler, he cannot extend; he must remove. If he used less, he is allowed the full resident period of 24 hours from the time of his hadath? The precise fiqh detail: the change of status does not add time beyond the maximum for the new status.

Key Terms
أتم (atamma): Completes the period; continues wiping for the remaining time up to the full traveler's period.
نزع (naza'a): To remove the khuffs immediately; wiping stops.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Continue wiping until the third day
B) Remove the khuffs immediately
C) Complete one more day and night
D) Start the resident's period from the beginning

Key Takeaway
A resident who travels gets the longer traveler period; a traveler who settles must remove if he has already wiped one full day, else he completes the resident period.

The Obligatory Act of Wiping on Khuffs: Three Fingers on the Front Upper Part
Declares the obligatory method of wiping: three fingers on top of foot

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the minimal obligatory amount of wiping on khuffs and identify the specific area required.

Core Idea
The fard of wiping on khuffs is only three small fingers on the front upper part of the foot.

In this lesson, we examine the minimal obligatory act (fard) of wiping over leather khuffs during wudu. The Hanafi school, based on prophetic practice, defines the indispensable portion as an area equivalent to three small fingers on the front upper part of the foot. Understanding this precise measure is crucial, as anything less does not fulfill the obligation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the hukm
Recognize that the passage states the ruling: wiping is fard (obligatory) when wearing khuffs.
2
Measure the fard
Determine the quantity: the area of three small fingers (the smallest fingers of the hand).
The fingers used are the three smallest of one hand.
3
Locate the area
Identify the specific part of the foot: the front upper part (zahir al-qadam) of each foot.
The front upper part extends from the toes upward, not the sole or heel.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(٢٢٨) مسح کرنا فرض ہے تین انگلی کی مقدار ہاتھ کی چھوٹی انگلیوں سے، ہر ایک پاؤں کے اگلے ظاہری حصہ پر.
(228) Wiping is obligatory: the measure of three fingers from the smallest fingers of the hand on the front upper part of each foot.
Source pages p. 170

Commentary
This is a ruling statement on the obligatory act (fard) of wiping. The minimal fard of masah on khuffs is to wipe an area equivalent to three small fingers (the smallest fingers of the hand) on the front (upper) part of each foot. This is the least amount required to fulfill the command. The commentary does not provide a separate proof here, but the basis is the hadith of Jabir and the general command to wipe. The description specifies the area: the front upper part (zahir al-qadam) from the toes upward. If one wipes less than that, the fard is not fulfilled. This ruling is consistent with the Hanafi view that the fard of wiping is a small amount, not covering the entire khuff.

Key Terms
الفرض (al-fard): The obligatory minimum act that must be performed for the wiping to be valid.
ظاهر القدم (zahir al-qadam): The upper part of the foot, as opposed to the sole.

Key Terms from Source Passage

6 min
Duration of Wiping: Beginning and Effect of Travel
States when wiping duration begins and how travel affects it

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state when the wiping duration begins according to the Hanafi school and apply the rule when a person's travel status changes.

Core Idea
The wiping duration starts from the first hadath after wearing khuffs, not from the moment of wearing.

In this lesson we pinpoint exactly when the clock starts for the concession of wiping over khuffs. The Hanafi school, relying on explicit hadith evidence, holds that the duration begins from the first hadath that occurs after donning the khuffs, not from the wearing itself. We also examine how a change in travel status mid-duration alters the applicable timeframe, a nuance critical for correct practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
State the basic ruling: a resident may wipe for one day and night, a traveler for three days and nights. The act is wiping over khuffs, and the ruling level is wajib.
Wiping is a concession (rukhsah) but wajib when conditions are met.
2
Locate the primary dalil
Find the hadith quoted: the Prophet permitted wiping for the traveler three days and for the resident one day, with the condition 'then he has an event (hadath)' after wearing the khuffs.
The hadith is ahad but accepted as proof for wajib rulings.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The phrase 'ثم أحدث' explicitly ties the start of the duration to the occurrence of hadath after wearing. The ruling is derived from the concession being linked to that event.
The Hanafi school reads this as the literal trigger; the Shafi'i school disagrees.
4
Apply status change rules
If a resident wipes then travels before his duration ends, he completes the traveler's 3-day duration. If a traveler wipes then becomes resident after 1 day/night, he removes khuffs immediately; if before, he completes 1 day/night.
The legal status at the time of the first wipe determines the initial duration, but a change in status overrides it.
5
Note the ikhtilaf with Shafi'i
Imam al-Shafi'i holds that the duration begins from the first wipe, not from the hadath. The practical difference: a person who wears khuffs, has hadath, but delays wiping for an hour loses an hour under the Hanafi view but not under the Shafi'i.
The Hanafi view is mufta bihi in the school.

باب المسح على الخفين
(۲۲۶) وابتداء المدة من وقت الحدث بعد لبس الخفين . (۲۲۷) وان مسح مقيم ثم سافر قبل تمام مدته اتم مدة المسافر. وان اقام المسافر بعد ما يمسح يوما وليلة نزع والا يتم يوما و ليلة .
تشریح : مقیم ایک دن اور ایک رات تک مسح کر سکتا ہے، اور مسافر تین دن تین رات تک مسح کر سکتا ہے۔ وجه : اس حدیث میں ہے۔ قال اتيت عائشة ..... فقال جعل رسول الله علم ثلاثة ايام ولياليهن للمسافر و يوما وليلة للمقيم - (مسلم شریف ، باب التوقیت فی اصلی علی الخفین ، ص ۱۳۰ نمبر ۱۳۹/۲۷۶ را بوداود شریف ، باب التوقیت فی المسح ص ۲۳ نمبر ۵۷ ارنسائی شریف، باب التوقيت في المح على الخفين المقيم ص ۱۸ نمبر ۱۲۹) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ مسافر کے لئے تین دن تین رات اور مقیم کے لئے ایک دن اور ایک رات۔
ترجمه : (۲۲۶) اور سح کی ابتداء مدت موزے پہنے کے بعد حدث سے لی جاوے گی۔ تشریح : موزے پہننے کے بعد جب حدث ہو وہاں سے مسح کی مدت شروع ہوگی ، مثلا فجر کے وقت موزہ پہنا اور ظہر کے وقت حدث ہوا تو ظہر کے وقت سے اگلے دن کے ظہر تک مقیم مسح کر سکتا ہے۔
وجه (۱) اس حدیث میں اسکا ثبوت ہے۔ عن عبد الرحمن بن ابى بكرة عن ابيه عن النبي أنه رخص للمسافر اذا توضأ و لبس خفيه ثم أحدث وضوء اً أن يمسح ثلاثة أيام ولياليهن و للمقيم يوما و ليلة (ابن ماجہ ، باب ما ص تم ، ما جاء في التوقيت في المح للمقيم والمسافر ج ۷۸ نمبر ۵۵۶) اس حدیث میں ہے ثم احدث وضوء ، جسکا مطلب یہ ہے کہ وضو کا حدث ہوا ہو اس وقت سے مسح کی مدت شروع ہوگی ۔ (۲) قول تابعی میں ہے ۔ عن الشورى في المسح على الخفين قال : ...... فانك تمسح من الحدث حتى كان العصر ، فانك تمسح عليهما حتى ا العصر من ا الغد . (مصنف عبدالرزاق ، باب المسح عليهما من الحدث، ج اول ص ۱۶۴ نمبر ۸۰۷) اس اثر میں ہے کہ حدث سے مسح کی مدت شروع ہوگی ، اس سے پہلے نہیں۔
ترجمه : (۲۲۷) اور اگر کسی مقیم نے مسح کیا پھر مسح کی مدت ختم ہونے سے پہلے سفر کیا تو اب وہ سفر کی مدت پوری کرے۔ اور اگر مسافر ایک رات دن مسح کرنے کے بعد مقیم ہو جائے تو فورا موزہ نکال ڈالے۔ اور اگر ایک رات دن سے پہلے مقیم ہوتو ایک رات دن پورا کرلے۔ تشریح : مقیم نے جب سفر شروع کر دیا تو اب وہ مقیم نہیں رہا مسافر ہو گیا اس لئے اب مسافرت کی مدت پوری کرے گا ، اور مسافر ایک دن ایک رات کے بعد مقیم بن گیا تو اب وہ مسافر نہیں رہا اس لئے موزہ کھول دے گا۔
(226) The beginning of the duration is from the time of hadath after wearing the khuffs. (227) And if a resident wipes and then travels before completing his duration, he completes the traveler's duration. And if a traveler after wiping a day and night becomes resident, he removes (the khuffs); if not (i.e., before a day and night), he completes a day and night. Explanation: A resident can wipe for a day and a night, and a traveler for three days and three nights. Evidence: In the hadith: 'I came to Aisha... the Messenger of Allah made it three days and their nights for the traveler and a day and a night for the resident' (Muslim, etc.). Translation of (226): And the beginning of the duration of wiping is taken from the hadath after wearing the khuffs. Explanation: When hadath occurs after wearing the khuffs, the wiping duration begins. For example, if khuffs are worn at Fajr and hadath occurs at Dhuhr, the resident can wipe from Dhuhr until the next day's Dhuhr. Evidence (1): The hadith of Abd al-Rahman ibn Abi Bakra: 'the Prophet allowed the traveler when he performs wudu and wears his khuffs then has an event (hadath) to wipe for three days and nights, and the resident for a day and night' (Ibn Majah). The phrase 'then had wudu' hadath' indicates the duration starts from that hadath. (2) The saying of al-Shu'bi: 'you wipe from the hadath until Asr, then you wipe them until Asr of the next day' (Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq). This indicates the duration begins from the hadath, not before. Translation of (227): And if a resident wipes, then travels before his duration ends, he completes the traveler's duration. And if a traveler after wiping for one day and night becomes resident, he immediately removes (the khuffs); and if he becomes resident before one day and night, he completes one day and night. Explanation: When a resident starts traveling, he is no longer a resident but a traveler, so he completes the traveler's duration. And when a traveler becomes resident after one day and night, he is no longer a traveler, so he removes the khuffs.
Source pages p. 170

Commentary
This passage contains two rulings from the chapter on wiping over khuffs. Ruling 226 establishes that the wiping duration (mudda) begins from the moment of hadath (ritual impurity) that occurs after wearing the khuffs, not from the moment of wearing them. The author provides evidence from hadith, notably the narration of Ibn Majah stating the concession is 'when he performs wudu and wears his khuffs, then has an event (hadath)'. This is supported by the practice of the tabi'i al-Shu'bi. Ruling 227 addresses the effect of a change in residence status. If a resident (muqim) wipes his khuffs and then travels before his one-day-one-night duration ends, he now adopts the traveler's three-day-three-night duration starting from his first wipe. Conversely, if a traveler wipes his khuffs and then becomes resident (muqim) after having already wiped for one day and night, he must immediately remove his khuffs (since his duration as traveler ends). If he becomes resident before completing one day and night, he completes the remainder of the one day and night (i.e., as a resident). The reasoning is that the legal status at the time of wiping determines the applicable duration, but once the status changes, the new ruling applies.

Key Terms
حدث (ḥadath): Ritual impurity that invalidates wudu, such as urination, defecation, wind, or sleep.
مقیم (muqīm): A person who is not traveling (i.e., resident in his hometown or staying less than the distance of safar but not intending to travel).
مسافر (musāfir): A person undertaking a journey of the distance of three days (approx. 77 km) with the intention of travel.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When does the wiping duration for khuffs begin according to the Hanafi school?
A) From the moment the khuffs are put on
B) From the first occurrence of hadath after wearing the khuffs
C) From the first wiping after wudu
D) From the time of the first salah after wearing the khuffs

Key Takeaway
The wiping duration begins from the first hadath after wearing khuffs, and a change in travel status alters the duration accordingly.

Taharah — Purification

The Obligatory Amount and Sunnah Method of Wiping Over Khuffs
Specifies the obligatory amount and sunnah method of wiping over khuffs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the fard amount of wiping over khuffs and describe the sunnah method, citing the primary evidence.

Core Idea
The fard of wiping khuffs is three fingers on the upper front; the sunnah expands from toe to shin with spread fingers.

This lesson clarifies the exact obligation (fard) when wiping over leather socks (khuffs) in wudu. While many know that wiping is permitted, the precise quantity and method are often misunderstood. The Hanafi school, based on the Prophet's demonstration, sets a minimum of three fingers on the upper part, with a recommended sunnah extending to the shin.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is wiping over khuffs as a substitute for washing feet. The ruling is fard (obligatory) with a specific minimum quantity.
Wiping is an alternative to washing when khuffs are worn after complete wudu.
2
Locate the dalil
Primary evidence is the hadith of Jabir where the Prophet demonstrated wiping from toes to shin with three fingers. Also the hadith of Ali emphasizes wiping the upper part.
These ahadith are the basis for the Hanafi position.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The phrase 'khatta bil-asabi' (drew with the fingers) indicates three fingers. The Prophet's demonstration shows the obligatory extent.
The imperative 'amirtu' implies obligation.
4
Distinguish fard from sunnah
The fard is the minimum of three fingers on the upper front of each foot. The sunnah is wiping from toes to shin with spread fingers.
Omitting the sunnah does not invalidate wudu, but omitting the fard does.
5
Cross-madhhab note
Imam al-Shafi'i holds that any part of the khuff suffices; no specific amount. The Hanafi view is based on the explicit demonstration.
Both positions are valid ikhtilaf.
