ترجمه : (۲۲۸) مسح کرنا فرض ہے تین انگلی کی مقدار ہاتھ کی چھوٹی انگلیوں سے، ہر ایک پاؤں کے اگلے ظاہری حصہ پر۔
وفرض المسح قدر ثلاث اصابع من اصغر اصابع اليد على ظاهر مقدّم كل رجل . (۲۲۹) وسـ الاصابع مفرّجة من رؤوس اصابع القدم الى الساق.
سننه
تشریح : ہاتھ کی چھوٹی انگلیوں سے تین انگلی کی مقدار پاؤں کے اگلے حصے پر جواو پر کا حصہ ہے اس پر مسح کرنا فرض ہے۔ وجه : (1) عن جابر قال مر رسول الله الله برجل يتوضأ و يغسل خفيه فقال بيده كانه دفعه انما امرت بالمسح قال رسول الله له بيده هكذا من اطراف الاصابع الى اصل الساق و خطط بالاصابع. (ابن ماجہ شریف ، باب فی مسح اعلی الخف واسفلہ، ص ۷۸ نمبر (۵۵) اس حدیث میں خطط بالا صابع جمع کے صیغے سے پتہ چلا کہ تین انگلیوں کی مقدار مسح کرے۔ (۲) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ پاؤں کے اوپر کے حصے پر سح کرے۔ عن على قال لو كان الدين بالرأى لكان اسفل الخف اولى بالمسح من اعلاه وقد رأيت رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم يمسح على ظاهر خفيه ( ابوداؤد شریف ، باب کیف امسح ،ص ۳۴ نمبر ۱۶۲) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ پاؤں کے اوپر سح کرنا ضروری ہے۔
ترجمه : (۲۲۹) اور مسح کی سنت یہ ہے کہ پاؤں کی انگلیوں کے سرے سے پنڈلی تک ہاتھ کی کھلی ہوئی انگلیوں کو کھینچے۔ تشریح : مسح کرنے کا سنت طریقہ یہ ہے کہ پاؤں کی انگلیوں سے شروع کرے، اور پنڈلی تک کھینچتے جائے ، اس حال میں کہ ہاتھ کی انگلیاں پاؤں پر کھلی ہوئی ہوں۔
وجه : (۱) اس حدیث میں ہے۔ عن جابر قال مر رسول الله له برجل يتوضأ و يغسل خفيه فقال بيده کانه دفعه انما امرت بالمسح قال رسول الله الا الله بيده هكذا من اطراف الاصابع الى اصل الساق و خطط بالاصابع . (ابن ماجہ شریف، باب فی مسح اعلی الخف واسفله، ص ۷۸ نمبر (۵۵) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ پاؤں کی انگلیوں سے پنڈلی تک کھینچا۔ اور خطط بالا صابع سے اس کا بھی اشارہ ہوتا ہے کہ ہاتھ کی انگلیاں کھلی ہوئی تھیں ۔ (۲) عـن الـمـغـيــرة بن شعبة قال : رأيت رسول الله له بال ثم جاء حتى توضأ ثم مسح على خفيه ووضع يده اليمنى على خفيه الايمن و يده اليسرى على خفيه الأيسر ثم مسح أعلاهما مسحة واحدة حتى كأني أنظر الى أصابع رسول الله على الخفين ۔ (سنن للبیھقی ، باب الاقتصار با سح على ظاهر الخفین ، ج اول ص ۴۳۶ نمبر ۱۳۸۵) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ پاؤں کی انگلیوں سے پنڈلی تک کھینچا۔ (۳) عن الشعبي .... قال ارانا كيف المسح فوضع اصابعه على مقدم خفه و فرج بينهما حتى أتى أصل الساق و من اسفل - (مصنف عبدالرزاق، باب المسح علی الخفین ، ج اول ص ۱۷۲ نمبر ۸۵۳) اس اثر میں ہے کہ انگلیاں کھلی رکھی۔
Translation: (228) Wiping is obligatory, with the quantity of three fingers from the smallest fingers of the hand, on the upper front part of each foot. The obligatory wiping is the measure of three fingers from the smallest fingers of the hand on the upper front of each foot. (229) And its sunnah: [wipe with] fingers spread from the tips of the toes to the shin. Explanation: It is obligatory to wipe the upper front part of the foot with three fingers from the small fingers of the hand. Evidence: (1) From Jabir: The Messenger of Allah saw a man performing wudu and washing his khuffs, so he gestured with his hand as if pushing him, saying 'I have only been commanded to wipe.' Then he demonstrated with his hand from the tips of the toes to the root of the shin, drawing his fingers. (Ibn Majah) The phrase 'khatta bil-asabi' (drew with the fingers) indicates the extent of three fingers. (2) This hadith also shows that wiping is on the upper part. From Ali: 'If religion were by opinion, the bottom of the khuff would be more worthy of wiping than the top, but I saw the Messenger of Allah wiping on the upper part of his khuffs.' (Abu Dawud) This proves wiping on top is necessary. Translation: (229) The sunnah of wiping is to draw the spread fingers from the tips of the toes to the shin. Explanation: The sunnah method is to start from the toes and draw up to the shin with the fingers spread over the foot. Evidence: (1) The same Jabir hadith shows wiping from toes to shin, and 'khatta bil-asabi' indicates spread fingers. (2) From al-Mughira ibn Shu'ba: He saw the Prophet place his right hand on his right khuff and left on left, then wipe the upper part once, as if he saw his fingers on the khuffs. (al-Bayhaqi) This shows wiping from toes to shin. (3) From al-Sha'bi: He showed how to wipe, placing his fingers on the front of the khuff with them spread until reaching the root of the shin, and from below. (Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq) This indicates spread fingers.
Source pages p. 170

Commentary
This passage details the obligatory (fard) and sunnah aspects of wiping over khuffs. Ruling 228 establishes that the obligatory wiping is a minimum of three fingers of the hand (from the smallest fingers) on the upper front part of each foot. The author provides evidence from the hadith of Jabir where the Prophet demonstrated wiping from the tips of the toes to the shin, and the phrase 'khatta bil-asabi' (he drew with his fingers) indicates that the wiping was done with three fingers. Additionally, the hadith of Ali emphasizes that wiping is on the upper part (zahir) of the khuff, not the bottom, as some might analogize. Ruling 229 describes the sunnah method: wiping with the fingers spread, starting from the toes and drawing up to the shin. This is supported by multiple narrations, including the practice of the Prophet and the tabi'i al-Sha'bi. The sunnah method completes the act, but the minimum obligation is three fingers on the upper front.

Key Terms
فرض المسح (farḍ al-masḥ): The obligatory component of wiping over khuffs, which is a minimum of three fingers on the upper front of each foot.
سنن المسح (sunan al-masḥ): The recommended method of wiping: starting from toes to shin with fingers spread.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
The fard of wiping khuffs is only three fingers on the upper front; the sunnah extends from toes to shin with spread fingers.

The Fard and Sunnah of Wiping Over Khuff
Fard and sunnah of masah with hadith proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the obligatory amount of masah (three fingers on the upper front) and describe the sunnah method (from toes to shin with spread fingers), citing the primary dalil.

Core Idea
The fard is a small area (three fingers); the sunnah completes the wipe from toes to shin.

Wiping over khuff is a concession in wudu. But what exactly must be wiped to fulfill the obligation? This lesson clarifies the minimum required (fard) and the recommended complete method (sunnah) based on Prophetic practice and explicit commands.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its two components
The passage distinguishes between the fard (obligatory minimum) and the sunnah (recommended method) of masah. Identify each and its specific description.
Fard is quantified by finger length; sunnah is a continuous motion.
2
Locate the dalil for the fard ruling
The author cites the hadith of Jabir. Focus on the phrase 'khatta bi'l-asabi' (drew lines with fingers) to understand how three fingers are derived.
The plural 'asabi' implies at least three in Hanafi usul.
3
Locate the dalil for the sunnah method
Multiple narrations (Jabir, Mughira, al-Sha'bi) show the Prophet wiping from toe to shin with spread fingers. Confirm the direction and finger position.
All narrations agree on the upper surface, not the bottom.
4
Understand the cross-madhhab difference
Note that other schools (e.g., Shafi'i) require wiping the entire upper part. The Hanafi position limits the fard to three fingers, citing the same hadith differently.
This illustrates how the same text yields different fard limits.
5
Apply the ruling in practice
When performing wudu with khuff, wipe at least three fingers on the upper front of each foot. For superior practice, wipe from toe to shin with spread fingers.
The sunnah method does not invalidate if omitted; the fard is the minimum.

وفرض المسح قدر ثلاث اصابع من اصغر اصابع اليد على ظاهر مقدّم كل رجل . (۲۲۹) وسـ الاصابع مفرّجة من رؤوس اصابع القدم الى الساق.

امرت بالمسح قال رسول الله له بيده هكذا من اطراف الاصابع الى اصل الساق و خطط بالاصابع. (ابن ماجہ شریف ، باب فی مسح اعلی الخف واسفلہ، ص ۷۸ نمبر (۵۵) اس حدیث میں خطط بالا صابع جمع کے صیغے سے پتہ چلا کہ تین انگلیوں کی مقدار مسح کرے۔ (۲) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ پاؤں کے اوپر کے حصے پر سح کرے۔ عن على قال لو كان
صلى الله
الدين بالرأى لكان اسفل الخف اولى بالمسح من اعلاه وقد رأيت رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم يمسح على ظاهر خفيه ( ابوداؤد شریف ، باب کیف امسح ،ص ۳۴ نمبر ۱۶۲) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ پاؤں کے اوپر سح کرنا ضروری ہے۔ ترجمه : (۲۲۹) اور مسح کی سنت یہ ہے کہ پاؤں کی انگلیوں کے سرے سے پنڈلی تک ہاتھ کی کھلی ہوئی انگلیوں کو کھینچے۔ تشریح : مسح کرنے کا سنت طریقہ یہ ہے کہ پاؤں کی انگلیوں سے شروع کرے، اور پنڈلی تک کھینچتے جائے ، اس حال میں کہ ہاتھ کی انگلیاں پاؤں پر کھلی ہوئی ہوں۔
وجه : (۱) اس حدیث میں ہے۔ عن جابر قال مر رسول الله له برجل يتوضأ و يغسل خفيه فقال بيده کانه دفعه انما امرت بالمسح قال رسول الله الا الله بيده هكذا من اطراف الاصابع الى اصل الساق و خطط بالاصابع . (ابن ماجہ شریف، باب فی مسح اعلی الخف واسفله، ص ۷۸ نمبر (۵۵) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ پاؤں کی انگلیوں سے پنڈلی تک کھینچا۔ اور خطط بالا صابع سے اس کا بھی اشارہ ہوتا ہے کہ ہاتھ کی انگلیاں کھلی ہوئی تھیں ۔ (۲) عـن الـمـغـيــرة بن
صلى الله
شعبة قال : رأيت رسول الله له بال ثم جاء حتى توضأ ثم مسح على خفيه ووضع يده اليمنى على خفيه الايمن و يده اليسرى على خفيه الأيسر ثم مسح أعلاهما مسحة واحدة حتى كأني أنظر الى أصابع رسول الله على الخفين ۔ (سنن للبیھقی ، باب الاقتصار با سح على ظاهر الخفین ، ج اول ص ۴۳۶ نمبر ۱۳۸۵) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ پاؤں کی انگلیوں سے پنڈلی تک کھینچا۔ (۳) عن الشعبي .... قال ارانا كيف المسح فوضع اصابعه على مقدم خفه و فرج بينهما حتى أتى أصل الساق و من اسفل - (مصنف عبدالرزاق، باب المسح علی الخفین ، ج اول ص ۱۷۲ نمبر ۸۵۳) اس اثر میں ہے کہ انگلیاں کھلی رکھی۔
Chapter on Wiping over Khuff. The obligatory part of wiping is the measure of three fingers from the smallest fingers of the hand on the upper front of each foot. (229) And its sunnah: fingers spread, from the tips of the toes to the shin. Commentary: The fard is to wipe three finger-measure from the smallest fingers of the hand on the front upper part of the foot. Evidence: (1) From Jabir who said: The Messenger of Allah passed by a man performing wudu and washing his khuff, and he said with his hand as if pushing him: 'I have been commanded to wipe.' The Messenger of Allah said with his hand like this, from the tips of the toes to the beginning of the shin, and he drew lines with his fingers. (Ibn Majah) This hadith indicates wiping three fingers. (2) It also shows wiping the upper part. From Ali: 'If religion were by opinion, the bottom of the khuff would be more deserving of wiping than the top; but I saw the Messenger of Allah wiping the upper of his khuff.' (Abu Dawud) Translation (229): The sunnah of wiping is to draw the spread fingers from the tips of the toes to the shin. Commentary: The sunnah method is to start from the toes and draw to the shin with fingers spread. Evidence: (1) Hadith from Jabir... (2) From Mughira ibn Shu'ba: I saw the Messenger of Allah wipe the upper of his khuff with one wipe, his right hand on his right khuff and left hand on his left khuff... (Bayhaqi) (3) From al-Sha'bi... he placed his fingers on the front of his khuff, spread them, and came to the beginning of the shin. (Abd al-Razzaq)
Source pages p. 171

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof on the obligation and sunnah of wiping over khuff (leather socks). It opens by stating the fard (obligatory part): wiping an area equivalent to three small fingers of the hand on the upper front of each foot. The author then explains the sunnah method: starting from the toes to the shin with fingers spread. The commentary cites three hadiths as evidence. The first hadith from Jabir shows the Prophet wiping from toes to shin with spread fingers, and the phrase 'khatta bi'l-asabi' (drew lines with fingers) indicates three fingers. The second from Ali confirms that the top of the khuff is wiped, not the bottom. The third from Mughira describes a complete demonstration. A fourth athar from al-Sha'bi emphasizes spreading fingers. All proofs establish the sunnah method as from toes to shin with spread fingers.

Key Terms
مسح (masah): Wiping wet hands over the khuff as a substitute for washing feet in wudu.
خف (khuff): Leather socks worn over the feet, upon which wiping is permissible.
فرض (fard): Obligatory part of the act, omission invalidates the act.
سنة (sunnah): Recommended practice; omission does not invalidate.
خطط بالاصابع (khatta bi'l-asabi): He drew lines with his fingers, indicating the area and number of fingers.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the obligatory amount of wiping over khuff according to this passage?
A) Wiping the entire upper surface
B) Wiping three small fingers of the hand on the upper front
C) Wiping the bottom of the khuff
D) Wiping from toes to shin once

Key Takeaway
The fard is minimal (three fingers on the upper front); the sunnah completes the wipe from toes to shin with spread fingers.

Taharah — Purification

Nullifiers of Wiping over Khuff
Lists four nullifiers of wiping over khuff with proof

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the four nullifiers of wiping over khuff and apply them to determine when masah is invalidated and what actions are required.

Core Idea
Four things nullify masah over khuff: hadath, removal, water reaching foot, time expiry.

The license to wipe over khuff is a dispensation within wudu, but it can be invalidated by specific events. In this passage, the author enumerates four nullifiers and supports each with evidence from hadith and athar. Understanding these nullifiers is essential for correctly maintaining your wudu while benefiting from the rukhsah of masah.

Guided Path
1
List the four nullifiers
Read the passage and identify the four things that break the wiping: (1) anything that breaks wudu, (2) removing the khuff (entire or most of the foot), (3) water reaching most of the foot, (4) expiry of the time limit.
The first and second are detailed; third and fourth are mentioned briefly.
2
Analyze the first nullifier
Note that any event that nullifies wudu also nullifies masah. The hadith of Safwan ibn Assal exempts only janabah, implying all other hadath break the wiping.
Janabah requires ghusl, so wiping over khuff is not allowed in janabah anyway.
3
Analyze the second nullifier
Removal of the khuff, whether entirely or most of the foot exiting, nullifies masah. Evidence from Mughira hadith: 'malam yakhla' (as long as they do not remove). Athar of Ibrahim: 'If you remove them, wash your feet.'
This nullifier is unique to Hanafis; Shafi'is do not consider removal a nullifier.
4
Distinguish consequences
When masah is nullified, washing the feet is required. If wudu is also broken (e.g., by hadath), full wudu is needed. If only masah is nullified (e.g., removal), only washing the feet suffices.
The passage clarifies that for removal, one does not need to repeat the whole wudu, only wash the feet.

Section on what nullifies wiping of khuff. Four things nullify wiping of khuff: (230) Everything that nullifies wudu, (231) Removing the khuff, even if most of the foot comes out to the shin of the khuff. Four things break the wiping: first, that which is a nullifier of wudu; second, removing the entire khuff or most of the foot coming out to the shin of the khuff; third, water reaching most of one foot according to the Imam's school; fourth, expiry of the time limit of wiping. Translation (230): That which breaks wudu also breaks wiping. Explanation: Things that break wudu also break masah, e.g., breaking wind (hadath) or major impurity (janabah). Evidence: Hadith from Safwan ibn Assal: The Prophet did not order us to remove our khuff for three days and nights except for janabah, but for defecation, urination, and sleep. (Tirmidhi, Nasai) Translation (231): Removal of the khuff, or most of the foot coming out to the shin of the khuff. Explanation: If the entire khuff comes off, wiping is nullified; then one must wash the feet and put on the khuff again. If most of the foot comes out to the shin of the khuff, it is also considered removal, and one should wash the feet and put on the khuff without repeating the whole wudu. Evidence: (1) Hadith from Mughira: We were with the Prophet and he commanded us to wipe for three days for a traveler and one day for a resident as long as they do not take off (the khuff). (2) Effect from Ibrahim: 'If you remove them, wash your feet.' (Abd al-Razzaq) (3) From a companion of the Prophet...
Source pages p. 171

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof on the nullifiers of wiping over khuff. It lists four things: (1) anything that nullifies wudu (e.g., passing wind, urination, sleep), (2) removing the khuff entirely or most of the foot coming out, (3) water reaching most of one foot (according to the madhhab), (4) expiry of the time period of wiping (three days for traveler, one day for resident). The commentary explains each with hadith evidence. For the first nullifier, a hadith from Safwan ibn Assal shows that janabah and other hadath break the wiping. For the second, a hadith from Mughira states the condition 'malam yakhla' (as long as they do not remove), and an athar from Ibrahim al-Nakha'i instructs washing the feet upon removal. The third and fourth nullifiers are mentioned in the Urdu but not fully detailed in the Arabic OCR; they are standard Hanafi rulings.

Key Terms
نقض المسح (naqd al-masah): Things that invalidate the license of wiping over khuff, requiring washing of feet or renewal.
حدث (hadath): Minor impurity that breaks wudu, such as passing wind, urination, sleep.
نزع الخف (naz' al-khuff): Removal of the khuff, either entirely or most of the foot exiting.

Key Takeaway
The four nullifiers of wiping over khuff are hadath, removal (whole or most), water reaching the foot, and expiry of the time limit.

Three Nullifiers of Wiping over Khuffs: Nawaqid al-Mash
Listing of three nullifiers with consequences

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three nullifiers of wiping over khuffs and apply the rule that after any nullifier, only the feet need washing if wudu remains.

Core Idea
Three things break the wipe: wet foot, time's up, or khuff comes off — then wash feet only.

Wiping over khuffs is a valuable concession that eases wudu, but it is not indefinite. This lesson identifies the three events that end the permissibility of wiping and explains what you must do next. Understanding these nullifiers ensures you maintain valid wudu without unnecessary repetition.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three nullifiers
Read the passage and list the three specific events that nullify the state of wiping over khuffs.
The nullifiers are: 1) water reaching most of one foot, 2) expiry of the period, 3) removal of the khuff.
2
Understand the principle behind nullifier 1
Recognize that washing and wiping cannot be combined on the same limb. If most of the foot is wetted, it counts as washing, so wiping is no longer valid.
This applies even if only one foot is affected; the other foot must also be washed.
3
Apply the time limit
Note that the wipe duration is one day for a resident and three days for a traveler. Once the period ends, the wipe becomes invalid.
However, if removing the khuff to wash feet would cause harm from cold, the ruling changes to that of a bandage (jabeerah).
4
Act after nullification
If any nullifier occurs and the original wudu is still valid, then only the feet need to be washed (not the whole wudu). After washing, put the khuffs back on.
This is the key practical outcome: nullification does not break wudu, only the concession of wiping.

Source Text

(۲۳۲) واصابة الماء اكثر احدى القدمين في الخف على الصحيح . (۲۳۳) ومضي المدة ان لم يخف ذهاب رجله من البرد . (۲۳۴) وبعد الثلاثة الاخيرة غسل رجليه فقط (۲۳۵) ولا يجوز الرجل يمسح على خفيه ثم يبدو له فينزعهما قال يغسل قدميه - ن للبیھقی ، باب من خلع خفیه بعد مامسح عليهما ص ۴۳۴، نمبر ۱۳۷۰) اس عمل صحابی میں ہے کہ موزہ کھل جائے تو دونوں قدم کو دھوئے۔
لغت : ساق الخف : موزہ کا جو حصہ پاؤں کی پنڈلی کے پاس رہتا ہے اس کو ساق الخف ، کہتے ہیں۔
ترجمه : (۲۳۲) [۳] ایک قدم کے اکثر حصہ کو پانی پہونچ جائے ہیچ مذہب یہی ہے۔ تشریح : یہ مسئلہ اس اصول پر ہے کہ دھونا اور مسح جمع نہیں کیا جاسکتا۔ اس لئے قدم کا اکثر حصہ بھیگ گیا تو ایک قدم کا غسل ہو گیا ، اس لئے دوسرے قدم کا مسح جمع کرنا درست نہیں ہے اس لئے دوسرے قدم کے موزے کو بھی نکال کر دھونا ہوگا۔ صیح مذہب یہی ہے ترجمه : (۲۳۳) [۴] مسح کی مدت ختم ہو جاوے، اگر ٹھنڈ سے پاؤں کے ضائع ہونے کا اندیشہ نہ ہو۔ تشریح : مسح کی مدت ایک دن یا تین دن ختم ہو جانے سے بھی مسح ٹوٹ جائے گا۔ لیکن اگر پاؤں دھونے سے برف کی وجہ سے پاؤں شل ہو جانے کا خطرہ ہو تو اب اس کا حکم جبیرہ [پٹی ] کا حکم ہو جائے گا کہ جب تک مجبوری رہے گی مسح کرتا رہے گا۔ وجه : عن على بن ابى طالب قال سألت رسول الله علي الله عن الجبائر يكون على الكسير ، كيف يتوضأ صاحبها و كيف يغتسل اذا اجنب ؟ قال يمسحان بالماء عليها في الجنابة و الوضوء ، قلت فان كان في برد يخاف على نفسه اذا اغتسل ؟ قال يمر على جسده ، و قرأ رسول الله الله و لا تقتلوا انفسكم ان الله كان بكم رحيما، ويتيمم اذا خاف (دار قطنی ، باب جواز امسح على الجبائر ص ۲۳۳، نمبر ۸۶۵) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ سردی کا خوف ہو تو جنابت کے لئے بھی جسم کو صرف پونچھ لے، اور اس سے بھی زیادہ خوف ہو تو تیم کر لے۔

(مصنف عبدالرزاق، باب نزع الخفین بعد امسح ، ج اول ص ۲۱۰ نمبر ۸۱۳ ) (۲) عن رجل من اصحاب النبي الله في الرجل يمسح على خفيه ثم يبدو له فينزعهما قال يغسل قدميه (سن للبیھقی ، باب من خلع خفیه بعد مامسح علیهما ص۲۳۴، نمبر۱۳۷۰) اس عمل صحابی میں ہے کہ موزہ کھل جائے تو دونوں قدم کو دھوئے۔
Chapter on what nullifies wiping over the khuff. (232) And the water reaching most of one foot while in the khuff, according to the correct position. (233) And the passing of the period, if he does not fear loss of his foot from the cold. (234) And after the three [nullifiers], washing his feet only. (235) And it is not permissible for a man who wiped over his khuffs then later decides to remove them, he said: wash his feet. (Narrated by al-Bayhaqi...) This is a Companion's action: if the khuff comes off, he should wash both feet. Lexicon: saq al-khuff: the part of the khuff that is near the shin is called saq al-khuff. Translation: (232) Water reaches most of one foot; this is the correct madhhab. Explanation: This ruling is based on the principle that washing and wiping cannot be combined. If most of the foot becomes wet, then that foot is washed, so it is not correct to combine wiping the other foot; therefore he must remove the other khuff and wash it. The correct madhhab is this. Translation: (233) The period of wiping expires, if there is no fear of losing the foot from cold. Explanation: The expiry of the period of one day or three days also nullifies the wipe. But if there is a danger of paralysis from washing in the cold, then the ruling becomes like the ruling of jabeerah (bandage): as long as the necessity remains, he may continue wiping. Evidence: From Ali ibn Abi Talib... (Dar Qutni) In this hadith: if there is fear of cold, then for janabah he only wipes his body, and if more fear, he performs tayammum. Translation: (234) And after these three, simply washing the feet is sufficient. Explanation: The three [nullifiers] are: (1) the khuff comes off, (2) most of the foot gets wet, (3) the period of wiping expires, and if wudu is still present, it is not necessary to repeat the whole wudu; just wash the feet and put on the khuffs. Evidence: (1) From Ibrahim: if you remove them, wash your feet, and this is the position of al-Thawri. (2) From a Companion of the Prophet: regarding a man who wiped over his khuffs then removed them, he said: wash his feet (al-Bayhaqi). This Companion's action indicates that if the khuff comes off, he should wash both feet.
Source pages p. 173

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement from the section on what nullifies the validity of wiping over khuffs during wudu. Three nullifiers are listed: (232) water reaching most of one foot while wearing the khuff; (233) expiry of the period of wiping (one day for resident, three for traveler) provided there is no fear of harm from cold; (234) after any of these three nullifiers, if the wudu is still valid, it is sufficient to wash only the feet and then put the khuffs back on. The passage also includes a related ruling (235) that if a person removes his khuffs after wiping, he must wash his feet. The Urdu commentary explains that wiping and washing cannot be combined, and that the ruling on jabeerah applies if there is fear of cold injury. The hadith evidence from Ali and Companions support the rulings.

Key Terms
خف (khuff): A leather sock or boot that covers the foot and ankle, over which wiping is permitted in place of washing the feet during wudu.
مسح (masah): To wipe a limb or covering with wet hands without flowing water.
نقض المسح (naqd al-mash): Nullification of the state of wiping, after which the original obligation (washing feet) returns.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following nullifies the wipe over khuffs?
A) Water reaching less than half of the foot
B) Expiry of the period for wiping
C) Putting on new khuffs over old ones
D) Wiping over the khuffs twice

Key Takeaway
The three nullifiers are water reaching most of the foot, expiry of the period, and removal of the khuff; after any, if wudu remains, only feet need washing.

Wiping over Bandages: The Obligation of Masah 'ala al-Jabeerah
Ruling on wudu with a bandage (jabeerah).

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling for wiping over a bandage during wudu and identify the condition that makes it obligatory (necessity).

Core Idea
When washing a limb is harmful, wiping over most of the bandage becomes obligatory.

This lesson addresses a common scenario: a person with a wound or fracture who has applied a bandage (jabeerah) and cannot wash the affected limb during wudu. The Hanafi school provides a clear ruling: wipe over most of the bandage with water. This is based on the principle of necessity (darurah) and a hadith from the Prophet ﷺ. Understanding this ruling ensures that one's wudu remains valid even when washing is impossible.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
Recognize when a person has a wound, fracture, or similar condition that requires a bandage (jabeerah) and washing the limb is harmful or impossible.
The bandage can be a cloth, splint, or any covering that prevents water from reaching the skin.
2
State the ruling
The obligatory action is to wipe over most of the bandage with wet hands. This is wajib (obligatory) and a substitute for washing that part.
Wiping less than most is not sufficient; the majority of the bandage must be covered.
3
Understand the basis
The ruling is based on the principle of necessity (darurah) and the hadith of Jabir (may Allah be pleased with him) where the Prophet ﷺ instructed a wounded companion to bandage his wound and wipe over it.
The hadith is cited as evidence, though its chain is ahad and requires careful acceptance.
4
Note the Hanafi emphasis
Hanafi fiqh stresses wiping over most of the bandage, not just the part covering the wound. This ensures the obligation is fulfilled generously.
Some schools allow wiping only over the wound itself, but the Hanafi view is more precautionary.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل : في الجبيرة
(۲۳۶) اذا افتصد او جُرحَ او كُسِر عضوه فسده بخرقة او جبيرة وكان لا يستطيع غسل العضو ولا
ترجمه : (۲۳۶) جب فصد لے، يازخمي ہو جائے ، یا کوئی عضو ٹوٹ جائے پھر اس پر پٹی یا کچیچی باندھ لے اور اس عضو کونہ دھو سکے، نہ اس پر مسح کر سکے تو اس عضو کے اکثر بندھے ہوئے حصہ پر مسح کرنا ضروری ہے۔
تشریح : پچھنا لگوایا جس سے زخمی ہو گیا، یا زخمی ہوگیا، یا کوئی عضوٹوٹ گیا اوراس پر پٹی بانھ لی، یا کینچی باندھ لی اور اس عضو کو دھو نہیں سکتا ہے تو اس پٹی اور کیچی پرمسح کرلے، اور اس کے اکثر پر مسح کر لے تب بھی کافی ہے۔
وجه : (۱) یہاں مجبوری ہے اس لئے اکثر پر مسح کر لینا کافی ہے۔ (۲) اس حدیث میں ثبوت ہے۔ عن جابر قال : خرجنا في سفر .... انـمـا يـكـفـيـه ان يتيمم و يعصر او يعصب ـ شک موسی ـ علی جرحه خرقه ثم يمسح عليها و
Chapter on the bandage. (236) When a person is cupped, or wounded, or a limb is broken, and he bandages it with a cloth or a splint, and he cannot wash the limb nor... Translation: (236) When blood is let, or wounded, or a limb is broken, then he bandages it with a bandage or strip, and he cannot wash that limb nor wipe over it, then it is obligatory to wipe over most of the bandaged part of that limb. Explanation: Cupping caused injury, or wounded, or broke a limb and bandaged it, and cannot wash it, then he wipes over the bandage, and it is sufficient to wipe over most of it. Evidence: (1) Here there is necessity, so wiping over most is sufficient. (2) In this hadith is proof: from Jabir: We went out on a journey... indeed it suffices him to perform tayammum and to squeeze or bandage his wound with a cloth then wipe over it.
Source pages p. 174

Commentary
This passage discusses the ruling on wudu when a bandage (jabeerah) is applied to a wound or fracture. The ruling applies in cases of necessity: if a person has been treated with a bandage and cannot wash the limb (because water would harm it), nor can he wipe directly over the skin because it is covered, then he must wipe over most of the bandage. The Urdu commentary explains that this is due to necessity, and the hadith of Jabir supports this, indicating that when washing is harmful, wiping over the bandage is sufficient. The Hanafi school holds that wiping over most of the bandage fulfills the obligation.

Key Terms
جبيرة (jabeerah): A bandage or splint used to cover a wound or fractured limb.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the required action for wudu when a limb is bandaged and cannot be washed?
A) Wash around the bandage and perform tayammum
B) Wipe over the bandage with water, covering most of it
C) Remove the bandage and wash the wound
D) Wipe over the bandage with dry hands

Key Takeaway
Wiping over most of a bandage (jabeerah) is wajib when washing the limb is harmful; this ensures wudu remains valid without causing harm.

Ruling on Wiping over Headgear and Gloves
Ruling with proof on wiping over headgear and gloves

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on wiping over a turban, cap, face-veil, and gloves, and explain the dalil from hadith that requires wiping the head as well.

Core Idea
Wiping over headgear is not a valid substitute for wiping the head itself.

In the Hanafi school, wiping over leather socks (khuff) is a well-known concession (rukhsah). However, this concession does not extend to other coverings such as turbans, caps, face-veils, or gloves. This lesson examines the ruling and the evidence that wiping over these items alone is insufficient; the underlying body part must also be wiped.

Guided Path
1
Identify the items
The passage explicitly mentions turban (imamah), cap (qalansuwah), face-veil (burqu‘), and gloves (quffazan). Recognize that these are coverings for the head or hands.
Face-veil and gloves are also included, not just head coverings.
2
State the ruling
The ruling is that wiping over these items alone is not permissible (haram or invalid for wudu). The head or hands must be wiped directly.
This is the mufta bihi position in the Hanafi school.
3
Understand the reasoning
The permission for khuff is based on mutawatir hadith and is contrary to analogy (qiyas). For other coverings, no such strong evidence exists. The available ahad hadith are interpreted to show the Prophet wiped his head and then his turban, indicating that wiping the turban alone is insufficient.
The weak analogy to khuff is rejected due to insufficient proof.
4
Examine the hadith proof
The hadith from Anas (Abu Dawood) shows the Prophet inserted his hand under the turban and wiped his forehead. The hadith from Muslim shows he wiped his socks, front of head, and turban. Both indicate combined wiping.
These hadith are cited as evidence that wiping only the covering is not the practice of the Prophet.
5
Note the scholarly consensus
The passage cites Imam Tirmidhi and many scholars from the Companions, Followers, and later imams (Sufyan al-Thawri, Malik, Ibn al-Mubarak, al-Shafi‘i) that wiping the head is required along with the turban.
This ruling is virtually unanimous across schools.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل في الجبيرة
المسح على عمامة و قلنسوة و برقع و قفازين
ترجمه : (۲۳۵) اور نہیں جائز ہے مسح پگڑی پر اورٹوپی پر اور برقعہ اور دستانوں پر۔
تشریح : موزے پر مسح حدیث کی بنا پر خلاف قیاس جائز ہے، اس لئے جب تک حدیث متواتر سے پگڑی، ٹوپی، برقع اور دستانوں پر مسح کرنا ثابت نہ ہو اس کی اجازت نہیں ہوگی۔ اور پگڑی پر مسح کے بارے میں جو حدیث ہے اس کو اس بات پر محمول کیا جائے گا کہ سر پر بھی مسح کیا اور ساتھ ہی پگڑی پر بھی مسح کیا۔
وجه: (ا) عــن انــس بـن مالک قال رأیت رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم يتوضأ وعليه عمامة قطرية فادخل يده من تحت العمامة فمسح مقدم رأسه فلم ينقض العمامة (ابوداؤد شریف ، باب مسح على العمامہ ص ۲۱، نمبر ۱۴۷) (۲) اس حدیث میں بھی ہے ان النبی صلى الله عليه وسلم مسح على الخفين ومقدم رأسه وعلى عمامته. ( مسلم شریف ، باب امسح على الناصية والعمامۃ ، ص۱۳۴ نمبر ۲۷۴) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ بعض سر پر مسح کیا اور پگڑی پر مسح کیا۔ اس لئے صرف پگڑی پر مسح کافی نہیں ہے (۳) امام ترمندی نے فرمایا کہ علماء فرماتے ہیں کہ صرف عمامہ پر مسح کرنا کافی نہیں ہو گا جب تک اس کے ساتھ سر پر بھی مسح نہ کر لے عبارت یہ ہے۔ و قال غیر واحد من اهل العلم من أصحاب النبي و التابعين : لا يمسح على العمامة الا ان يـمـسـح بـرأسه مع العمامة وهو قول سفيان الثورى ومالک بن انس و ابن المبارك، والشافعي. (ترندی شریف ، باب ماجاء فی المسح علی الجوربین والعمامة ص ۲۸، نمبر ۱۰۰)
Chapter on the Splint. Wiping over a turban, cap, face-veil, and gloves. Translation: (235) And it is not permissible to wipe over a turban, cap, face-veil, and gloves. Explanation: Wiping over socks is permissible contrary to analogy due to hadith; therefore, as long as wiping over turban, cap, face-veil, and gloves is not established by mutawatir hadith, it is not allowed. And the hadith about wiping over the turban is interpreted to mean that he wiped over his head and also wiped over his turban. Proof: (1) From Anas ibn Malik, he said: I saw the Messenger of Allah performing wudu while wearing a Qatari turban; he inserted his hand under the turban and wiped the front of his head and did not untie the turban. (2) In this hadith also: The Prophet wiped over his socks, the front of his head, and his turban. This hadith shows that he wiped part of his head and his turban; therefore, wiping only the turban is not sufficient. (3) Imam Tirmidhi said: Many scholars from the Companions and Followers have said: One should not wipe over the turban unless he wipes his head with the turban. That is the saying of Sufyan al-Thawri, Malik ibn Anas, Ibn al-Mubarak, and al-Shafi'i.
Source pages p. 174

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof. It states the Hanafi position that wiping over the turban, cap, face-veil, or gloves is not permissible if done alone without also wiping the underlying body part. The reason is that the exception for wiping over socks (khuff) is established by mutawatir hadith, while for these items the evidence is insufficient. The hadith presented show that the Prophet (peace be upon him) wiped his head and his turban together, implying that wiping the turban alone is not enough. The passage also cites the agreement of many scholars, including those from other schools, that wiping over the turban alone is invalid unless combined with wiping the head.

Key Terms
عمامة (imamah): A turban wrapped around the head
قلنسوة (qalansuwah): A cap or hood worn on the head
برقع (burqu'): A face-veil covering the face
قفازين (quffazan): Gloves covering the hands
المسح (al-mash): Wiping with wet hands over a body part or covering

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) It is sufficient to wipe over the turban alone.
B) One must also wipe the head along with the turban.
C) Wiping over the turban is never allowed.
D) One must undo the turban and wipe the head separately.

Key Takeaway
Wiping over a turban, cap, face-veil, or gloves alone does not fulfill the obligation of washing the underlying body part; the head or hands must be wiped directly.

Ruling on Wiping over a Splint When Unable to Wash
Ruling that wiping over most of the bandage is obligatory when washing is impossible.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on wiping over a splint, identify the conditions that trigger this ruling, and cite the hadith evidence that supports it.

Core Idea
When washing an injured limb is impossible, wiping over most of the bandage is obligatory — necessity overrides the normal requirement of washing.

This lesson addresses a common fiqh scenario: what to do when a bandaged limb cannot be washed due to harm. The Hanafi school provides a clear ruling based on prophetic practice. By the end, you will understand the legal basis and conditions for this concession.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is wiping over a bandage (jabirah or khirqah) on an injured limb. The ruling is wajib (obligatory) when washing or directly wiping the skin is impossible.
Wajib, not fard, because the evidence is zanni al-thubut.
2
Locate the conditions for this ruling
The conditions are: a wound, fracture, or phlebotomy; a bandage applied; and inability to wash or wipe the skin without harm.
These conditions are derived from the text's scenario.
3
Examine the hadith evidence
Two hadiths are cited: Jabir's report about wiping over a cloth on a wound, and Ali's report about the Prophet commanding him to wipe over splints.
Both hadiths are ahad, giving zanni certainty.
4
Understand the wajh al-dalalah
The command to wipe over the covering indicates that it substitutes for washing the wound itself. The hadith states 'it is sufficient for him to wipe over it'.
The implication is clear: the bandage is treated as a proxy for the skin.
5
Note the cross-madhhab difference
Some schools require washing the healthy parts and then wiping over the bandage for the affected area only. The Hanafi school allows wiping over the entire bandaged area without washing the skin underneath.
The practical difference: Hanafi is more lenient in cases of extensive bandaging.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل : في الجبيرة
(۲۳۶) اذا افتصد او جُرحَ او كُسِر عضوه فسده بخرقة او جبيرة وكان لا يستطيع غسل العضو ولا يستطيع مسحه وجب المسح على اكثر ما شدّ به العضو .
ترجمه : (۲۳۶) جب فصد لے، یازخمی ہو جائے ، یا کوئی عضو ٹوٹ جائے پھر اس پر پٹی یا کچیچی باندھ لے اور اس عضو کونہ دھو سکے، نہ اس پر مسح کر سکے تو اس عضو کے اکثر بندھے ہوئے حصہ پر مسح کرنا ضروری ہے۔
تشریح : پچھنا لگوایا جس سے زخمی ہو گیا، یا زخمی ہوگیا، یا کوئی عضوٹوٹ گیا اوراس پر پٹی بانھ لی، یا کینچی باندھ لی اور اس عضو کو دھو نہیں سکتا ہے تو اس پٹی اور کیچی پرمسح کرلے، اور اس کے اکثر پر مسح کر لے تب بھی کافی ہے۔
وجه : (۱) یہاں مجبوری ہے اس لئے اکثر پر مسح کر لینا کافی ہے۔ (۲) اس حدیث میں ثبوت ہے۔ عن جابر قال : خرجنا في سفر .... انـمـا يـكـفـيـه ان يتيمم و يعصر او يعصب ـ شک موسی ـ علی جرحه خرقه ثم يمسح عليها و يغسل سائر جسده ۔ (ابوداؤد شریف، باب فی المجد در تیم ص ۶۱ نمبر ۳۳۶) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ زخم کے اوپر پٹی باندھ کر اس پر سح کرے (۳) عـن عـلـى بن ابی طالب قال : انكسرت احدى زندى فسألت النبي فأمرني أن امسح على الجبائر ( ابن ماجہ شریف، باب امسح علی الجبائر، ص ۹۳ نمبر ۶۵۷ ردار قطنی ، باب جواز امسح علی الجبائر، ص ۲۳۳، نمبر ۸۶۷) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ کچھی پرمسح کرنا جائز ہے۔
لغت : اقتصد : فصد لگوایا، پچھنا لگوایا۔ کسر ٹوٹ گیا۔ خرقہ : کپڑے کا ٹکڑا، شد بخرقہ : پی با ندھی۔ جبیرہ بھیچی ، بانس کی بتی کے ذریعہ سے ٹوٹی ہوئی ہڈی کو باندھتے ہیں۔
Chapter on the Splint. (236) When one undergoes phlebotomy or is wounded or a limb is broken, and then he bandages it with a cloth or splint, and he is unable to wash the limb or wipe it, then it is obligatory to wipe over most of what he tied the limb with. Translation: (236) When one has cupping or is wounded or a limb is broken, then he ties a bandage or splint on it, and he cannot wash that limb or wipe it, then it is necessary to wipe over most of the tied part of the limb. Explanation: He had cupping causing a wound, or was wounded, or a limb broke, and he tied a bandage or splint, and he cannot wash that limb; then he wipes over the bandage or splint, and it is sufficient if he wipes over most of it. Proof: (1) There is necessity, so wiping over most is sufficient. (2) There is evidence in this hadith: from Jabir, he said: We went on a journey... it is sufficient for him to do tayammum and squeeze or bandage—Shu'bah doubted—a cloth over his wound, then wipe over it and wash the rest of his body. (3) From Ali ibn Abi Talib, he said: My forearm broke, so I asked the Prophet, and he commanded me to wipe over the splints. Vocabulary: iftasad: had cupping; kasara: broke; khirqah: piece of cloth; shadda bi-khirqah: tied with cloth; jabirah: splint, made of bamboo sticks to bind broken bones.
Source pages p. 174

Commentary
This passage gives a ruling with proof. It states that if a person has a wound, fracture, or undergoes phlebotomy, and the limb is bandaged, and washing or directly wiping the skin is not possible, then it is obligatory (wajib) to wipe over the bandage or splint, covering most of the area. The Hanafi position is that this substitutes for washing due to necessity. The proof comes from hadith: Jabir's report shows the Prophet allowed wiping over the cloth on a wound, and Ali's report confirms the command to wipe over splints. The commentary also notes that it is sufficient to wipe over most of the bandage, meaning partial coverage is acceptable.

Key Terms
جبيرة (jabirah): A splint or bandage used to support a broken or injured limb
خرقة (khirqah): A piece of cloth used as a bandage

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi ruling, what is the minimum area that must be wiped on the bandage?
A) The entire bandage
B) Most of the bandage
C) A small part of the bandage
D) The wound itself

Key Takeaway
Wiping over most of the splint or bandage suffices when washing the injured limb is not possible, based on the Prophet's command.

Wiping over Exposed Skin between Bandages
Ruling that wiping over visible skin between bandages is sufficient

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on wiping over exposed skin between bandages and explain the proof from the hadith of Ali (ra).

Core Idea
When a bandage leaves skin exposed, wiping over that skin suffices due to necessity.

This lesson addresses a practical scenario: a bandage covering a wound leaves a patch of skin visible. Must that skin be washed during wudu? The Hanafi school, based on a hadith, permits wiping over such exposed skin as a concession due to hardship. We will examine the ruling, its proof, and how it differs from other schools.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Ruling
Determine what act is being ruled upon and the legal status according to the Hanafi school.
The passage states: 'وكفى المسح على ما ظهر من الجسد بين عصابة المفتصد' meaning wiping over the exposed skin is sufficient.
2
Locate the Proof
Find the dalil (evidence) cited in the text. Here it is a hadith narrated by Ali (ra) about wiping over splints.
The hadith is from Dar Qutni, though the text is partially incomplete.
3
Analyze the Wajh al-Dalalah
Understand how the hadith proves the ruling. The Prophet commanded wiping over the splint, indicating the entire area (including exposed skin) is covered by the dispensation.
The key phrase is 'يمسحان بالماء عليها' – wipe over them.
4
Note the Ikhtilaf
Compare with other schools. Some scholars, like Imam al-Shafi'i, require washing the exposed skin if possible, limiting the dispensation to the bandaged area only.
The cross-madhhab status is 'mukhtalaf fih' (disputed).
5
Determine the Mufta Bihi
Identify the operative ruling for fatwa in the Hanafi school. Later Hanafi texts confirm that wiping over exposed skin is sufficient.
Authority weight: fatawa mutakhkhirin.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وكفى المسح على ما ظهر من الجسد بين عصابة المفتصد
ترجمه : (۲۳۷) اور فصد کی پٹی کے ظاہر بدن پر بھی مسح کر لینا کافی ہے۔
تشریح : مثلا چاروں طرف پٹی بندھی ہوئی ہے اور درمیان میں خالی ہے جس سے کھال نظر آ رہی ہے تو درمیان کی کھال کو دھونے کی ضرورت نہیں ہے اس پر بھی مسح کر لینا کافی ہے، کیونکہ مجبوری ہے۔
وجه : عـن عـلـى بن ابى طالب قال سألت رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم عن الجبائر يكون على الكسير ، كيف يتوضأ صاحبها و كيف يغتسل اذا اجنب ؟ قال يمسحان بالماء عليها في الجنابة و الوضوء : ء، ..... و . و قرأ رسول الله ال و لا تقتلوا انفسكم ان الله كان بكم رحيما و يتيمم اذا خاف ۔ ( دار قطنی ، باب جواز امسح علی الجبائر بص ۲۳۳، نمبر ۸۶۵)
And it is sufficient to wipe over what appears of the body between the bandage of the phlebotomist. Translation: (237) And wiping over the apparent body of the phlebotomy bandage is sufficient. Explanation: For example, the bandage is tied all around and there is an empty space in the middle showing the skin; then there is no need to wash the middle skin, wiping over it is sufficient, because of necessity. Proof: From Ali ibn Abi Talib, he said: I asked the Messenger of Allah about the splints on the broken bone: how does the person perform wudu and how does he perform ghusl if he is junub? He said: Wipe over them with water for janabah and wudu... and he recited: 'And do not kill yourselves, indeed Allah is merciful to you' and perform tayammum if afraid.
Source pages p. 175

Commentary
This ruling extends the principle of necessity: if a bandage covers most of the limb but leaves some skin exposed, it is sufficient to wipe over the exposed skin rather than wash it. This is because the condition of necessity (being injured) makes wiping an acceptable substitute. The proof from Ali's hadith shows that the Prophet allowed wiping over the splint itself, and by extension, the exposed skin is treated similarly.

Key Terms
عصابة (isabah): A bandage or binding

In Hanafi fiqh, wiping over exposed skin between bandages is sufficient due to the overarching excuse of injury.

Wiping Over a Splint: No Fixed Duration and No Prior Purity Required
Ruling with expansion on two characteristics of splint wiping

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two key rulings regarding wiping over a splint (jabirah): no fixed time limit and no requirement of prior purity, and explain the rationale based on necessity (darurah) and the practice of the Companions.

Core Idea
Splint wiping is like washing: no fixed period and no prior purity needed – necessity overrides analogy to khuff.

In this lesson, we examine a short but significant passage from our text that clarifies two key aspects of wiping over a splint (jabirah). Unlike wiping over leather socks (khuff), which has a fixed duration and requires prior wudu, the splint ruling follows the principle of washing (ghusl). This is due to the ongoing necessity of the injury. We will unpack the rulings and their proofs.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its analogy
The text compares wiping over splint to washing, not to tayammum or khuff. Recognize that this analogy drives the subsequent rulings: no time limit and no prior purity requirement.
Washing (ghusl) has no fixed time; applying that analogy means splint wiping is indefinite.
2
State the first ruling: no fixed duration
The phrase 'فلا يتوقت بمدة' explicitly negates a time limit. One continues wiping over the splint until the wound heals.
This contrasts with khuff wiping which has a time limit of one day for a resident and three for a traveler.
3
State the second ruling: prior purity not required
The text 'ولا يشترط شد الجبيرة يغسل سائر جسده' indicates that the splint need not be applied in a state of wudu. Wiping over it is valid even if tied while impure.
This is due to necessity; the injury may require the splint to be applied immediately.
4
Understand the rationale: necessity (darurah)
The commentary explains that necessity elevates splint wiping to the level of washing, making the rulings more flexible. The ongoing excuse (udhr) allows continued wiping without time bounds.
Necessity overrides normal restrictions to prevent hardship.
5
Note the evidence from practice
The passage cites the practice of the Companions: they used to tie bandages without wudu and wipe over them, and specifically the action of Umar who continued praying despite blood seeping from a wound.
This demonstrates that the ruling is grounded in prophetic practice (Sunnah) and agreed upon action of the Sahaba.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والمسح كالغسل فلا يتوقت بمدة . ولا يشترط شد الجبيرة يغسل سائر جسده
ترجمه : (۲۳۸) اور مسح دھونے کی طرح ہے۔ اس لئے اس کے لئے کوئی مدت مقرر نہیں ہے۔ اور طہارت پر پٹی باندھنا بھی شرط نہیں۔
تشریح : یہاں مجبوری ہے اس لئے پٹی پر مسح کرنے کو دھونے کے درجے میں رکھا، تیم یا موزے پر مسح کے درجے میں نہیں رکھا ۔ اب اس اصول پر یہاں ۵ مسئلے کو متفرع کر رہے ہیں [1] چونکہ پٹی پر مسح غسل کی طرح ہے اس لئے اس کے لئے کوئی وقت متعین نہیں ہے جب تک زخم ٹھیک نہ ہو پٹی پر مسح کرتار ہے، [۲] اسی طرح وضو کیا ہوا نہ ہو اور پٹی باندھا تب بھی اس پٹی پر مسح کر سکتا ہے۔
وجه : (۱) صحابہ بغیر وضو کے پٹی باندھتے تھے اور اس پر مسح کرتے رہتے تھے۔ (۲) او پر حضرت عمر کا عمل آیا کہ خون رس رہا تھا اور وہ نماز پڑھتے رہتے تھے۔
And wiping is like washing, so it is not limited to a specific time. And it is not a condition that the splint was tied in a state of purity. Translation: (238) And wiping is like washing, therefore there is no fixed duration for it. And tying the splint in a state of purity is also not required. Explanation: Here there is necessity, so wiping over the splint is considered like washing, not like tayammum or wiping over socks. Based on this principle, five issues are derived: [1] Since wiping over the splint is like washing, there is no set time; one continues wiping until the wound heals. [2] Similarly, it is permissible to wipe over the splint even if it was tied without wudu. Proof: (1) The Companions used to tie bandages without wudu and would wipe over them. (2) The practice of Umar is reported: blood was seeping and he continued praying.
Source pages p. 175

Commentary
This passage states two important rulings regarding wiping over a splint (jabirah). First, unlike wiping over socks (khuff) which has a fixed duration (one day for a resident, three for a traveler), wiping over a splint lasts until the injury heals. Second, it is not required that the splint be applied while in a state of wudu; one may tie it while impure and still wipe over it for subsequent wudu or ghusl. The rationale is that necessity dictates this, as the injury creates a continuous excuse. The proof cited is the practice of the Companions and specifically Umar's practice of continuing prayer despite bleeding.

Key Terms
يتوقت بمدة (yatawaqqatu bi-muddah): To be restricted to a fixed period of time
الجبيرة (al-jabirah): Splint or bandage used to set a broken bone or cover a wound
الضرورة (al-darurah): Necessity that permits relaxation of usual rules

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) One day and one night.
B) Three days and three nights.
C) Until the wound heals.
D) Only for a single prayer.

Key Takeaway
Splint wiping is not time-bound and does not require prior purity, based on necessity and the practice of the Companions.

Masah Without Intention: The Hanafi Exception
States ruling on wiping without intention

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that masah over khuff, jabirah, and head does not require niyyah, and distinguish it from acts of purification that do require intention.

Core Idea
Wiping over khuff, bandage, and head is valid without intention – an exception in Hanafi fiqh.

This lesson examines a specific Hanafi ruling: masah (wiping) over certain coverings and the head does not require niyyah (intention). While intention is a pillar in wudu, ghusl, and tayammum, the school eases the requirement for masah. Understanding this exception clarifies the scope of niyyah in purification.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act being ruled
Locate the act of masah in the passage: wiping over the khuff (leather socks), jabirah (splint/bandage), and the head. Note that these are three distinct cases.
The Urdu commentary explicitly contrasts these with tayammum.
2
Extract the ruling on niyyah
The passage states that intention is not required (لا يفتقر إلى النية). Confirm that the ruling applies to all three types of masah mentioned.
In Hanafi usul, 'لا يفتقر' indicates lack of prerequisite.
3
Compare with acts that require niyyah
Recall that wudu, ghusl, and tayammum require niyyah. This ruling carves out an exception. Understand why: masah is a lesser form of purification, and requiring intention would cause hardship, especially in repeated acts.
This is a ruling of ease (rukhsah).
4
Note the madhhab context
The Hanafi position is that intention is not needed for masah. Contrast with the Shafi'i school, which requires niyyah for all purification acts. This difference stems from different usul principles about the role of intention.
Al-Marghinani in al-Hidayah supports this view.
5
Apply the ruling to a practical scenario
Given a person who wipes over their khuff without consciously intending purification, the masah is valid. The act suffices even if the mind is elsewhere.
This highlights the leniency of the Hanafi school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

ترجمه : (۲۴۲) اور موزہ اور پٹی اور سر کے مسح میں نیت کی حاجت نہیں۔
تشریح : جس طرح تیم کرنے میں نیت کی ضرورت ہوتی ہے اس طرح موزے پر مسح ، پٹی پر مسح ، اور سر پر مسح کرنے کے لئے نیت کی ضرورت نہیں ہے ،صرف کرلے تو ادا ہو جائے گا۔

Translation: (242) And for wiping the sock, the bandage, and the head, intention is not needed. Explanation: Just as intention is required in tayammum, similarly for wiping over the sock, the bandage, and the head, intention is not needed; simply performing it suffices.
Source pages p. 177

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling from the matn. It states that wiping (masah) over the khuff (leather socks), jabirah (splint/bandage), and the head does not require niyyah (intention). The Urdu commentary explains that unlike tayammum, where intention is obligatory, these acts of wiping are valid without specific intention. The ruling is based on ease and common practice.

Key Terms
مسح (masah): Wiping a wet hand over a limb or covering.
نية (niyyah): Intention in the heart to perform an act of worship.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Definition of Hayd and Its Conditions
Defines hayd with four conditions and Quranic proof.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi definition of hayd and identify its four conditions from the source text.

Core Idea
Blood from a mature woman, free from illness, pregnancy, and menopause — that is hayd.

This passage from Thamaratun Najah introduces the three types of blood that can exit a woman's private part: hayd (menstruation), nifas (postpartum), and istihadah (chronic bleeding). The author then precisely defines hayd with four conditions that distinguish it from the others. Understanding this definition is essential for every Muslim woman to correctly fulfill her acts of worship, as hayd affects salah, fasting, and other rulings.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three types of blood
The passage first lists hayd, nifas, and istihadah. Recognize that these are the only categories of blood from the female private part.
2
Extract the definition of hayd
Find the sentence defining hayd: blood expelled from a mature woman without illness, pregnancy, or menopause.
3
List the four conditions
The definition includes four conditions: maturity, absence of illness, absence of pregnancy, and not reaching menopause.
4
Apply each condition to examples
Consider a minor girl, a pregnant woman, a woman with chronic illness, and a post-menopausal woman. Their blood is istihadah or nifas, not hayd.
5
Locate the Quranic proof
The passage cites Surah Al-Baqarah 2:222 to establish the legal significance of hayd.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۲۴۳) يخرج من الفرج حيض و نفاس واستحاضة . (۲۴۴) فالحيض دم ينفضه ر[؟] بالغة لا داء ولا حبل ولم تبلغ سن الاياس
ترجمه : (۲۴۳) عورت کی شرمگاہ سے جو خون نکلتا ہے وہ یا حیض ہے یا نفاس ہے یا استحاضہ ہے۔
تشریح : عورت کی شرمگاہ سے جو خون نکلتا ہے ، اس کی تین قسمیں ہیں [1] حیض، [۲] نفاس،[۳] استحاضہ، اور تینوں کے احکام الگ الگ ہیں تفصیل آگے آرہی ہے۔
ترجمه : (۲۴۴) جو خون بالغہ عورت کے رحم سے نکلے بغیر مرض و حمل وسن ایاس کے وہ حیض ہے۔
تشریح : یہاں حیض کی تعریف کر رہے ہیں۔ بالغہ عورت کے رحم سے جو خون نکلے اس کو حیض کہتے ہیں۔ اس عبارت میں ۴ قیدیں ہیں (1) پہلی قید یہ ہے کہ عورت بالغہ ہو، پس اگر نابالغ لڑکی کی شرمگاہ سے خون نکلے وہ حیض نہیں استحاضہ ہے۔ [۲] دوسری قید ہے کہ مرض کے بغیر ہو، کیونکہ مرض کی وجہ سے ہومثلا پر دل کی بیماری ہو تو وہ خون استحاضہ ہے۔[۳] تیسری قید ہے کہ حمل سے نہ ہو، کیونکہ حمل نکلنے کے بعد جو خون آئے وہ نفاس کا خون ہے، حیض کا خون نہیں ہے۔ [۴] چوتھی قید یہ ہے کہ سن ایاس کے بعد نہ ہو، کیونکہ سن ایاس میں خون آئے تو وہ استحاضہ کا خون ہے، حیض کا خون نہیں ہے۔
ضروری نوٹ: حیض کے معنی بہنا ہے۔ شریعت میں ایسی عورت جو نابالغہ نہ ہو، آئسہ نہ ہو، جریان خون کا مرض نہ ہو اور حمل نہ ہو اس کے رحم سے خون نکلے تو اس کو حیض کہتے ہیں۔ اس کی دلیل یہ آیت ہے۔ ویسئلونک عن المحيض قل هو اذى
فاعتزلوا النساء في المحيض ولا تقربوهن حتى يطهرن (آیت ۲۲۲سورة البقرة ٢)
(243) From the private part comes out hayd, nifas, and istihadah. (244) So hayd is blood that the [؟] expels from a mature woman, without illness, pregnancy, and not having reached the age of menopause. Translation: (243) The blood that comes out of a woman's private part is either hayd, nifas, or istihadah. Explanation: The blood that comes out of a woman's private part has three types: 1) hayd, 2) nifas, 3) istihadah. Their rulings are separate, details to come. Translation: (244) The blood that comes out of the womb of a mature woman without illness, pregnancy, and age of menopause is hayd. Explanation: Here they are defining hayd. Blood that comes from the womb of a mature woman is called hayd. This phrase has four conditions: 1) The woman is mature; if a minor girl's private part bleeds, it is istihadah. 2) Without illness; if due to illness, e.g., heart disease, it is istihadah. 3) Not from pregnancy; blood after miscarriage is nifas. 4) Not after age of menopause; blood at menopause is istihadah. Essential note: Hayd means flowing. In Shariah, for a woman who is not a minor, not menopausal, not suffering from chronic bleeding, and not pregnant, if blood comes from her womb, it is called hayd. Its evidence is this verse: 'And they ask you about menstruation. Say: It is harm, so keep away from women during menstruation and do not approach them until they are pure.' (Surah Al-Baqarah 2:222)
Source pages p. 177

Commentary
This passage defines the three types of blood from the female private part: hayd (menstruation), nifas (postpartum), and istihadah (chronic/non-menstrual). The author then defines hayd specifically with four conditions: the woman must be mature (balighah), not ill, not pregnant, and not past menopause. The Urdu commentary expands on each condition. The proof is Surah Al-Baqarah 2:222, which establishes the ruling of withdrawal during hayd.

Key Terms
حيض (hayd): Blood from the womb of a mature woman not due to illness, pregnancy, or old age.
نفاس (nifas): Blood that comes out after childbirth.
استحاضة (istihadah): Chronic or irregular bleeding not fitting the description of hayd or nifas.
سن الياس (sinn al-i'yas): The age of menopause, after which blood is not considered hayd.

D) The woman must not be ill

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi definition of hayd is precise: blood from a mature woman, free from illness, pregnancy, and menopause, distinguishing it from nifas and istihadah.

Duration of Menstruation (Hayd): 3 to 10 Days
States minimum, average, and maximum days of menstruation with hadith proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the minimum, average, and maximum durations of hayd according to the Hanafi school and identify the hadith evidence that establishes these limits.

Core Idea
Hayd is at least three days and at most ten; any deviation is istihadah.

Menstruation (hayd) is a natural state that affects many rulings in taharah, such as salah, fasting, and marital relations. The Hanafi school relies on clear prophetic hadith to define its duration. In this lesson, you will learn the precise limits – three days minimum, five average, ten maximum – and the evidence that distinguishes normal menstruation from irregular bleeding (istihadah).

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi ruling on durations
Memorize the three key numbers: minimum 3 days, average 5, maximum 10. Note that blood outside this range is istihadah.
These limits apply to both a virgin and a woman past menopause.
2
Identify the evidence (dalil)
The author cites two hadith from Darqutni (nos. 834 and 836). Read the Arabic carefully; the key phrases are 'la yakun al-hayd aqall min thalathati ayyam' (no hayd less than three days) and 'wa la akthar min 'asharati ayyam' (nor more than ten days).
These hadith are ahad (single-narrator), but are accepted as proof in Hanafi fiqh.
3
Analyse how the hadith proves the ruling (wajh al-dalalah)
The explicit negation ('la yakun...') establishes a definitive prohibition of considering less than three or more than ten as hayd. This directly yields the ruling: hayd must be between 3–10 days.
The hadith also describes the quality of hayd blood (black, thick) vs. istihadah (yellow, thin), which is an additional diagnostic sign.
4
Note the cross-madhhab difference
The Shafi'i school holds the minimum is 24 hours and maximum is 15 days. Compare their evidence to the Hanafi position.
This difference affects practical rulings; e.g., a woman bleeding 2 days is in hayd for Shafi'i but istihadah for Hanafi.
5
Apply the ruling to a scenario
Given a woman who bleeds for 8 days – this is within the Hanafi limits, so she is in hayd. If she bleeds for 12 days, the last 2 days become istihadah and she must resume prayers.
The ruling also affects making up missed prayers (qada) after the habit is established.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۲۴۵). وأقل الحيض ثلاثة ايام واوسطه خمسة واكثره عشرة.
ترجمه : (۲۴۵) اور حیض کی اقل مدت تین دن اور اوسط پانچ ، اکثر دس روز ہے۔
تشریح : تین دن سے کم خون آئے تو وہ استحاضہ ہے ، اسی طرح دس دن سے زیادہ خون آئے تو وہ بھی استحاضہ کا خون ہے۔
وجه : (۱) حدیث یہ ہے۔ عن ابی امامة الباهلی قال قال رسول الله الا الله لا يكون الحيض للجارية والثيب الذي قد ايئست من الحيض اقل من ثلاثة ايام ولا اكثر من عشرة ايام فاذا رأت الدم فوق عشرة ايام فهى مستحاضة فمازاد على ايام اقرائها قضت و دم الحيض اسود خائر تعلوه حمرة ودم المستحاضة اصفر رقیق (دارقطنی نمبر ۸۳۴) (۲) عن واثلة بن الأسقع قال قال رسول الله الله الله اقبل الحيض ثلاثة ايام و اكثره عشرة ايسام - ( دار قطنی ، کتاب الحیض ، ج اول بی ۲۲۵ نمبر ۸۳۶) دار قطنی میں اس قسم کی کئی احادیث ہیں جن سے معلوم ہوتا ہے کہ کم سے کم مدت تین دن ہے اور زیادہ سے زیادہ مدت دس دن ہیں۔ اور اس سے کم یا زیادہ ہو تو وہ استحاضہ ہے۔
(245) And the minimum of hayd is three days, its average is five, and its maximum is ten. Translation: (245) The minimum duration of hayd is three days, average five, maximum ten days. Explanation: If blood comes less than three days, it is istihadah; similarly if more than ten days, it is also istihadah. Evidence: (1) Hadith from Abu Umamah al-Bahili: The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said, 'Indeed, there is no hayd for a virgin or a woman who has reached menopause less than three days nor more than ten days. So if she sees blood beyond ten days, she is mustahadah. Then whatever exceeds her usual days, she makes up (prayers). And the blood of hayd is black, thick, with a red tint, while the blood of istihadah is yellow, thin.' (Darqutni no. 834) (2) From Wathilah ibn al-Asqa': The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said, 'The minimum of hayd is three days, and its maximum is ten days.' (Darqutni, Kitab al-Hayd, vol. 1, p. 225, no. 836) There are several hadith in Darqutni indicating that the minimum is three days and maximum ten, and less or more is istihadah.
Source pages p. 178

Commentary
This passage states the durations of hayd: minimum 3 days, average 5, maximum 10. The Urdu commentary adds that blood less than 3 or more than 10 is istihadah. Two hadith from Darqutni support these limits. The first hadith describes characteristics of hayd blood (black, thick) versus istihadah (yellow, thin). These durations are used to distinguish between normal menstruation and irregular bleeding, affecting rulings on salah, fasting, and marital relations.

Key Terms
اقل الحيض (aqall al-hayd): The minimum number of days for menstruation, which is three days.
اكثر الحيض (akthar al-hayd): The maximum number of days for menstruation, which is ten days.
استحاضة (istihadah): Irregular vaginal bleeding that is not menstruation, occurring outside the normal hayd limits or with different characteristics.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the minimum duration for hayd according to the Hanafi school?
A) One day
B) Two days
C) Three days
D) Five days

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school defines hayd as a period between 3 and 10 days, based on prophetic hadith; blood outside this range is istihadah.

Definition and Duration of Nifas
Defines nifas and its maximum duration (40 days) with hadith proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi definition of nifas, its maximum duration of 40 days, and identify the key hadith proofs.

Core Idea
Nifas ends as soon as bleeding stops, with a maximum of 40 days — no fixed minimum.

In this lesson, we examine the Hanafi ruling on nifas (postpartum bleeding). The text defines nifas, sets a maximum of 40 days, and establishes that there is no minimum. Three hadith are cited to support these points. Understanding this ruling is essential for women to know when they are ritually pure after childbirth.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Nifas is the blood after childbirth (full-term or miscarriage). The ruling: maximum 40 days, no minimum.
This is a definition (hukm wad'i) that determines legal purity.
2
Locate the dalil
Three hadith are cited: (1) Umm Salamah on the 40-day custom, (2) Abdullah ibn Amr on waiting 40 nights, (3) Mu'adh ibn Jabal on purity after 7 days.
All three have zanni thubut (single transmission).
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The first hadith establishes the maximum by practice; the second explicitly states the 40-day limit; the third shows that earlier purity is valid, proving no minimum.
The Prophet's silence on the practice indicates approval (taqrir).
4
Note the ikhtilaf
The Shafi'i school holds the maximum is 60 days, citing different narrations. The Hanafi school relies on the 40-day hadith as stronger.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf in the fiqh of taharah.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The relied-upon Hanafi position: maximum 40 days, no minimum. A woman is pure as soon as bleeding stops.
If bleeding exceeds 40 days, she becomes mustahadah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۲۴۶) والنفاس هو الدم الخارج عقب الولادة واكثره اربعون يوما ولا حد لاقلـه
ترجمه: (۲۴۶) اور جوخون ولادت کے بعد خارج ہو وہ نفاس ہے۔ اس کی اکثر مدت چالیس روز ہے اور اقل کی کوئی حد نہیں
تشریح : مکمل بچے کی ولادت ہو یا سقط یعنی ناقص بچے کی ولادت ہو دونوں صورتوں میں ولادت کے بعد جو خون ہوگا وہ نفاس کا خون ہے۔ اس کی زیادہ سے زیادہ مدت چالیس روز ہے، اور کم سے کم مدت کی حد نہیں ہے۔
وجه : (۱) عن ام سلمة قالت كانت النفساء تجلس على عهد رسول الله علم اربعين يوما (ترندی شریف، باب ماجاء فی کم تمکث النفساء ،ص ۱۳۵، نمبر ۱۳۹ ابوداؤد شریف، باب ماجاء فی وقت النفساء ،ص ۴۹، نمبر ۳۱۲) ان احادیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ نفاس کی زیادہ سے زیادہ مدت چالیس دن ہے (۲) عن عبد الله بن عمرو قال : قال رسول الله الا الله : تنتظر النفساء أربعين ليلة ، فان رأت الطهر قبل ذالک فهى طاهر ، و ان جاوزت الاربعين فهي بمنزلة المستحاضة ، تغتسل و تصلى ، فان غلبها الدم توضأت لكل صلوة - ( دارقطنی ، باب الحیض ، ج اول ص ۲۲۸ نمبر ۸۴۷) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ چالیس دن سے پہلے بھی ھر دیکھے تو وہ پاک شمار کی جائے گی (۳) حدیث میں ہے ۔ عن معاذ بن جبل عن النبي الله قال : اذا مضى للنفساء سبع ثم رأت الطهر فلتغتسل و لتصل (سنن ، باب النفاس، ج اول، ص ۵۰۵ نمبر ۱۶۱۷) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ سات روز کے بعد پاک ہو جائے تو بھی پاک سمجھی جائے گی ، اس سے معلوم ہوا کہ کم سے کم کی کوئی حد نہیں ہے۔
(246) And nifas is the blood that comes out after childbirth. Its maximum is forty days, and there is no limit for its minimum. Translation: (246) And the blood that comes out after childbirth is nifas. Its maximum duration is forty days, and there is no limit for its minimum. Explanation: Whether it is a full-term birth or a miscarriage, the blood after birth is nifas. Its maximum duration is forty days, and there is no fixed minimum. Evidence: (1) From Umm Salamah: The women in the time of the Messenger of Allah used to sit (in waiting) for forty days after childbirth. (Tirmidhi, Bab ma ja'a fi kam tamkuth al-nufasa', p. 135, no. 139; Abu Dawud, Bab ma ja'a fi waqt al-nufasa', p. 49, no. 312) These hadith show that the maximum is forty days. (2) From Abdullah ibn Amr: The Messenger of Allah said, 'The woman in nifas waits forty nights. If she sees purity before that, she is pure. If she exceeds forty, she is like a mustahadah; she performs ghusl and prays, and if bleeding overwhelms her, she performs wudu for each prayer.' (Darqutni, Bab al-Hayd, vol. 1, p. 228, no. 847) This hadith indicates that if she becomes pure before forty days, she is considered pure. (3) Hadith from Mu'adh ibn Jabal from the Prophet: 'When seven days have passed for the woman in nifas and then she sees purity, let her perform ghusl and pray.' (Sunan, Bab al-Nifas, vol. 1, p. 505, no. 1617) This hadith shows that even after seven days, if she becomes pure, she is considered pure, indicating no fixed minimum.
Source pages p. 178

Commentary
This passage defines nifas as the blood following childbirth, whether full-term or miscarriage. The maximum duration is forty days, and there is no minimum. The Urdu commentary explains these points. Three hadith are cited: the first establishes the forty-day custom, the second confirms that purity before forty days is valid, and the third shows that even seven days can be the end of nifas. Thus, a woman becomes pure and must pray as soon as bleeding stops, even if before forty days.

Key Terms
نفاس (nifas): Postpartum blood following childbirth, full-term or miscarriage.
سقط (suqt): Miscarriage; delivery of an incomplete fetus.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) 30 days
B) 40 days
C) 50 days
D) 60 days

Key Takeaway
Nifas has a maximum of 40 days and no minimum; a woman becomes pure as soon as bleeding stops.

Defining Istihadah: Blood Beyond the Limits of Hayd and Nifas
Defines istihadah by durational limits

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define istihadah according to the Hanafi school by stating the durational limits that distinguish it from hayd and nifas.

Core Idea
Blood outside the limits of hayd and nifas is istihadah, not menstrual or postpartum.

The text introduces the definition of istihadah (chronic irregular bleeding) by specifying which blood is not considered menstrual or postpartum. This is a critical foundational ruling, as it determines when a woman must continue her prayers and fasting despite bleeding. Mastery of these limits is essential for correct application of taharah rules.

Guided Path
1
Identify the topic
The passage defines a type of bleeding called istihadah. Recognize that this is not a ruling on an act but a classification of blood.
Istihadah is distinct from hayd and nifas.
2
Extract the numeric limits
Note the three thresholds: hayd minimum 3 days, hayd maximum 10 days, nifas maximum 40 days. These are from the Hanafi school.
Any blood less than 3 days or more than 10 days (or more than 40 for nifas) is outside the normal categories.
3
Apply the definition
Determine the type of blood in a given scenario by comparing its duration to these limits. If it falls outside, it is istihadah.
The exact timing of the start of bleeding matters.
4
Understand the consequence
Istihadah does not prevent prayer, fasting, or marital relations. The woman is considered in a state of ritual purity for acts of worship.
This contrasts with hayd and nifas where prayer is prohibited.

Source Text

Source pages p. 178

This passage begins the definition of istihadah (chronic/irregular bleeding). It describes blood that falls outside the normal limits of hayd (less than 3 days or more than 10) and nifas (more than 40 days). The passage is incomplete but establishes the parameters for istihadah. The ruling is that such blood is not considered menstrual or postpartum, and hence the woman is required to pray and fast, etc.

Key Terms
استحاضة (istihadah): Irregular bleeding that is not hayd or nifas, defined by being less than 3 days or more than 10 for hayd, or more than 40 for nifas.

Minimum, Average, and Maximum Duration of Menstruation
Defines the durations of menstruation with hadith proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi durations of menstruation (minimum, average, maximum) and identify which bleeding qualifies as hayd vs. istihadah based on the hadith proofs.

Core Idea
Menstruation in the Hanafi school is defined as bleeding between 3 and 10 days; outside this range it is istihadah.

This passage establishes the Hanafi definition of menstruation (hayd) by specifying its minimum, average, and maximum durations. Understanding these limits is essential for distinguishing menstrual blood from irregular bleeding (istihadah), which has different legal consequences. The proof is drawn from two hadith narrated by Abu Umamah and Wathilah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Ruling
State the three durations given: minimum 3 days, average 5 days, maximum 10 days.
These are the key numbers to memorize.
2
Locate the Dalil
The proof is two hadith from al-Daraqutni. One is from Abu Umamah, the other from Wathilah.
The hadith are ahad (single-narrator) but accepted in Hanafi fiqh.
3
Analyze the Dalil Text
Both hadith explicitly negate menstruation below 3 and above 10 days. The Abu Umamah version adds: 'When she sees blood beyond ten days, she is mustahadah.'
The explicit negation establishes the limits.
4
Apply the Ruling
Bleeding less than 3 days or more than 10 days is istihadah. Within 3-10 days is hayd.
Istihadah does not prevent prayer or fasting.
5
Note Additional Details
The hadith also describes blood characteristics: menstrual blood is black and thick; istihadah blood is yellow and thin.
Characteristics are secondary; duration is the primary criterion.

This passage is a ruling with proof. It states the Hanafi position on the duration of menstruation: the minimum is three days, the average is five, and the maximum is ten days. Blood less than three days or more than ten is istihadah (irregular bleeding), not menstruation. The proofs are two hadith: one from Abu Umamah and one from Wathilah. This distinction is practically important for women who experience bleeding.

Key Terms
الحيض (al-hayd): Blood that exits from the womb within the normal menstrual duration (3-10 days).
الاستحاضة (al-istihadah): Irregular bleeding that is not menstrual, either less than 3 days or more than 10.
