Definition and Maximum Duration of Postpartum Bleeding (Nifas)
Defines nifas and states its maximum duration

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define nifas, state its maximum duration according to the Hanafi school, and cite the primary hadith evidence.

Core Idea
Postpartum bleeding (nifas) has a maximum of 40 days but no minimum – purity can occur earlier.

This lesson establishes the Hanafi ruling on nifas, the blood that follows childbirth. Unlike menstruation, nifas has a defined upper limit but no fixed lower limit. We will examine the key hadith evidence that supports this position and clarify the distinction between nifas and istihadah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the definition of nifas
The text defines nifas as the blood that exits after childbirth. Note that this includes blood following a miscarriage.
The definition is crucial for distinguishing nifas from other types of uterine bleeding.
2
State the maximum duration
According to the Hanafi school, the maximum duration of postpartum bleeding is forty days. This is derived from explicit hadith.
The maximum is a fixed upper limit; bleeding beyond this becomes istihadah.
3
Analyze the primary evidence
The hadith of Umm Salamah and Abdullah ibn Amr explicitly state that a woman experiencing nifas waits forty days (or nights). The phrase 'tantaẓiru arbaʿīna laylah' establishes the maximum.
These ahadith are of the category Sunnah ahad with zanni thubut and dalala, yet they are relied upon in the Hanafi school.
4
Understand the absence of a minimum
The hadith of Muadh ibn Jabal indicates that if a woman sees purity after seven days, she may perform ghusl and pray. This proves that nifas can end before forty days and has no minimum duration.
This ruling gives flexibility and avoids unnecessary hardship.
5
Distinguish nifas from istihadah
If bleeding continues beyond forty days, it ceases to be nifas and is considered istihadah (chronic uterine bleeding). The woman then follows the rules for istihadah: making wudu for each prayer if bleeding is continuous.
This distinction is essential for ritual purity and prayer obligations.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(٢٤٦) والنفاس هو الدم الخارج عقب الولادة وأكثره أربعون يوما ولا حد لأقله. عن أم سلمة قالت كانت النفساء تجلس على عهد رسول الله ﷺ أربعين يوما. (الترمذي، باب ما جاء في كم تمكث النفساء، ص135 رقم139 وأبو داود، باب ما جاء في وقت النفساء، ص49 رقم312) عن عبد الله بن عمرو قال قال رسول الله ﷺ تنتظر النفساء أربعين ليلة، فإن رأت الطهر قبل ذلك فهي طاهر، وإن جاوزت الأربعين فهي بمنزلة المستحاضة، تغتسل وتصلي، وإن غلبها الدم توضأت لكل صلاة. (الدارقطني، باب الحيض، ج1 ص228 رقم847) عن معاذ بن جبل عن النبي ﷺ قال إذا مضى للنفساء سبع ثم رأت الطهر فلتغتسل ولتصل. (السنن، باب النفاس، ج1 ص505 رقم1617)
(246) Postpartum bleeding (nifas) is the blood that exits after childbirth. Its maximum is forty days, and there is no limit for its minimum. From Umm Salamah: 'Women experiencing nifas would sit (wait) forty days during the time of the Messenger of Allah ﷺ.' (Tirmidhi, Abu Dawud) From Abdullah ibn Amr: the Messenger of Allah ﷺ said: 'A woman experiencing nifas waits forty nights. If she sees purity before that, she is pure. If she exceeds forty, she is like a mustahadah; she bathes and prays, and if blood overwhelms her, she makes wudu for each prayer.' (al-Daraqutni) From Muadh ibn Jabal from the Prophet ﷺ: 'When seven days have passed for a woman in nifas and she then sees purity, let her bathe and pray.' (Sunan)
Source pages p. 178

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof on postpartum bleeding (nifas). Nifas is defined as blood that exits after childbirth, whether full term or miscarriage. Its maximum duration is forty days; there is no minimum—she may become pure before forty days, even after seven days as the hadith from Muadh indicates. The proofs are three hadith: from Umm Salamah shows the practice of waiting forty days; from Abdullah ibn Amr explicitly states the forty-day limit and the ruling if exceeded (she becomes mustahadah); and from Muadh shows that purity can occur after seven days, establishing no set minimum. The Hanafi school relies on these hadith to set the maximum at forty days.

Key Terms
النفاس (an-nifas): Blood that exits after childbirth (including miscarriage).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Defining Istihadah: Duration and Proofs
Defines istihadah with temporal limits and proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define istihadah according to the Hanafi school, state its temporal boundaries, and cite the hadith evidence for each boundary.

Core Idea
Istihadah is blood outside the 3-10 day hayd range or beyond 40 days nifas, as proven by authentic hadith.

This lesson establishes the Hanafi definition of istihadah (irregular bleeding) by clarifying when bleeding ceases to be menstrual or postpartum. The passage provides textual proofs from the Prophet ﷺ that set clear temporal boundaries, distinguishing istihadah as a distinct legal category with its own rulings.

Guided Path
1
Identify the definition and boundaries
Read the definition carefully: Istihadah is blood that is less than 3 days or more than 10 days in menstruation, or more than 40 days in postpartum bleeding. Note the three thresholds.
The definition sets the outer limits of normal hayd and nifas.
2
Locate the textual proofs for each boundary
Identify which hadith supports each part: the 3-10 day hayd range from Wathilah ibn al-Asqa', the 40-day nifas limit from Abdullah ibn Amr, and the general principle from Fatimah's hadith that istihadah blood is from a vein.
Each hadith is from al-Daraqutni or al-Bukhari.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah (legal implication)
Explain how each hadith proves the definition: e.g., the explicit statement in Fatimah's hadith that the blood is 'not menstruation' and the command to pray indicates it is istihadah. The other hadith set the numerical limits.
The evidence is direct and clear (zahir al-dalalah).
4
Note cross-madhhab differences
While the Hanafi school firmly holds these limits, other schools may differ on the minimum duration of hayd or the maximum. Recognize that the definition is accepted by most but details vary.
The ikhtilaf is legitimate and based on different interpretations of evidence.
5
Apply the definition
Practice by categorizing given durations: e.g., 2 days = istihadah, 8 days = hayd, 15 days = istihadah (since exceeds 10). This leads to different rulings on prayer and fasting.
The mustahadah prays and fasts; the menstruating woman does not.

(247) Istihadah is blood that is less than three days or exceeds ten days in menstruation, and exceeds forty days in postpartum bleeding. Source pages p. 179

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof defining istihadah. Istihadah is blood that falls outside the normal durations: in menstruation, less than 3 days or more than 10; in postpartum bleeding, more than 40 days. The proofs include the hadith establishing the 3-10 day range for hayd and the 40-day limit for nifas, plus the hadith from Aisha explicitly stating that istihadah blood is from a vein, not menstruation. This is crucial because mustahadah (the woman experiencing istihadah) is required to pray and fast, unlike a menstruating woman.

Key Terms
الاستحاضة (al-istihadah): Irregular bleeding that is not menstrual or postpartum, occurring outside the normal durations (less than 3 days or more than 10 days in hayd; more than 40 days in nifas).
المستحاضة (al-mustahadah): A woman experiencing istihadah.

Definition of Istihadah and Its Proofs
Defines istihadah with hadith evidence

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi definition of istihadah, identify its three constituent scenarios, and cite the hadith proofs that establish the boundaries of hayd and nifas.

Core Idea
Istihadah is any bleeding outside Hanafi limits: 10 days in hayd, >40 days in nifas.

This lesson defines istihadah (non-menstrual bleeding) and provides the hadith evidence that distinguishes it from hayd and nifas. Understanding these boundaries is crucial for a woman's worship obligations – a mustahadah must perform wudu for each prayer, unlike a menstruating woman. We will examine four key narrations that the Hanafi school uses to set the minimum and maximum durations.

Guided Path
1
State the definition of istihadah
Read the opening sentence and the Urdu explanation. Istihadah is defined as blood that is less than three days or more than ten days in hayd, or more than forty days in nifas.
2
Identify the three scenarios
There are three cases that constitute istihadah: (1) bleeding less than 3 days in hayd, (2) bleeding more than 10 days in hayd, (3) bleeding more than 40 days in nifas.
Also note that the minimum for hayd is 3 days and maximum is 10 days, while nifas maximum is 40 days.
3
Examine the hadith proofs
The commentator cites four hadith. The first and second set the 10-day maximum and 3-day minimum for hayd. The third sets the 40-day limit for nifas. The fourth indicates that istihadah blood is from a vein, not menstruation, and that a mustahadah must perform wudu for each prayer.
These hadith are the primary textual evidence (dalil naqli) for the definition.
4
Understand the qiyas (analogy) for the minimum
The second hadith states the minimum is three days, so by analogy (qiyas), what is less than three days is not hayd – it is istihadah. This shows the use of logical deduction alongside direct texts.
This analogy is a form of qiyas jaliy (clear analogy).
5
Note the practical implications
A woman in istihadah is not considered menstruating. She does not stop praying or fasting; she performs ghusl once (at the end of hayd) and then performs wudu for each prayer if bleeding continues. This is derived from the hadith of Fatimah bint Abi Hubaysh.
This is the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence) of the definition.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۲۴۷) والاستحاضة دم نقص عن ثلاثة ايام او زاد على عشرة في الحيض وعلى اربعين في النفاس . تشریح : یہ استحاضہ کی تعریف ہے کہ [1] حیض میں تین دن سے کم خون آئے ،[۲] یا دس دن سے زیادہ خون آئے ۔ [۳] یا نفاس میں چالیس دن سے زیادہ خون آئے تو وہ سب استحاضہ ہیں۔ وجه : (1) عن ابی امامة الباهلي قال قال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم : فاذا رأت الدم فوق عشرة ايام فهى مستحاضة (دار قطنی، نمبر ۸۳۴ ) ( ۲ ) عن واثلة بن الاسقع قال قال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم : اقـل الحيض ثلاثة ايام و اكثره عشرة ايام (دار قطنی ، کتاب الحیض ، ج اول ص ۲۲۵ نمبر ۸۳۶) اسی پر قیاس کیا جائے گا کہ تین دن سے کم ہو تو وہ بھی استحاضہ ہوگا۔ (۳) عن عبد الله بن عمرو قال : قال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم : تنتظر النفساء أربعين ليلة ، فان رأت الطهر قبل ذالك فهى طاهر ، و ان جاوزت الاربعين فهى بمنزلة المستحاضة ، تغتسل و تصلى ، فان غلبها الدم توضأت لكل صلوة (دار قطنی ، باب الحیض ، ج اول ص ۲۲۸، نمبر ۸۴۷) (۴) عن عائشة انها قالت قالت فاطمة بنت ابي حبيش لرسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم : يا رسول الله ! انى لا اطهر افأدع الصلاة ؟ فقال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم : انـمـا ذالک عرق و ليس بالحيضة ، فاذا اقبلت الحيضة فاتركى الصلاة فاذا ذهب قدرها فاغسلی عنک الدم و صلی ۔ ( بخاری شریف، باب الاستحاضہ ، ص ۵۳ ، نمبر ۳۰۶)
(247) And istihadah is blood that is less than three days or exceeds ten in hayd and forty in nifas. Explanation: This is the definition of istihadah: (1) In hayd, if blood comes for less than three days, (2) or if blood comes for more than ten days, (3) or in nifas, if blood comes for more than forty days, then all of that is istihadah. Proof: (1) From Abu Umamah al-Bahili that the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: 'When she sees blood beyond ten days, she is a mustahadah.' (2) From Wathilah ibn al-Asqa' that the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: 'The minimum of hayd is three days and its maximum is ten days.' By analogy, what is less than three days is also istihadah. (3) From Abdullah ibn Amr that the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: 'The woman in nifas waits forty nights. If she becomes pure before that, she is pure. If she exceeds forty, she is like a mustahadah; she performs ghusl and prays. If blood overcomes her, she performs wudu for each prayer.' (4) From Aishah that Fatimah bint Abi Hubaysh said to the Messenger of Allah: 'O Messenger of Allah, I do not become pure. Should I abandon prayer?' He said: 'That is only a vein, not menstruation. When menstruation comes, leave prayer. When it goes, wash the blood from yourself and pray.'
Source pages p. 179

Commentary
This passage defines istihadah (non-menstrual bleeding) by setting the limits for hayd (3-10 days) and nifas (up to 40 days). Any bleeding that falls outside these ranges is considered istihadah, which does not prevent worship. The commentator provides four hadith proofs: (1) establishes the 10-day maximum for hayd, (2) establishes the 3-day minimum and 10-day maximum for hayd, leading to the analogy that less than 3 days is istihadah, (3) sets the 40-day limit for nifas, and (4) indicates that istihadah blood is from a vein, not menstruation, so it does not invalidate prayer. This is a foundational ruling in Hanafi fiqh for distinguishing menstrual from non-menstrual bleeding.

Key Terms
الاستحاضة (al-istihāḍah): Bleeding that is less than three days or more than ten days in hayd, or more than forty days in nifas; it is not menstrual blood but from a vein.
الحيض (al-ḥayḍ): Menstrual blood that lasts between three and ten days.
النفاس (al-nifās): Postpartum bleeding that lasts up to forty days.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi definition of istihadah is based on clear hadith bounds: hayd min 3, max 10 days; nifas max 40 days; anything outside is istihadah.

The Minimum Tuhr: Fifteen Days of Purity Between Menstruations
States the minimum interval of purity between two menstrual periods

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the minimum period of purity between two menstruations according to the Hanafi school and explain the textual evidence used to derive this ruling.

Core Idea
The minimum purity between two menstruations is fixed at fifteen days — a ruling derived from the interaction of maximum hayd and tuhr periods.

This lesson addresses a critical question in Hanafi fiqh of taharah: how long must a woman remain in a state of purity between two menstrual cycles? The passage establishes a minimum of fifteen days, no less, and leaves the maximum unlimited. Understanding this ruling is essential for determining the beginning of a new menstrual period, which in turn affects salah, fasting, and 'iddah calculations.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
What is the minimum duration of tuhr between two hayd periods? The text explicitly states fifteen days.
2
Understand the underlying principle
Why fifteen days? The maximum hayd is ten days in the Hanafi school, but the text uses an indication (isharat al-nass) from the narration that hayd can be up to fifteen days, implying that the month is divided into two halves of fifteen days each.
This combines the maximum hayd of ten days with the general indication to set the minimum tuhr.
3
Examine the proof
The narration from Ata' (maximum hayd fifteen days) is cited. Although the Hanafi school takes maximum hayd as ten days, this narration is used as an indirect evidence (isharat al-nass) to support the fifteen-day minimum tuhr.
The proof is of the dalil naqli type (narration).
4
Consider the implications
The maximum tuhr is unlimited; a woman may have years of purity. This affects rulings on 'iddah and when the next hayd begins.
5
Distinguish from other schools
The Shafi'i school also holds the minimum tuhr to be fifteen days, but their evidence is more direct: they take the narration that maximum hayd is fifteen days as literal.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۲۴۸) واقل الطهر الفاصل بين الحيضتين خمسة عشر يوما ولا حد لاكثره . ترجمه : دو حیض کے درمیان طہر کی اقل مدت پندرہ روز ہے، اور اکثر کی کوئی حد نہیں۔ تشریح : دو حیضوں کے درمیان کم سے کم پندرہ دن تک طہر رہ سکتا ہے اس سے کم نہیں ، اور زیادہ سے زیادہ طہر کی کوئی حد متعین نہیں ہے، کسی کو تین سال اور چار سال تک حیض نہیں آتا ہے، پھر آ جاتا ہے۔ وجه : اس قول کے اشارۃ النص سے استدلال کیا جا سکتا ہے کہ اس میں مہینے میں پندرہ دن تک حیض ہے تو باقی پندرہ دن طہر کا شمار کیا جا سکتا ہے۔ عن عطاء قال اكثر الحيض خمسة عشرة وقال ادنى الحيض يوم - (دار قطنی ، کتاب الحیض میں ۲۱۶ نمبر ۷۹۰٫۷۸۹ رسنن ابیھقی ، باب اقل الحیض ، ج اول ص ۲۷۶، نمبر ۱۵۳۲)
(248) And the minimum period of purity between two menstruations is fifteen days, and there is no limit for its maximum. Translation: The minimum duration of purity between two menstruations is fifteen days, and there is no fixed maximum. Explanation: The minimum purity between two menstruations can be fifteen days, no less, and there is no set maximum for purity; some women may not menstruate for three or four years, then it comes. Proof: This can be inferred from the indication of the text, that in a month there can be up to fifteen days of menstruation, so the remaining fifteen days can be counted as purity. From Ata' he said: 'The maximum of menstruation is fifteen days, and the minimum is one day.' (Dar Qutni, book of hayd, no. 790, 789; Sunan al-Bayhaqi, chapter on minimum hayd, vol. 1, p. 276, no. 1532)
Source pages p. 179

Commentary
This ruling establishes the minimum period of purity (tuhr) between two menstrual periods as fifteen days. It is based on the principle that a menstrual period cannot exceed ten days in the Hanafi school, so if a woman menstruates for the maximum of ten days, she must have at least fifteen days of purity before the next menstruation. The maximum purity is unlimited, as some women may go months or years without menstruating. The proof is a narration from Ata' that the maximum hayd is fifteen days and the minimum is one day, though the Hanafi school sets the minimum for hayd at three days and maximum at ten. This ruling is essential for determining the start of a new menstrual cycle and for calculations related to 'iddah and worship.

Key Terms
الطهر (al-ṭuhr): The period of purity between two menstrual bleedings, which must be at least fifteen days.
اقل الطهر (aqall al-ṭuhr): The minimum duration of purity between two hayd periods, fixed at fifteen days in the Hanafi school.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway

Ruling for a Mustahadah at Puberty
Specifies hayd and tuhr durations for a mustahadah at puberty

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the default hayd and tuhr durations for a girl who becomes mustahadah at puberty and explain why habit is not used.

Core Idea
For a mustahadah without prior habit, hayd is set at 10 days (maximum) and tuhr at 15 days (minimum).

This lesson covers the Hanafi ruling for a girl who experiences prolonged bleeding from her very first menstruation. Since she has no established habit, the school fixes her menstruation period at ten days and her purity period at fifteen days. Understanding this default is essential for her to fulfill her acts of worship correctly.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
Recognize that the passage applies to a girl who bleeds for the first time and the bleeding exceeds 10 consecutive days.
2
Distinguish the two cases
Note the difference between a girl with a prior habit (whose habit is used) and one without (first bleeding).
3
Apply the defaults
State the default durations: hayd = 10 days, tuhr = 15 days.
4
Understand the legal consequence
Recognize that these defaults govern her worship until she establishes a regular habit.

Source pages p. 179

Commentary
This passage provides the ruling for a woman who experiences istihadah from the onset of puberty (i.e., her first bleeding exceeds ten days). Since she has no prior menstrual habit, the Hanafi school fixes her hayd at ten days (the maximum) and her tuhr at fifteen days (the minimum). This serves as a default until she establishes a regular habit. The ruling distinguishes between a woman with a known habit (whose habit is used) and a woman without any prior history (whose hayd is set at ten days). This is crucial for determining when she must pray, fast, and observe other acts of worship.

Key Terms
مستحاضة (mustaḥāḍah): A woman who experiences irregular bleeding outside the normal limits of hayd and nifas.
عادت ('ādat): A woman's established menstrual habit, used to determine hayd in case of irregularity.

The Eight Prohibitions During Hayd and Nifas
Lists eight prohibitions and provides hadith proof

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the eight acts prohibited during hayd and nifas, explain the Hanafi position, and identify the hadith proof.

Core Idea
Eight acts are haram during hayd and nifas—prayer, fasting, Quran recitation, touching the mushaf, entering the mosque, tawaf, intercourse, and direct contact.

This lesson lists the eight prohibitions that apply to a woman during menstruation (hayd) and postpartum bleeding (nifas) according to the Hanafi school. Understanding these prohibitions is essential for maintaining ritual purity and avoiding sin. The source also provides a hadith proof for the prohibition of prayer and fasting.

Guided Path
1
Memorize the list
Recite the eight prohibitions in order from the text: prayer, fasting, Quran recitation, touching the mushaf, entering the mosque, tawaf, intercourse, and direct contact between navel and knee.
Repetition helps embedding.
2
Understand the rationale
Each prohibition relates to the state of ritual impurity (hadath akbar). Acts requiring wudu or ghusl are invalid without purity.
Prayer and tawaf require purity; fasting is prohibited because it is not valid during impurity until ghusl.
3
Examine the proof
The hadith from Abu Sa'id al-Khudri narrates the Prophet (peace be upon him) stating that a menstruating woman does not pray or fast, indicating these are prohibited.
The hadith is ahad (single narration) but accepted by the majority.
4
Note the exceptions
Some prohibitions have degrees: reciting Quran even one verse is prohibited, but certain acts like dhikr or dua are allowed.
Touching the mushaf without a barrier is prohibited, but with a barrier it may be allowed.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

(250) And eight things are prohibited during hayd and nifas. Explanation: During hayd and nifas, eight things are forbidden: (1) Prayer, (2) Fasting, (3) Reciting even one verse of the Quran, (4) Touching the Quran without a cover, (5) Entering the mosque, (6) Tawaf, (7) Sexual intercourse, (8) Direct contact between the navel and the knee. Proof: (1) From Abu Sa'id al-Khudri: 'The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) went out on the day of Eid... He said: Is it not that the testimony of a woman is half that of a man? They said: Yes. He said: That is from the deficiency of her intellect. Is it not that when she menstruates, she does not pray or fast? They said: Yes. He said: That is from the deficiency of her religion.' (Bukhari, chapter on the fasting woman leaving fast, p. 53, no. 304) In this hadith...
Source pages p. 180

Commentary
This passage enumerates the eight acts prohibited for a woman during hayd (menstruation) and nifas (postpartum bleeding). The first two (prayer and fasting) are major acts of worship that require ritual purity. The next two (Quran recitation and touching the mushaf) are prohibited because of the impurity state. Entering the mosque is prohibited to maintain its sanctity. Tawaf requires purification. The last two (intercourse and direct contact) are prohibited to avoid intimacy during impurity. The hadith from Abu Sa'id al-Khudri is used as proof for the prohibition of prayer and fasting, as the Prophet explicitly linked the leaving of prayer and fasting by a menstruating woman to a deficiency in religion (not a moral deficiency, but a legal one).

Key Terms
الحيض (al-ḥayḍ): Menstrual bleeding within the limits of 3 to 10 days.
النفاس (al-nifās): Postpartum bleeding up to 40 days.
مباشرة (mubāsharah): Direct skin-to-skin contact between the navel and the knee, including the genitals.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is NOT among the eight prohibited acts during hayd and nifas?
A) Reciting Quran
B) Looking at the Kaaba
C) Entering the mosque
D) Tawaf

Key Takeaway
A menstruating or postpartum woman must avoid eight specific acts to maintain the sanctity of worship and avoid sin.

Taharah — Purification
beginner
6 min
Eight Prohibitions During Menstruation and Postpartum Bleeding
Listing eight prohibitions and proving first two

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the eight prohibitions during menstruation and postpartum bleeding, and explain the Hanafi ruling on make-up of missed prayers and fasts with its evidence.

Core Idea
Prayer and fasting are forbidden during menstruation; fasts must be made up, prayers are not.

This passage introduces eight acts that become prohibited during menstruation (hayd) and postpartum bleeding (nifas). The first two—prayer and fasting—are discussed in detail with proof from the Sunnah. A critical distinction is made: while both are forbidden at that time, only missed fasts require make-up, not prayers. Understanding this ruling is essential for a woman to correctly fulfill her religious duties.

Guided Path
1
Identify the eight prohibitions
List the eight acts that become haram during hayd and nifas as stated in the text.
The first two are prayer and fasting; others include reciting Quran, touching the Quran, entering the mosque, tawaf, sexual intercourse, and intimacy between navel and knee.
2
Understand the ruling for prayer and fasting
Note that both are forbidden. The woman must not perform them during the state. However, she must make up missed fasts but not missed prayers.
This is a distinguishing feature of the Hanafi school based on hadith and consensus.
3
Locate the dalil (evidence)
Identify the two hadith cited: one from Abu Sa'id al-Khudri and one from Aisha (may Allah be pleased with them).
Both are from Sahih al-Bukhari.
4
Analyze the wajh al-dalalah
See how the hadith explicitly state that a menstruating woman does not pray or fast, establishing the prohibition.
The wording 'فاذا اقبلت الحيضة فاتركى الصلاة' directly commands leaving prayer.
5
Note the practical consequence
The woman will make up fasts later, but not prayers. This is the mufta bihi position.
This ruling is applied by all Hanafi muftis.

What is prohibited due to menstruation and postpartum bleeding. (250) Prayer. And eight things are prohibited due to menstruation and postpartum bleeding. ... Translation: (250) Eight actions are prohibited during menstruation and postpartum bleeding: [1] prayer [2] fasting. Explanation: The menstruating and postpartum woman are impure, so she will not pray nor fast. However, she will later make up the fasts and will not make up the prayers. Evidence: (1) From Abu Sa'id al-Khudri ... (Bukhari) (2) From Aisha ... (Bukhari).
Source pages p. 180

Commentary
This is a ruling with proof section. The author begins by listing eight prohibitions during menstruation (hayd) and postpartum bleeding (nifas). The first two are prayer and fasting. The author then explains that the woman is impure and thus cannot perform these acts. However, she must make up missed fasts but not prayers. This is based on hadith from Abu Sa'id al-Khudri and Aisha (may Allah be pleased with them). The prohibition is established and the wisdom is mentioned: deficiency in religion due to leaving these acts during menses.

Key Terms
حيض (hayd): Menstrual blood that flows regularly from the womb, lasting a minimum of 3 days and maximum of 10 days in the Hanafi school.
نفاس (nifas): Postpartum bleeding that follows childbirth, with no minimum limit and a maximum of 40 days in the Hanafi school.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what must a woman do for missed prayers due to menstruation?
A) She must make up all missed prayers.
B) She must not make up missed prayers.
C) She must make up prayers but not fasts.
D) She must make up both prayers and fasts.

Key Takeaway
Prayer and fasting are forbidden during menstruation and postpartum bleeding; only fasts are made up, not prayers.
